# Audit 07 вҖ” Full Codebase Review

**Performed:** 2026-06-16 В· **Branch:** `staging` В· **Baseline:** audits/01вҖ“06 (2026-04-28)

## Method

A 16-agent fan-out review followed by per-finding adversarial verification, run as a single orchestrated workflow:

- **16 reviewers** вҖ” 7 main-process areas (sync use-cases, download use-cases, edit/collections/tags use-cases, repositories, media drivers, platform drivers, IPC layer), 4 renderer areas (player+editor, hooks+lib, feature components, routes+i18n), and 5 cross-cutting sweeps (security, dead-code, spec-violations, documented-vs-implemented, performance). Each reviewer read the real source, quoted evidence, and rated severity + confidence.
- **1 adversarial verifier per finding** вҖ” re-read the cited code and surrounding context, defaulted to skepticism, and returned `confirmed` / `refuted` / `uncertain` plus a corrected severity. This is what keeps the signal high: 8 plausible-but-wrong findings were caught and refuted, and one finding was downgraded criticalвҶ’high.

**Totals:** 105 raised вҶ’ **95 confirmed, 8 refuted, 2 uncertain.** 121 agents, ~4.8M tokens.

### Confidence & severity

- `confidence` (0вҖ“1) is the reviewer's pre-verification certainty; the **verdict** (and its `notes`) is the post-verification truth. Trust the verdict over the confidence.
- Severities shown are the **effective** severity (verifier's correction applied where it overrode the reviewer). No confirmed criticals survived review.

### Confirmed counts

| Severity | Count |
| --- | --- |
| рҹ”ҙ High | 6 (5 distinct вҖ” yt-dlp injection was raised twice) |
| рҹҹ  Medium | 13 |
| рҹҹЎ Low | 57 |
| в„№пёҸ Info | 19 |
| **Total confirmed** | **95** |

By category (all 105 raised): bug 30 В· weird-logic 19 В· spec-violation 16 В· dead-code 13 В· security 11 В· performance 11 В· other 5.

---

## Headline

The codebase is genuinely solid вҖ” the Clean Architecture layering holds, the security posture is real (the `klip-media://` handler, `argv-builder`, and `security-hardening` were personally read and are sound), and **no documented-as-shipped feature is actually missing** (auto-update is now fully wired via `ElectronAutoUpdater` + `UpdaterController` + composition-root, resolving the old baseline gap). The findings cluster around **two root-cause families** plus the **post-baseline features** (in-app editor, comments, transcripts, downloads UI) that haven't yet caught up to the rigor of the older code.

### Root-cause family A вҖ” the `Creator.id` identity split

Memory/spec says *"Creator.id is a UUID, separate from Creator.folderName; use findByFolderName for disk-keyed lookups."* `RegisterCreator` honors that (`id = idGenerator.generate()`), but **`DownloadVideo.ensureCreator` sets `id = folderName`** (the slug) for auto-created creators. Two id conventions now coexist, and this single inconsistency produces:

- **F-H1 (FK crash + orphaned file)** вҖ” downloading a video for a *previously registered* creator writes `video.creatorId = <slug>`, which doesn't match the creator's UUID `id` вҶ’ `SQLITE_CONSTRAINT_FOREIGNKEY` after the file is already on disk вҶ’ phantom "download failed" + orphaned media.
- **F-H3 (file mis-linkage)** вҖ” `MoveVideosToCreator` builds on-disk paths from `creator.id` instead of `folderName`; for any registered creator the move silently doesn't happen but the DB `creatorId` flips вҶ’ video catalogued under the wrong creator.
- **F-M? (root cause)** вҖ” `DownloadVideo.ensureCreator` should mint a UUID for auto-created creators too. Fixing this dissolves the other two.

**Fix the root cause once:** auto-created creators get a UUID `id` (inject `IIdGenerator`); `folderName` stays the disk key; all disk-path construction uses `folderName`; all FK writes use `creator.id`.

### Root-cause family B вҖ” crash-recovery atomicity on multi-step FS sagas

`MigrateRootFolder` commits the path-rewrite + `rootPath` setting in a transaction but marks the operation `'completed'` *after* the transaction (several awaited steps later). A hard kill in that window makes `RecoverOperations` **reverse a successful migration** (moves every folder back while the DB points at the new root) вҶ’ mass "missing" library. The DB-failure branch has the mirror problem: it marks the op terminally `'failed'` (which recovery never revisits) while leaving files at the new root. The fix is to make the operation's terminal status atomic with the DB commit, or to make recovery idempotent against `settingsRepo.rootPath`.

---

## Prioritized fix order

1. **F-H4 вҖ” yt-dlp `--` terminator + URL scheme validation.** One literal `'--'` per args array + a zod `.url()`/http(s) check. Closes an **RCE** (`--exec`) reachable from a compromised renderer per your own threat model. The 2026-04-28 audit marked this "clean" because it checked *shell* injection and missed *option* injection. Highest urgency, lowest effort.
2. **F-H1 / F-H3 вҖ” creator-id unification** (root-cause family A). Fixes three bugs at once.
3. **F-H2 вҖ” migrate-recovery atomicity** (root-cause family B). Data-loss.
4. **F-M1 (ffprobe `--` + containment), F-M4/F-M5 (`pushSchema` + migration test).** Small; M4/M5 also unblock testing the download-history feature.
5. **F-H5 / F-M7 вҖ” virtualize CommentsTab + TranscriptTab.** Then **F-M6 (reconcile invalidation)**, then the LOW tail.

> Commit each fix as its own atomic commit (per project convention). Suggested branch start: the H4 injection fix, then the creator-id family.

---

## Already resolved / verified clean (do not re-chase)

- **Auto-update** is fully wired (old baseline "electron-updater never wired" gap is closed).
- **`klip-media://` protocol** вҖ” entity-keyed parse вҶ’ resolve вҶ’ realpath containment вҶ’ stat вҶ’ `net.fetch`; no traversal escape found.
- **`ffmpeg argv-builder`** вҖ” paths passed as separate argv elements, no shell. (The injectable sinks are *yt-dlp* and *ffprobe*, not ffmpeg, because ffmpeg's paths are server-derived.)
- **`security-hardening`** вҖ” denies all cross-origin navigation, `window.open`, and permission requests; tight YouTube-only external allowlist.
- **`/`-while-typing palette hijack** вҖ” correctly guarded via `isTextInputActive()`.
- **XSS surface** вҖ” all YouTube-origin text (comments, titles, descriptions, transcripts, snippets) is rendered as React children / text props, never `dangerouslySetInnerHTML`. `img-src` allow-list intact.
- **`smart` collections** (`kind='smart'`) are correctly **reserved for future** вҖ” inventory, not a gap.

## knip false-positives filtered out (so they aren't re-investigated)

knip flags many things that are **not** dead and were excluded after verification:

- Runtime entry points dynamically loaded by electron-vite: `src/main/index.ts`, `src/preload/index.ts` + `index.d.ts`, `routes/main.tsx`, `EditorApp.tsx`, all route files, `*.d.ts`, `*.config.ts`, `scripts/*`.
- `src/renderer/components/ui/**` unused named exports вҖ” shelved shadcn primitives, intentional.
- Build/CSS-time deps reported as "unused": `tailwindcss`, `@tailwindcss/vite`, `tw-animate-css`, `shadcn` (CLI).
- `EditorController`, `DownloadHistoryController`, the renderer `editor/*` files, `use-render-progress.ts`, `logger.ts` вҖ” all **ARE** wired (verified in `index.ts` / `composition-root.ts`). knip can't see the dynamic wiring.

The deps that ARE genuinely unused (verified by grep): `react-router`, `@tanstack/react-table`, `react-hotkeys-hook`, `@dnd-kit/react`, `@marshallofsound/ipc` вҖ” see F-dead-code section.

## How to read the appendix

Every confirmed finding below has a stable ID (`F01`вҖҰ), grouped by effective severity then category. Each carries: location, category, confidence, whether it was already in the 2026-04-28 baseline (`known`), the impact, the exact evidence, the fix, and the **verifier's** independent reasoning + notes (sharper repro for confirmed, or where-it's-handled for nuance). Refuted and uncertain findings are listed at the end.

> **Note on near-duplicates:** a few issues were independently surfaced by more than one reviewer (e.g. the two yt-dlp injection findings, two `pushSchema` `download_history` findings, the `MigrateRootFolder` pair, multiple `PersistentPlayer` rAF entries). All are preserved below вҖ” duplicates often carry complementary detail or a different repro вҖ” but they describe the same underlying defect.

# Confirmed findings (95)


## рҹ”ҙ HIGH

### F01 вҖ” Download for a pre-registered creator violates videos.creator_id FK and orphans the file

- **Severity:** рҹ”ҙ HIGH
- **Category:** bug
- **Location:** `src/main/use-cases/DownloadVideo.ts:210-256, 356-449`
- **Confidence:** 0.82 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

videos.creator_id is a FK to creators.id (schema.ts:55-57) and `foreign_keys = ON` (database.ts:28). For creators auto-created by ensureCreator, id === folderName so the FK holds. But RegisterCreator assigns id = idGenerator.generate() (a UUID) with a separate folderName. When a user registers a channel, then downloads a video for it using the same display name, ensureCreator's findByFolderName finds the existing UUID-keyed creator and takes the else branch (no insert) вҖ” but the Video is still written with creatorId: folderName (the slug), which does NOT equal the creator's UUID id. The videos INSERT then fails with SQLITE_CONSTRAINT_FOREIGNKEY, performDownload's catch classifies it as terminal, emits a spurious 'error' event and an error history row вҖ” while the media file already sits on disk with no DB row. Net effect: a perfectly valid download of a registered creator's video appears to fail and leaves an orphaned file. The in-code comment at lines 363-377 acknowledges only the youtube_channel_id UNIQUE edge for a differing display name; it misses that even the matched-folderName happy path writes the wrong creatorId.

**Evidence**

~~~text
const folderName = slugify(creatorName) ... await this.ensureCreator(folderName, ...) ... const video: Video = { id: videoId, creatorId: folderName, ... }; this.videoRepo.upsert(video).  ensureCreator does `const existing = this.creatorRepo.findByFolderName(folderName)` and returns void вҖ” it never threads the resolved creator id back to the caller.
~~~

**Fix**

Have ensureCreator return the resolved Creator (or its id), and write video.creatorId = resolvedCreator.id instead of the raw folderName slug. The output directory can still use folderName for disk layout, but the DB FK must reference the creator's actual id.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I verified every cited fact against the real code:

1. schema.ts:55-57 вҖ” videos.creatorId is text('creator_id').notNull().references(() => creators.id, { onDelete: 'cascade' }). It is a genuine FK to creators.id.
2. database.ts:28 вҖ” raw.pragma('foreign_keys = ON') is executed unconditionally on every DB open, so the FK is enforced at runtime.
3. RegisterCreator.ts:66-68 вҖ” a registered creator gets id = idGenerator.generate() (UUID) with a SEPARATE folderName field (the validated slug). So for registered creators, id !== folderName.
4. DownloadVideo.ts:211-214 вҖ” folderName = slugify(creatorName); ensureCreator(folderName, ...) returns void (signature line 356 returns Promise<void>); it never threads the resolved creator id back.
5. ensureCreator (lines 378, 421-446) вҖ” looks up via findByFolderName(folderName). When the creator already exists (registered case), it takes the else branch and does NOT insert; touched = existing, but the resolved id is discarded.
6. DownloadVideo.ts:254-256 + 283 вҖ” the Video is built with creatorId: folderName (the slug) and passed to videoRepo.upsert(video).
7. SqliteVideoRepository.ts:189-194 вҖ” upsert performs a real .insert(videos).values({ creatorId: video.creatorId, ... }). better-sqlite3 throws SQLITE_CONSTRAINT_FOREIGNKEY synchronously when creator_id (slug) does not match any creators.id (UUID).
8. The download completes (downloader.download resolves at lines 247-250, result.filePath on disk) BEFORE the upsert. The throw is caught at line 301; classifyDownloadError (download-error.ts) has no pattern matching a FK message, so it returns 'terminal' -> emits a status:'error' progress event (retriable:false) and a non-retryable error history row.

Net effect exactly as claimed: a valid download for a previously-registered creator (whose folderName equals slugify(creatorName), the normal case when the UI sends the display name) fails at the DB write, surfaces a spurious error to the user, and leaves the media file orphaned on disk with no DB row. No mitigation exists in any code path вҖ” the else branch never reinserts the creator and the video always references the slug, not the UUID. The in-code comment at lines 362-377 explicitly acknowledges the related findByFolderName-miss case but, as the reviewer notes, misses that even the matched-folderName happy path writes the wrong creatorId.

**Verifier notes**

Sharper repro: (1) Register a channel "Foo Bar" via RegisterCreator -> creators row with id=<uuid>, folder_name='foo-bar'. (2) Start a download passing creatorName 'Foo Bar'. ensureCreator computes folderName='foo-bar', findByFolderName hits the existing UUID-keyed row, takes else branch (no insert). (3) yt-dlp finishes, file written to <root>/foo-bar/downloads/<videoId>/. (4) videoRepo.upsert({ creatorId:'foo-bar', ... }) throws SQLITE_CONSTRAINT_FOREIGNKEY because 'foo-bar' is not a creators.id. (5) catch -> terminal error event + error history row; file orphaned.

Fix as suggested: change ensureCreator to return the resolved Creator (it already computes `touched` in every branch вҖ” return touched), and set video.creatorId = resolvedCreator.id. Keep folderName only for the on-disk output path (pathResolver.join at line 217). Note the duplicate-check pre-flight at line 202 also writes existing.creatorId into creatorFolderName for history, which is fine, but confirms creatorId in the videos table is already a UUID for any video that survived a prior insert вҖ” so reading it back as a folder name elsewhere (history creatorFolderName) is a separate latent inconsistency worth a glance, though out of scope for this finding.

Auto-created (non-registered) creators are unaffected because ensureCreator's !existing branch sets id=folderName (line 396), so the FK coincidentally holds there вҖ” which is why fresh-install testing would not surface this.

---

### F02 вҖ” MigrateRootFolder marks op 'completed' outside the DB transaction вҖ” crash there makes RecoverOperations move every folder back while the DB points at the new root (mass media loss)

- **Severity:** рҹ”ҙ HIGH _(verifier corrected from critical)_
- **Category:** bug
- **Location:** `src/main/use-cases/MigrateRootFolder.ts:174-203`
- **Confidence:** 0.82 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

The folders have already been physically moved to newRoot and the transaction has committed the path rewrite + rootPath setting. But the operation row is still status='in_progress' until updateStatus('completed') runs several awaited steps later (watcher restart, resume, reconcile). If the process crashes/quits in that window, RecoverOperations.recoverMigrateRootOp (RecoverOperations.ts:191-203) unconditionally replays the moves in reverse вҖ” moveDirectory(newRoot/folder -> oldRoot/folder) for every folder вҖ” because it only checks whether the source exists at newRoot, never whether the DB already committed. Outcome: every creator folder is moved back to the old root while the DB (rootPath + all video/cut filePaths) points at the new root. The entire library reads as missing on disk; recovery has actively un-done a successful migration.

**Evidence**

~~~text
this.transaction.run(() => {
  this.videoRepo.updateFilePathPrefix(oldRootPath, newRootPath)
  this.cutRepo.updateFilePathPrefix(oldRootPath, newRootPath)
  this.settingsRepo.set('rootPath', newRootPath)
})
this.rootPathRef.value = newRootPath
...
// в”Җв”Җ Complete в”Җв”Җ
this.operationRepo.updateStatus(operationId, 'completed')
await this.fileWatcher.restart(newRootPath)
await this.processNotifications.resume()
~~~

**Fix**

Make the operation terminal atomically with the DB commit: move operationRepo.updateStatus(operationId,'completed') INSIDE the same transaction.run that rewrites the paths and sets rootPath, or persist a 'db-committed' flag into the payload before leaving the transaction and have recoverMigrateRootOp short-circuit to markCompleted (not roll back) when that flag is set / when settingsRepo.rootPath already equals payload.newRoot.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I read both cited files in full. The atomicity flaw is real. MigrateRootFolder.execute commits the path rewrite + rootPath=newRoot inside transaction.run() (lines 174-178, SqliteTransactionScope wraps better-sqlite3 transaction() synchronously), sets rootPathRef (line 180), but leaves the operation row status='in_progress' until updateStatus(operationId,'completed') at line 198. The operation-status write is NOT part of the transaction, so the DB commit and the terminal-status write are non-atomic.

RecoverOperations.recoverMigrateRootOp (lines 164-231) is replayed for any 'in_progress'/'pending' migrate_root row at startup. For a v2 payload where every folder has status='moved', it unconditionally moves each folder back newRootвҶ’oldRoot (line 202) as long as the source still exists at newRoot (line 196). I confirmed via grep that RecoverOperations never references settingsRepo/rootPath and has no ISettingsRepository in its constructor вҖ” there is NO check of committed DB state. So a crash after the transaction commits but before updateStatus('completed') yields: files moved back to oldRoot by recovery, while the DB (rootPath + all video/cut filePaths) points at newRoot. The whole library reads as missing and recovery has actively un-done a successful migration. The suggested fix (move updateStatus inside the transaction, or have recovery short-circuit when settingsRepo.rootPath === payload.newRoot) is correct.

One factual correction to the finding's framing: the title claims the crash window includes 'several awaited steps later (watcher restart, resume, reconcile)'. That is wrong вҖ” those awaits (lines 201-202, 211) run AFTER updateStatus('completed') at line 198. The actual vulnerable window is the purely synchronous gap between transaction.run() returning (line 178) and updateStatus('completed') (line 198): lines 179-197 contain no await. The catch block's awaits (187-188) only run on dbError, not on the success path. So triggering this requires a hard process kill (SIGKILL/power loss/segfault/OOM) inside a sub-millisecond synchronous window, not an ordinary async-yield crash or a graceful app quit.

**Verifier notes**

Bug and catastrophic outcome are genuine; severity lowered from critical to high because the trigger window is much narrower than the title implies вҖ” it is the synchronous gap between the transaction commit (line 178) and updateStatus('completed') (line 198), reachable only by a hard process kill in a sub-ms window (no await yields there, and a graceful quit fires after the sync block). The 'several awaited steps' in the title actually occur after the op is marked completed, so they are not part of the exposure. Sharper repro: (1) run a migration with вүҘ1 creator folder; (2) inject a process.kill/segfault between transaction.run() and operationRepo.updateStatus on the success path; (3) restart вҖ” RecoverOperations moves all folders back to oldRoot while settingsRepo.get('rootPath') still equals newRoot and all video/cut filePaths are rewritten to newRoot, so the library is unreadable. Best fix: put updateStatus(operationId,'completed') inside the same transaction.run, OR inject ISettingsRepository into RecoverOperations and short-circuit recoverMigrateRootOp to markCompleted when settingsRepo.get('rootPath') === payload.newRoot.

---

### F03 вҖ” MoveVideosToCreator builds on-disk paths from creator id instead of folderName вҖ” corrupts file linkage for any RegisterCreator'd creator (id is a UUID, folder is a slug)

- **Severity:** рҹ”ҙ HIGH
- **Category:** bug
- **Location:** `src/main/use-cases/MoveVideosToCreator.ts:35-79`
- **Confidence:** 0.85 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

video.creatorId and targetCreatorId are the creator ENTITY ids. For creators created via RegisterCreator, id is a generated UUID while the on-disk folder is creator.folderName (a slug) вҖ” confirmed by ReconcileDirectory which builds paths from creator.folderName (line 355) but stores video.creatorId = creator.id (line 395). MoveToCreatorDialog passes target = creator.id. So for a RegisterCreator'd creator both oldDir and newDir use the UUID, which does not exist on disk: directoryExists(oldDir) is false, moveDirectory is skipped, and rewritePath finds video.filePath does not startWith the UUID-based oldDir so it returns the path unchanged. Net effect: the DB row's creatorId flips to the target but the file is never moved and filePath still points into the source creator's folder вҖ” a permanent mis-linkage where the cataloged video lives under the wrong creator's directory. (It happens to work only when id == folderName, which is true for download-created creators.)

**Evidence**

~~~text
const oldDir = this.pathResolver.join(root, video.creatorId, 'downloads', videoId)
const newDir = this.pathResolver.join(root, targetCreatorId, 'downloads', videoId)
...
if (this.fsReader.directoryExists(oldDir)) { this.fsWriter.moveDirectory(oldDir, newDir) }
...
filePath: rewritePath(video.filePath, oldDir, newDir) ?? video.filePath,
~~~

**Fix**

Look up the source creator (via the video) and the target creator, and build both paths from folderName: oldDir = join(root, sourceCreator.folderName, 'downloads', videoId); newDir = join(root, target.folderName, 'downloads', videoId). This mirrors ReconcileDirectory and the documented 'use findByFolderName for disk-keyed lookups' rule.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I read MoveVideosToCreator.ts, RegisterCreator.ts, ReconcileDirectory.ts, DownloadVideo.ts, NodeIdGenerator.ts, and MoveToCreatorDialog.tsx, and every link in the reviewer's chain holds.

(1) Creator id is a UUID independent of the slug folderName: RegisterCreator.ts:67 sets id = idGenerator.generate(), and NodeIdGenerator returns randomUUID(). folderName is a separate field (RegisterCreator.ts:56-57, slug-validated).

(2) ReconcileDirectory builds disk paths from creator.folderName (line 355) but stores video.creatorId = creator.id (line 395). So a RegisterCreator'd creator's videos have creatorId = UUID while their files live under <root>/<folderName>/downloads/... (filePath set at line 401).

(3) MoveVideosToCreator.ts:54-55 builds oldDir/newDir from video.creatorId and targetCreatorId (the entity ids), not folderName. The target lookup at line 35 is findById вҖ” correct for resolving the entity, but the path construction ignores its folderName.

(4) MoveToCreatorDialog.tsx:88 passes value={creator.id}; line 52 sends it as targetCreatorId. So target is the UUID for RegisterCreator'd creators.

Resulting failure for a RegisterCreator'd source and/or target: oldDir = <root>/<UUID>/downloads/<videoId> does not exist on disk, so directoryExists(oldDir) is false and moveDirectory is skipped (line 64-66). rewritePath (line 95-100) checks video.filePath.startsWith(oldDir); filePath points into the folderName-based path, not the UUID path, so it returns unchanged. Then upsertWithPrevious (line 79) flips the DB creatorId to the target UUID while filePath still points under the source creator's folder вҖ” a permanent mis-linkage. The comment at lines 67-69 ("If the source dir is missing we still update the DB row... reconcile will mark missing") actively masks the bug: the dir is not missing, it just has a different name.

This is exactly the documented "Creator.id вү  Creator.folderName вҖ” use findByFolderName for disk-keyed lookups" rule, and DownloadVideo.ensureCreator (lines 362-378) carries an explicit comment about having previously committed the same class of bug (findById(folderName)). The bug is masked only for download-created creators, where DownloadVideo deliberately sets id = folderName (lines 256, 396), making id == folderName so the UUID-vs-slug divergence vanishes.

**Verifier notes**

Repro: register a creator via RegisterCreator (gets a UUID id, slug folderName), get a video catalogued under it via ReconcileDirectory (video.creatorId = UUID, filePath under <root>/<folderName>/downloads), then move it to another creator via the Move dialog. The file is never moved, filePath is left pointing into the original folder, and the DB creatorId flips to the target вҖ” silent permanent mis-linkage in both directions (source folderName!=id, or target folderName!=id). Suggested fix is correct: resolve sourceCreator = creatorRepo.findById(video.creatorId) and use sourceCreator.folderName / target.folderName for oldDir/newDir, mirroring ReconcileDirectory.ts:355. Note both creators are already loadable (target at line 35; source via video.creatorId) so the fix is cheap. Severity high is justified: data-shape corruption that npm run clean won't catch since it produces wrong-but-valid-looking rows, and it affects the fully-wired RegisterCreator path, not a hypothetical one.

---

### F04 вҖ” CommentsTab renders all comments unvirtualized; "Fetch all" (up to 50,000) freezes the UI

- **Severity:** рҹ”ҙ HIGH
- **Category:** performance
- **Location:** `src/renderer/components/features/videos/CommentsTab.tsx:361-368`
- **Confidence:** 0.82 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

filteredThreads is rendered in full with no windowing. handleFetchAll requests up to FETCH_ALL_MAX = 50,000 comments and the IPC schema (ipc-schemas.ts:122) allows it. Each top-level CommentRow is a heavy node (Avatar, Item, Badge, Collapsible, two i18n hooks, useState). A popular YouTube video easily has tens of thousands of comments; rendering 10k-50k of these components in one synchronous commit produces a multi-second main-thread freeze and a large memory footprint, and every keystroke in the username/text filter re-renders the survivors. User-visible: the user clicks "Fetch all" on a big video and the renderer locks up. The feature post-dates the 2026-04-28 baseline (comments filtering is new).

**Evidence**

~~~text
<ScrollArea className="h-150 rounded border">
  <div className="divide-y">
    {filteredThreads.map((thread) => (
      <CommentRow key={thread.top.id} thread={thread} dateLocale={dateLocale} />
    ))}
  </div>
</ScrollArea>
// FETCH_ALL_MAX = 50_000 (line 97), wired to the IPC cap z.int().min(1).max(50_000)
~~~

**Fix**

Virtualize the thread list (the codebase already uses @tanstack/react-virtual in VirtualAuditList) вҖ” render only visible CommentRows. As a cheaper interim guard, also cap the *rendered* count (e.g. show first N with a "show more" pager) independent of how many were fetched.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I read CommentsTab.tsx in full. Lines 361-368 render `filteredThreads.map(...)` inside a plain ScrollArea with no windowing вҖ” every thread mounts a full CommentRow node (Avatar, Item/ItemMedia/ItemContent, conditional Badge, two useTranslation hooks at lines 100/416, a useState(open) at 417, and a Collapsible when replies exist). filteredThreads === threads when no filter is active (line 129), so the entire fetched set renders.

The 50,000 ceiling is real and reachable: FETCH_ALL_MAX = 50_000 (line 97), handleFetchAll requests exactly that (line 167), and the IPC schema confirms it at ipc-schemas.ts:122 `z.int().min(1).max(50_000)`. The comment block above that schema (lines 115-119) even acknowledges "the highest-volume videos." So a popular video's Fetch all can hand the renderer tens of thousands of comment objects, all of which mount synchronously in one React commit вҖ” a clear multi-second main-thread freeze plus large DOM/memory footprint.

The keystroke concern is also valid: filteredThreads is a useMemo keyed on usernameFilter/textFilter (line 146); each keystroke recomputes the filter over the full set and re-renders all surviving rows (each a fresh component tree because CommentRow holds local useState, so React must reconcile every mounted instance).

The codebase already solves exactly this problem elsewhere: VirtualAuditList.tsx uses @tanstack/react-virtual (already a dependency) precisely because "a plain entries.map(...) mounted every row up-front, which dropped scroll performance to a crawl past ~500 entries" вҖ” and that list is capped at 1000, far below comments' 50k. So the suggested fix is directly precedented and low-risk.

I checked for mitigations: there is no slice/cap on the rendered array, no react-window/virtual usage in CommentsTab, and the ScrollArea is just an overflow container (it does not window children). The only bound is on how many are *fetched*, not how many are *rendered*.

**Verifier notes**

Repro: open a video tab with a high comment count, click "Fetch all" (Zap button, line 393). yt-dlp scrapes up to 50k; on success the renderer mounts that many CommentRow trees in one commit. Even a few thousand will jank; 10k-50k freezes for seconds. Note the freeze magnitude depends on yt-dlp actually returning that many comments (rate-limited scraping may cut it short), but the render path itself is fully unbounded and is the bug. Two-tier fix as the reviewer suggests: (1) virtualize with useVirtualizer like VirtualAuditList.tsx (rows are NOT uniform height here вҖ” Collapsible replies expand вҖ” so rely on measureElement + a reasonable estimateSize); (2) a cheap interim guard is to render `filteredThreads.slice(0, N)` with a "show more" pager so even an unvirtualized commit stays bounded. The Collapsible's per-row useState(open) means virtualization must preserve expand state across recycle (lift open-state into a Set keyed by thread.top.id, or accept collapse-on-scroll). Filtering also stays O(n) per keystroke; debouncing the filter inputs would help but is secondary to the render bound.

---

### F05 вҖ” yt-dlp URL is argument-injectable: no end-of-options `--` and no scheme validation

- **Severity:** рҹ”ҙ HIGH
- **Category:** security
- **Location:** `src/main/framework-drivers/yt-dlp/YtDlpDownloader.ts:31, 88-96, 143, 221-234, 297-307, 404-467`
- **Confidence:** 0.82 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

Passing the value as a separate argv element prevents *shell* injection (shell:false) but NOT *argument* injection. yt-dlp parses any positional value beginning with `-` as an option. A URL like `--exec` / `--exec=calc.exe` (runs an arbitrary command per downloaded file), `--config-location=<path>`, or `-o<traversal>` is interpreted as a flag, not a video URL. The trigger is a renderer-supplied string the user pastes into the download box (a crafted clipboard/page value) or a compromised renderer (XSS). `--exec` yields arbitrary code execution. The 2026-04-28 security audit (audits/06-security.md:568) explicitly marked 'yt-dlp argument injection for URLs' as safe because URLs are 'separate array elements' вҖ” it covered shell injection but missed the leading-dash option-injection vector.

**Evidence**

~~~text
Every yt-dlp invocation appends the caller-supplied URL as the final positional arg with no `--` separator before it, e.g. fetchInfo: `const args = ['--dump-json', '--no-download', '--no-playlist', '--no-warnings', url]`; download: `'-o', `${outputDir}/${videoId}.%(ext)s`, url`. The IPC schema validates the URL as a bare string only вҖ” `'download-video': z.tuple([z.string(), z.string()])` and `'fetch-video-info': z.tuple([z.string()])` (src/shared/ipc-schemas.ts:89-90) вҖ” no `.url()`, no http(s) restriction, no max length.
~~~

**Fix**

Insert a literal `'--'` element immediately before `url` in every yt-dlp args array (fetchInfo, fetchChannelInfo, fetchVideoDetail, fetchTranscript, fetchComments, download) so yt-dlp treats the URL strictly as a positional. Additionally tighten the IPC schemas for `download-video`/`fetch-video-info`/`fetch-channel-info`/`fetch-video-detail`/`get-transcript` to `z.string().url().max(4096)` and reject non-http(s) schemes at the use-case boundary.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I read YtDlpDownloader.ts in full and every cited args array is exactly as quoted: fetchInfo (L31), fetchChannelInfo (L88-96), fetchVideoDetail (L143), fetchTranscript (L221-234), fetchComments (L297-307), and download (L404-467) all append the caller-supplied url/channelUrl as the FINAL positional with NO literal '--' end-of-options separator anywhere. All six use spawn(bin, args, { stdio: [...] }) with the default shell:false, so classic shell injection is blocked вҖ” but yt-dlp itself treats any positional beginning with '-' as an option. Flags like --exec / --exec=CMD (runs an arbitrary command per file вҶ’ arbitrary code execution), --config-location, --batch-file, or -o<traversal> would be parsed as options rather than a video URL. The end-of-options '--' is the standard defense and it is absent.

The IPC schemas in ipc-schemas.ts confirm the boundary is wide open: 'fetch-video-info' = z.tuple([z.string()]) (L89), 'download-video' = z.tuple([z.string(), z.string()]) (L90), 'fetch-channel-info' (L93), 'fetch-video-detail' (L108), 'get-transcript' (L110) вҖ” all bare z.string() with no .url(), no http(s) restriction, no max length. Notably the file's OWN header comment (L7-21) and other entries (e.g. 'open-external-url' uses z.string().url() at L220) prove the authors know how to constrain URLs and chose not to here.

I traced the path from boundary to spawn for false positives: DownloadController passes url straight through; FetchVideoInfo.execute only checks url.trim().length>0; DownloadVideo.execute only checks non-empty. No scheme/host validation exists in main at all. The only URL validation (isYouTubeUrl/isHttpUrl in src/renderer/lib/youtube-url.ts) lives in the RENDERER and is a UX filter, not a security control вҖ” and the codebase's stated threat model (ipc-schemas.ts L7-15) explicitly assumes a renderer compromised by stored-YouTube-content XSS can call window.api.* with arbitrary payloads, which bypasses renderer validation entirely. The videoId from yt-dlp IS allowlisted (DownloadVideo L172), but that protects the -o template, not the URL positional.

audits/06-security.md L568 confirms the reviewer's claim: 'yt-dlp argument injection for URLs вҖ” all URLs passed as separate array elements; shell:false' marks this clean, covering only shell injection and missing the leading-dash option-injection vector entirely.

The reviewer's only slight imprecision: the trigger requires either an XSS-compromised renderer or a UI path that lets an arbitrary string reach the channel without renderer validation. The renderer normally gates the download box. So real-world exploitability hinges on the XSS-compromised-renderer assumption вҖ” which is precisely the threat model this very file adopts to justify all its other zod caps. Under that adopted model the finding stands.

**Verifier notes**

Repro under the codebase's own threat model: a renderer compromised via stored-content XSS calls window.api['download-video']('--exec=calc.exe https://youtu.be/x', 'creator') or window.api['fetch-video-info']('--exec=touch /tmp/pwned'). The bare z.string() schema accepts it; FetchVideoInfo/DownloadVideo accept any non-empty string; YtDlpDownloader spawns yt-dlp with the string as a trailing positional and no '--', so yt-dlp parses --exec as a flag and runs the command for each processed item вҶ’ arbitrary code execution in the main process context.

Two-part fix, both needed (defense in depth): (1) insert a literal '--' element immediately before url/channelUrl in all six args arrays in YtDlpDownloader.ts вҖ” this is the load-bearing fix and is cheap/local. (2) Tighten the schemas to z.string().url().max(4096) for fetch-video-info/download-video/fetch-channel-info/fetch-video-detail and reject non-http(s) at the use-case boundary (FetchVideoInfo.execute / DownloadVideo.execute), mirroring the existing 'open-external-url' z.string().url() precedent at ipc-schemas.ts:220. Note get-transcript (L110) maps to fetchTranscript which also lacks '--'; include it. The '--' fix alone closes the ACE; the schema fix closes the broader argument-injection class and matches the file's existing hardening conventions. Severity high is appropriate (ACE) but is gated on the XSS-compromised-renderer precondition, consistent with how the repo scopes its other IPC-hardening findings; not critical because there is no remote-without-XSS trigger given renderer-side URL gating on the normal path.

---

### F06 вҖ” yt-dlp option injection via unvalidated download/fetch URL (no -- terminator)

- **Severity:** рҹ”ҙ HIGH
- **Category:** security
- **Location:** `src/main/framework-drivers/yt-dlp/YtDlpDownloader.ts:31, 88-96, 143, 221-234, 297-307, 404-467`
- **Confidence:** 0.8 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

The download URL is a renderer-supplied (user-pasted) free-form string. It reaches every yt-dlp spawn as a trailing positional argument with no '--' argument terminator and no http(s) scheme check. yt-dlp parses any argument beginning with '-' as an OPTION, not a URL. A value like '--exec=calc.exe' (or '--config-location=\\attacker\share\evil.conf', whose config can itself set --exec) yields arbitrary command execution by the yt-dlp child process. Under the threat model a compromised renderer (XSS via stored YouTube content) can call window.api.downloadVideo('--exec=...', 'x') directly; even absent XSS, a user pasting a crafted 'link' from a forum trips it. The baseline audit (06-security 'Verified clean') explicitly declared yt-dlp URL injection safe because URLs are 'passed as separate array elements' вҖ” that reasoning is incorrect: array elements prevent shell metacharacter injection but NOT option injection when the value starts with '-' and no '--' terminates the option list.

**Evidence**

~~~text
const args = ['--dump-json', '--no-download', '--no-playlist', '--no-warnings', url]
const proc = spawn(bin, args, { stdio: ['ignore', 'pipe', 'pipe'] })  // url is the final positional element, NOT preceded by a '--' separator. Provenance: DownloadController 'download-video' / 'fetch-video-info' schema is z.tuple([z.string()]) (ipc-schemas.ts:89-90) and FetchVideoInfo.execute only checks url.trim().length>0 вҖ” no scheme validation anywhere.
~~~

**Fix**

Two defenses, both cheap: (1) Insert a literal '--' immediately before `url` in every yt-dlp args array so yt-dlp treats everything after it as positional (e.g. ['--dump-json', ..., '--', url]). (2) Validate the scheme at the use-case / schema boundary: reject anything where new URL(url).protocol is not https:/http: (tighten further to the youtube host allowlist already defined in security-hardening.ts). Apply the same '--' + scheme check to fetchChannelInfo (FetchChannelInfo.ts).

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I read the full chain and the cited lines match the quotes. In src/main/framework-drivers/yt-dlp/YtDlpDownloader.ts, every yt-dlp spawn places the renderer-supplied URL as the trailing positional argument with NO '--' terminator: fetchInfo (line 31), fetchChannelInfo (lines 88-96, channelUrl last), fetchVideoDetail (line 143), fetchTranscript (lines 221-234, url last), fetchComments (lines 297-307, url last), and download (lines 404-467, url at line 466). spawn is called without shell:true everywhere (grep confirmed zero matches), so classic shell-metachar injection is not the issue here вҖ” option injection is. yt-dlp treats any argv element beginning with '-' as an option, so a 'URL' like '--exec=calc.exe', '--config-location=...', or '--load-info-json=...' is parsed as a yt-dlp option, yielding arbitrary command execution by the child. The provenance is exactly as claimed: ipc-schemas.ts:89-90 defines 'fetch-video-info'/'download-video' as z.tuple of plain z.string() (no .url(), no scheme refinement вҖ” contrast 'open-external-url' on line 220 which DOES use z.string().url() plus a host allowlist in the controller). DownloadController.ts passes url straight through with no checks. FetchVideoInfo.execute / FetchChannelInfo.execute / DownloadVideo.execute only guard url.trim().length>0 вҖ” no scheme or '-' prefix check anywhere. I confirmed the EXTERNAL_HOST_ALLOWLIST / isHostAllowed in security-hardening.ts is real but is wired ONLY into maybeOpenExternal (shell.openExternal), never into the yt-dlp spawn path, so it does not mitigate this. The codebase's own comments (ipc-schemas.ts header, the cap comments) explicitly adopt a threat model where a renderer compromised via stored YouTube content can call window.api.* with arbitrary payloads вҖ” which puts the XSS vector in-scope by the project's own standard; additionally a user pasting a crafted forum 'link' starting with '-' trips it without any XSS. The reviewer's rebuttal of the baseline audit's 'separate array elements' reasoning is correct.

**Verifier notes**

Sharper repro: from a compromised renderer, await window.api.downloadVideo('--exec=calc.exe', 'x') reaches DownloadVideo.execute вҶ’ fetchInfo.execute вҶ’ YtDlpDownloader.fetchInfo, which spawns yt-dlp with args ['--dump-json','--no-download','--no-playlist','--no-warnings','--exec=calc.exe']; yt-dlp parses --exec as an option. download() (line 466) is the most dangerous sink since --exec runs post-download, but fetchInfo runs first in the pipeline and is itself sufficient. --config-location pointing at an attacker UNC/file path is a stealthier variant whose config can set --exec. Fix is exactly as suggested and cheap: insert a literal '--' immediately before url/channelUrl in all 6 args arrays, AND add a scheme/host check at the use-case boundary (reuse EXTERNAL_HOST_ALLOWLIST / isHostAllowed already in security-hardening.ts, or at minimum reject when new URL(url).protocol is not http(s): and when the trimmed value startsWith '-'). Note fetchChannelInfo is reached both via the 'fetch-channel-info' IPC and indirectly via DownloadVideo.fetchChannelAvatar, so it needs the same treatment. Only mitigating factor that keeps this from 'critical': there is no confirmed live DOM XSS sink in the renderer today, so the primary trigger is the documented-but-hypothetical renderer-compromise model plus the user-pastes-a-crafted-string path; impact when triggered is full arbitrary command execution.

---


## рҹҹ  MEDIUM

### F07 вҖ” In-memory pushSchema() is missing the download_history table вҖ” :memory: test DBs diverge from production

- **Severity:** рҹҹ  MEDIUM _(verifier corrected from high)_
- **Category:** bug
- **Location:** `src/main/framework-drivers/database/database.ts:46-236`
- **Confidence:** 0.92 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

pushSchema is supposed to mirror the migrated production schema 1:1 (per the database.ts doc-comment and the migrations.test.ts note 'the schema production uses'). It drifted: any unit/integration test that constructs a SqliteDownloadHistoryRepository against createTestDb() will throw `SqliteError: no such table: download_history`. The persistent finished-downloads feature (DownloadHistoryController, ListDownloadHistory, RetryDownload) therefore cannot be tested against the in-memory harness at all, and the divergence will silently hide future regressions in that code path.

**Evidence**

~~~text
pushSchema() creates creators, videos, cuts, settings, operations, audit_log, collections, collection_videos, collection_cuts and the FTS5 objects, but there is NO `CREATE TABLE ... download_history`. The real schema (schema.ts:281-304) and migration 0011_slimy_blue_shield.sql both define `download_history`. createTestDb() (tests/main/helpers/createTestDb.ts) returns initializeDatabase(':memory:'), which calls pushSchema.
~~~

**Fix**

Add a `CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS download_history (...)` block plus `CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_download_history_finished_at ON download_history(finished_at)` to pushSchema, matching 0011's DDL. Better: replace the hand-maintained pushSchema with a generated-DDL push (drizzle-kit) or run the on-disk migrations into :memory: so the two can never drift again.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I read database.ts:46-236 in full. pushSchema() creates creators, videos, cuts, settings, operations, audit_log, collections, collection_videos, collection_cuts, all indexes, and the FTS5 virtual table + triggers вҖ” but there is NO `CREATE TABLE download_history` and no `idx_download_history_finished_at` index. Meanwhile production defines this table: schema.ts:281-304 declares `downloadHistory = sqliteTable('download_history', ...)` with the finished_at index, and migration 0011_slimy_blue_shield.sql creates the table + index on disk. createTestDb() (tests/main/helpers/createTestDb.ts:14-16) returns initializeDatabase(':memory:'), and database.ts:32-33 routes :memory: through pushSchema (file migrations are only run for on-disk paths). So the in-memory test schema genuinely diverges from production for this one table. This also directly violates the project's own documented contract: AGENTS.md:169 ('Update the pushSchema() function ... to match the new schema') and AGENTS.md:499 / 860 ('pushSchema() matches the production schema'). The divergence is real and the suggested fix (add the matching CREATE TABLE/INDEX, or generate the push from drizzle / replay migrations into :memory:) is correct.

**Verifier notes**

The factual core is confirmed, but the reviewer's high severity overstates current impact. There is NO existing test for the download-history path: glob tests/**/*DownloadHistory* finds nothing, and grep for SqliteDownloadHistoryRepository/download_history across tests/ returns no matches. So nothing throws today вҖ” the claim 'any test that constructs SqliteDownloadHistoryRepository against createTestDb() will throw no such table: download_history' is a correct prediction of what WOULD happen, not a currently-failing test. This is a latent test-infrastructure divergence: it blocks writing in-memory tests for DownloadHistoryController/ListDownloadHistory/RetryDownload and will silently let that path go untested. Repro for confirmation: in any test, `new SqliteDownloadHistoryRepository(createTestDb().db).list(...)` (or equivalent) throws SqliteError: no such table: download_history. Production runtime is unaffected (on-disk DBs run 0011). Severity medium given real schema-drift + violated documented contract but zero current functional/test breakage.

---

### F08 вҖ” pushSchema() omits the download_history table (breaks :memory: tests + violates documented migration workflow)

- **Severity:** рҹҹ  MEDIUM
- **Category:** bug
- **Location:** `src/main/framework-drivers/database/database.ts:46-236`
- **Confidence:** 0.92 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

AGENTS.md's migration workflow (step 3, lines 169 & 499) mandates updating pushSchema() to match every schema change so in-memory test DBs stay in sync. download_history was added (entity, SqliteDownloadHistoryRepository, ListDownloadHistory/RetryDownload use-cases, DownloadHistoryController, migration 0011) but pushSchema was never updated. The bug is latent today only because no test instantiates SqliteDownloadHistoryRepository against createTestDb(); the moment one does (per the testing convention at AGENTS.md:617 'Repository tests instantiate the real Sqlite*Repository with the Drizzle db from createTestDb()'), it will fail with 'no such table: download_history'. File-based prod DBs are unaffected (they run migrate()).

**Evidence**

~~~text
pushSchema() creates creators, videos, cuts, settings, operations, audit_log, collections, collection_videos, collection_cuts (+ videos_fts), but there is NO `CREATE TABLE ... download_history`. The schema (schema.ts:281 `export const downloadHistory = sqliteTable('download_history', ...)`) and migration 0011_slimy_blue_shield.sql both define it.
~~~

**Fix**

Add the `CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS download_history (...)` + `CREATE INDEX idx_download_history_finished_at` block to pushSchema(), mirroring 0011_slimy_blue_shield.sql, the same way videos_fts mirrors 0009.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I read database.ts:46-236 in full. pushSchema() issues CREATE TABLE for exactly: creators, videos, cuts, settings, operations, audit_log, collections, collection_videos, collection_cuts, plus the videos_fts virtual table and its three triggers (explicitly noted as "mirrored in 0009"). There is NO CREATE TABLE for download_history and no idx_download_history_finished_at index. Meanwhile schema.ts defines downloadHistory and migration 0011_slimy_blue_shield.sql creates `download_history` + `idx_download_history_finished_at` вҖ” so the table is a real, current part of the schema. download_history is fully wired: SqliteDownloadHistoryRepository (real class), composition-root.ts:303 instantiates it against database.db, RetryDownload/DownloadVideo use-cases reference it. AGENTS.md:169 (Database Migrations Workflow step 3) explicitly mandates "Update the pushSchema() function in database.ts to match the new schema (for in-memory test DBs)" on every schema change вҖ” this step was skipped for 0011, a genuine spec violation. AGENTS.md:617 documents that repository tests instantiate the real Sqlite*Repository with the db from createTestDb() (which calls initializeDatabase(':memory:') -> pushSchema). I confirmed the bug is latent today: the only test touching download history (tests/main/use-cases/DownloadVideo.test.ts) uses a mockDownloadHistoryRepo() stub, not the real Sqlite repo, so nothing currently hits the missing table. File-based prod DBs run migrate() (database.ts:35-36) and are unaffected. The claim, evidence, location, and quoted lines all check out.

**Verifier notes**

Latent, not currently failing вҖ” only manifests when a real SqliteDownloadHistoryRepository test is written against createTestDb(); current coverage uses a mock (DownloadVideo.test.ts:135 mockDownloadHistoryRepo). Repro to confirm: write tests/main/interface-adapters/repositories/SqliteDownloadHistoryRepository.test.ts that does `const { db } = createTestDb(); new SqliteDownloadHistoryRepository(db).list()` -> throws SqliteError 'no such table: download_history'. Fix: add `CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS download_history (...)` mirroring 0011 plus `CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_download_history_finished_at ON download_history(finished_at)` to pushSchema, exactly as videos_fts mirrors 0009. Medium (not higher) is fair: no production impact and no current test breakage; it is a forward-looking spec-compliance gap that will bite the next repo test author. One nuance: 0011 declares finished_at NOT NULL DEFAULT (datetime('now')) and error_retryable integer DEFAULT true NOT NULL вҖ” mirror those defaults faithfully.

### F09 вҖ” No spawn timeout on fetchInfo/fetchVideoDetail/fetchChannelInfo/download/probe вҖ” hung yt-dlp leaks process, promise never settles

- **Severity:** рҹҹ  MEDIUM
- **Category:** bug
- **Location:** `src/main/framework-drivers/yt-dlp/YtDlpDownloader.ts:22-75, 79-134, 138-204`
- **Confidence:** 0.78 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

yt-dlp can stall indefinitely on a network hang, a captcha/consent wall, or a geo-block that keeps a connection open. fetchInfo is invoked synchronously when a user adds a download (DownloadVideo.ts:164) with no user-facing cancel path. A stalled call leaves the child process alive and the returned Promise pending forever, so the download row sits in 'fetching-info' with no error and the user cannot retry. Multiple stalled adds leak multiple orphaned yt-dlp processes.

**Evidence**

~~~text
fetchInfo/fetchVideoDetail/fetchChannelInfo each do `const proc = spawn(bin, args, ...)` and only resolve/reject inside `proc.on('close')` / `proc.on('error')`. There is no setTimeout reaper. Only fetchComments has one (line 321-331: `const timeoutMs = Math.min(15*60_000, 60_000 + maxComments*120)`). FfprobeMediaProbe.runFfprobe (src/main/framework-drivers/ffprobe/FfprobeMediaProbe.ts:45-102) is likewise timeout-less.
~~~

**Fix**

Wrap each metadata/probe spawn in the same settled-guard + setTimeout(kill('SIGTERM')) reaper pattern already used in fetchComments (e.g. a 60-120s cap for info calls), rejecting with a timeout error so the use-case can mark the row failed and retryable.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I read the cited file in full. fetchInfo (22-75), fetchChannelInfo (79-134), fetchVideoDetail (138-204), and fetchTranscript (208-286) each do `spawn(bin, args, {stdio})` and resolve/reject ONLY inside `proc.on('close')` / `proc.on('error')`. None install a setTimeout reaper. The only method with one is fetchComments (lines 312-331: `settled` guard + `setTimeout(() => { proc.kill('SIGTERM'); reject(...) }, timeoutMs)`). FfprobeMediaProbe.runFfprobe (41-103) is likewise timeout-less. The download() method (386-557) also has no spawn-level timeout, though it at least registers the proc in activeProcesses so cancel() can kill it. The metadata methods do NOT register in activeProcesses вҖ” cancel() (561-567) only looks up that map, so a hung fetchInfo child is genuinely unreachable by cancel. Caller chain confirms exposure: DownloadVideo.performDownload awaits this.fetchInfo.execute(url) at line 164 on the critical add-download path, after emitting status 'fetching-info' (155-163); FetchVideoInfo.execute is a pure pass-through with no timeout. So a yt-dlp stall (consent/captcha wall, geo-block, slow-trickle connection) leaves the child alive and the Promise pending forever, the row stuck in 'fetching-info', no cancel path, and repeated adds leak multiple orphaned processes. yt-dlp's --socket-timeout is per-read, not a total wall-clock cap, so it does not save this. No higher-level guard (zod, transaction wrapper, AbortController) handles it. The finding is accurate as written.

**Verifier notes**

Sharper repro: add a download whose URL hits an interstitial that keeps the HTTP connection open (or pull the network mid-handshake after spawn). The 'fetching-info' row never transitions and the yt-dlp PID persists; cancel() is a no-op because activeProcesses is populated only in download() (line 470), never by fetchInfo. Best fix is the existing fetchComments pattern: a `settled` flag + setTimeout(SIGTERM)+reject (~60-120s cap) wrapped around each metadata spawn AND runFfprobe; rejecting lets DownloadVideo classify the error retriable so the row can fail and retry. Scope note for the team: the same timeout-less spawn applies to fetchVideoDetail/fetchTranscript (and ffprobe via ProbeMediaFile/EnrichMediaMetadata), so a single shared spawn-with-timeout helper would cover all of them rather than patching one method.

---

### F10 вҖ” EnrichMediaMetadata read-modify-write clobbers concurrent updates to the same video/cut row

- **Severity:** рҹҹ  MEDIUM
- **Category:** bug
- **Location:** `src/main/use-cases/EnrichMediaMetadata.ts:29-50`
- **Confidence:** 0.72 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

`video` (the full row) is read at the top of execute(), then ffprobe is awaited (can take seconds for large files). The repo `upsert` writes EVERY column of the stale snapshot back (insert-or-replace; confirmed in SqliteVideoRepository.upsert which sets all fields including status, viewCount, transcriptText, detailFetchedAt). If anything mutates that row during the await window вҖ” `MarkVideoMissing` flipping status to 'missing' (reachable from download/youtube-error paths), or `FetchVideoDetail` (run via EnrichAllVideos queue, also a full read-then-upsert) writing viewCount/likeCount/transcriptText вҖ” that concurrent write is silently lost, or a freshly-set 'missing' status is reverted to the stale 'active'. Both flows are triggered after reconcile discovers new videos, so the windows overlap in practice. Same hazard exists for the cut loop.

**Evidence**

~~~text
const metadata = await this.mediaProbe.probe(video.filePath)
        this.videoRepo.upsert({
          ...video,
          duration: metadata.duration ?? video.duration,
          ... probeStatus: 'complete', updatedAt: new Date().toISOString()
        })
~~~

**Fix**

Don't write back the whole stale entity. Use a narrow update that only touches the probed columns (a dedicated repo method like updateProbeResult(id, {duration, resolution, fileSize, probeStatus}) using SQL SET on those columns), or re-read the row inside the write and merge, so concurrent status/detail changes survive. The existing updateProbeStatus pattern shows the column-scoped approach already exists.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I read EnrichMediaMetadata.ts, SqliteVideoRepository.ts (the real path is src/main/interface-adapters/repositories/), AuditedVideoRepository.ts, FetchVideoDetail.ts, MarkVideoMissing.ts, EnrichAllVideos.ts, ProcessFileNotifications.ts and database.ts.

The mechanism is exactly as claimed:
1. EnrichMediaMetadata.execute() reads full rows via findByProbeStatus('pending') up front, then per-row awaits this.mediaProbe.probe(video.filePath) (seconds for large files), then synchronously calls this.videoRepo.upsert({...video, duration, resolution, fileSize, probeStatus:'complete', updatedAt}).
2. SqliteVideoRepository.upsert (lines 189-252) writes EVERY column via onConflictDoUpdate set: { ... = excluded.* } including status, viewCount, likeCount, transcriptText, transcriptPath, detailFetchedAt, description, tags, etc. So the stale snapshot overwrites whatever the row currently holds вҖ” this is a true read-modify-write clobber, not a column-scoped UPDATE.
3. The DB is synchronous better-sqlite3, but the use-cases are async and interleave on the single event loop across the await probe boundary. During that window, FetchVideoDetail (run via the EnrichAllVideos dedicated queue) does its own full read-then-upsert of viewCount/likeCount/transcriptText/detailFetchedAt, and MarkVideoMissing (reachable from FetchVideoDetail's YouTube-error path) does updateStatus(...,'missing',...). A newly downloaded video is simultaneously probeStatus='pending' (qualifies for EnrichMediaMetadata) AND detailFetchedAt IS NULL (qualifies for EnrichAllVideos/findNeedingDetail), so both pipelines target the same rows at the same time вҖ” the overlap is real, not hypothetical.
4. The audited decorator does NOT save this: AuditedVideoRepository.upsert re-reads findById only to compute the audit diff, but still passes the caller's stale `video` to inner.upsert(video). The transactionScope.run makes each individual write atomic but the stale snapshot was captured before the transaction, so concurrent writes between the read and the write are silently lost.

Extra reinforcement the reviewer didn't note: the `if (video.status !== 'active') continue` guard (line 30) reads the stale in-memory status from before the await, so it does not protect against a status flip to 'missing' during the probe вҖ” the subsequent upsert writes status:'active' back from the snapshot, reverting MarkVideoMissing. Same hazard applies verbatim to the cut loop (lines 53-65) for any concurrent cut mutation, though cuts have fewer concurrent writers.

The audit doc (audits/02-weird-logic.md S10) already flags a related concern (two enrichMedia runs racing) and ProcessFileNotifications now guards self-overlap with this.enrichPromise вҖ” but that guard only dedupes EnrichMediaMetadata against itself; it does nothing for the cross-use-case race against FetchVideoDetail/MarkVideoMissing, which is the actual bug claimed here. So this is not a false positive on 'already handled' grounds.

**Verifier notes**

Confirmed at medium. Realistic data-loss repro: user downloads a video вҶ’ it lands probeStatus='pending', detailFetchedAt=NULL вҶ’ ProcessFileNotifications.flush() fires EnrichMediaMetadata (fire-and-forget) AND the user/post-download flow triggers EnrichAllVideosвҶ’FetchVideoDetail on the same row. FetchVideoDetail upserts viewCount/likeCount/tags/transcriptText/detailFetchedAt while EnrichMediaMetadata is awaiting ffprobe; when ffprobe resolves, EnrichMediaMetadata.upsert writes its stale snapshot back, wiping the just-fetched detail (detailFetchedAt reverts to NULL вҶ’ the row re-qualifies for findNeedingDetail and gets re-fetched, wasting a YouTube request, or stays permanently un-enriched if the loop already passed it). The status-revert variant (missingвҶ’active) is also real but rarer since it needs a YouTube error mid-window.

Severity is medium not higher: the race window requires a concurrent writer to hit the exact same row during the probe await; better-sqlite3 serializes the actual writes so there is no corruption, only last-writer-wins loss; and the lost data is recoverable on a subsequent enrich pass for the detail-clobber case. Not low because it silently loses already-fetched metadata and can revert a 'missing' flag, both user-visible.

Suggested fix is sound: add a column-scoped repo method (e.g. updateProbeResult(id, {duration, resolution, fileSize, probeStatus})) using a SET-only UPDATE, mirroring the existing updateProbeStatus/updateStatus pattern that already exists in SqliteVideoRepository (lines 289-303). That confines the write to the four probed columns and lets concurrent status/detail writes survive. Apply the same to the cut repo.

---

### F11 вҖ” MigrateRootFolder DB-update-failed branch leaves files at newRoot but rootPath at oldRoot with no recovery path, stranding the entire library

- **Severity:** рҹҹ  MEDIUM
- **Category:** bug
- **Location:** `src/main/use-cases/MigrateRootFolder.ts:181-195`
- **Confidence:** 0.62 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

If the transaction throws, all creator folders are physically at newRoot but settingsRepo.rootPath and all filePaths still reference oldRoot. The op is marked 'failed' (terminal), so RecoverOperations will NOT touch it on next launch, and the watcher is restarted on newRootPath even though rootPathRef.value was never updated (the mutation at line 180 only runs on commit). The app now watches/uses oldRoot semantics in the DB while files live at newRoot вҖ” every entity reads as missing and there is no automatic remedy. Because transaction.run rolls back the path rewrite this is unlikely in practice, but the chosen 'don't roll back files' strategy with a terminal 'failed' status guarantees a stuck, unrecoverable state when it does happen.

**Evidence**

~~~text
} catch (dbError) {
  // DB update failed after all folders moved вҖ” this is a critical state.
  // Mark operation failed but don't roll back files (they're already moved).
  this.operationRepo.updateStatus(operationId, 'failed', errorMsg)
  await this.fileWatcher.restart(newRootPath)
  ...
  return { success: false, movedCount: folders.length, error: `Files moved but DB update failed: ${errorMsg}` }
~~~

**Fix**

On dbError, roll the folders back to oldRoot (the DB never changed, so oldRoot is the consistent state) before marking failed, and restart the watcher on oldRootPath (not newRootPath). Alternatively keep the op non-terminal so RecoverOperations can finish the rollback.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I read MigrateRootFolder.ts:166-195 and RecoverOperations.ts in full. The finding is accurate on every load-bearing point:

1. Files are moved to newRoot BEFORE the DB transaction (lines 128-164 move folders; lines 174-178 do the DB rewrite). So when the transaction throws, folders are physically at newRoot.

2. transaction.run() wraps videoRepo/cutRepo prefix updates + settingsRepo.set('rootPath') atomically, so on dbError the DB filePaths and settings.rootPath remain at oldRoot (rolled back). Confirmed.

3. rootPathRef.value = newRootPath is line 180, OUTSIDE/after the transaction, so on dbError it never runs вҖ” rootPathRef stays oldRoot. Confirmed.

4. The dbError branch (181-195) marks the op 'failed' (line 186) and restarts the watcher on newRootPath (line 187). This is asserted as intentional in MigrateRootFolder.test.ts:312-313 ("Watcher restarted on new root (files are already there)").

5. RecoverOperations.execute() (lines 87-89) queries ONLY findByStatus('pending') and findByStatus('in_progress'). A 'failed' operation is never enumerated, so there is no automatic recovery for this state. Confirmed вҖ” 'failed' is terminal for recovery.

Resulting incoherent state when the transaction throws: files at newRoot, but DB filePaths + settings.rootPath + rootPathRef all at oldRoot. Every video/cut filePath resolves to oldRoot where nothing exists вҶ’ reads as missing. The watcher is on newRoot but the DB/rootPathRef semantics are oldRoot. No automatic remedy exists. The reviewer's chosen-fix analysis (roll folders back to oldRoot since the DB is consistent at oldRoot, OR keep op non-terminal) is the correct remedy.

The one nuance: the trigger probability is genuinely low. better-sqlite3 transactions are synchronous and atomic, and the only operations inside are simple prefix UPDATEs + a settings set; a throw there is unusual (e.g. DB locked/corrupt/disk error). The reviewer correctly notes this. But the consequence is catastrophic (entire library stranded, no auto-recovery), so it is a real latent bug, not a false positive.

**Verifier notes**

Confirmed real, not handled anywhere. Verified: (a) RecoverOperations.ts:87-89 only scans 'pending'+'in_progress' вҖ” 'failed' is never recovered; (b) transaction.run at MigrateRootFolder.ts:174-178 rolls back the path rewrite so DB stays at oldRoot, while files were already moved to newRoot at 128-164; (c) rootPathRef.value=newRootPath at line 180 is post-transaction so it stays oldRoot on dbError; (d) watcher-on-newRoot at line 187 is deliberately asserted in MigrateRootFolder.test.ts:312-313.

Sharper repro: trigger the catch at line 181 (e.g. SQLITE_BUSY / disk error during videoRepo.updateFilePathPrefix). Outcome: folders live at newRoot, DB+settings+rootPathRef all at oldRoot, op='failed'. On next launch RecoverOperations skips it (terminal). All videos resolve to oldRoot and read as missing; the user has no in-app remedy.

Severity kept at medium: severe blast radius (whole library) but narrow trigger (atomic sync sqlite transaction rarely throws). Suggested fix matches: on dbError move folders back to oldRoot (DB is already consistent there) and restart watcher on oldRootPath, OR leave the op 'in_progress'/'pending' so RecoverOperations.recoverMigrateRootOp can finish the reverse moves (it already handles v2 'moved' entries idempotently at lines 191-223).

---

### F12 вҖ” Save dialog double-click fires two renders / creates two cut rows

- **Severity:** рҹҹ  MEDIUM
- **Category:** bug
- **Location:** `src/renderer/components/features/editor/SaveCutDialog.tsx:63-91, 139`
- **Confidence:** 0.7 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** yes

**Impact**

submitting is React state, set asynchronously. The guard `if (!timeline || !canSubmit) return` reads the value captured in the click closure. Two fast clicks (or a double-click) both enter handleSubmit before React commits the setSubmitting(true) re-render that disables the button, so editorStartRender fires twice -> two render jobs and two Cut rows for the same trim. The disabled attribute alone does not protect against the second in-flight discrete event. This is MI-12 from the prior editor review, still unfixed.

**Evidence**

~~~text
const canSubmit = saveable && titleTrimmed.length > 0 && !submitting
const handleSubmit = async (): Promise<void> => {
  if (!timeline || !canSubmit) return
  setSubmitting(true)
  ...
  const response = await window.api.editorStartRender({ recipe, title: titleTrimmed, tags })
  beginTracking({ jobId: response.jobId, cutId: response.cutId })
...
<Button onClick={handleSubmit} disabled={!canSubmit}>
~~~

**Fix**

Add a synchronous ref guard: `const submittingRef = useRef(false)`; at the top of handleSubmit do `if (submittingRef.current) return; submittingRef.current = true` and reset in finally. Refs update synchronously so the second click is rejected.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I read SaveCutDialog.tsx (lines 45-91, 139) and the cited code matches the finding verbatim. `canSubmit` (line 65) is derived from the `submitting` React state; `handleSubmit` (line 67) gates only on `if (!timeline || !canSubmit) return`, then calls the async `setSubmitting(true)` (line 69) before the synchronous work, with the IPC `await` at line 79. The Button's `disabled={!canSubmit}` (line 139) only updates after React commits the re-render. There is NO synchronous ref guard. Two discrete click events processed before that commit both capture `submitting=false` in their render closures and both pass the gate.\n\nI then traced the downstream blast radius to rule out a handled-elsewhere false positive: EditorController.ts:38 calls `renderCut.execute(request)` unconditionally with no dedupe. RenderCutFromVideo.execute (src/main/use-cases/RenderCutFromVideo.ts:71-260) mints a fresh `cutId`/`jobId` per call (lines 101-102), inserts an operation row (146), inserts a Cut row via `cutRepo.upsertWithPrevious` (177), opens a session, and enqueues a render (207). There is no idempotency key, no in-flight-by-recipe check, and no unique constraint that would collapse the second submission. So two invocations genuinely produce two distinct Cut rows, two operation rows, and two render jobs for the same trim.\n\nThis is MI-12 from plans/editor-review-findings.md:345 (logged at 65% confidence, marked 'to verify'), and the companion low-priority doc line 390 lists the double-submit guard as still uncovered. The code shows it remains unfixed. The reviewer's suggested fix (submittingRef via useRef, set synchronously at the top of handleSubmit, reset in finally) is the correct remedy since refs update synchronously and reject the second in-flight event.

**Verifier notes**

Real race, but the exploit window is narrow: React processes discrete click events and typically flushes the re-render between them, so a single deliberate double-click often does NOT slip two calls through. The reliable repro is two clicks landing within the same synchronous event-dispatch window before the commit (very fast machine, programmatic/replayed click, or input lag). Consequence when it does fire is concrete and user-visible: two phantom Cut rows + two ffmpeg render jobs for the same trim, both pointing at distinct cutId folders. Severity is at the boundary of low/medium вҖ” I'd keep medium because the consequence (duplicate persisted rows + wasted render) is non-trivial and there is zero downstream guard, but a case for low is defensible given the timing window and required user action. Confirmed unfixed; the useRef guard the reviewer suggests is the right fix.

---

### F13 вҖ” Manual reconcile leaves the entire UI stale (no invalidation, no db-updated push)

- **Severity:** рҹҹ  MEDIUM _(verifier corrected from high)_
- **Category:** bug
- **Location:** `src/renderer/hooks/use-reconcile.ts:4-8`
- **Confidence:** 0.92 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

useReconcile has no onSuccess invalidation. The main side is also silent: ReconcileController.registerReconcileController (src/main/interface-adapters/controllers/ReconcileController.ts:13-15) just calls reconcileDirectory.execute, and ReconcileDirectory (src/main/use-cases/ReconcileDirectory.ts) contains zero notifier.notify('db-updated', ...) calls even though it adds creators/videos/cuts, marks entities missing, and recovers them inside its transaction. ReconcileButton (src/renderer/components/features/settings/ReconcileButton.tsx:30-37) shows the numeric result card but nothing invalidates the React Query cache. After a user clicks 'Run reconcile' from Settings, every list (videos, creators, cuts), the dashboard stats, collections, search, and tag autocomplete keep showing the pre-reconcile data until an unrelated chokidar event fires or the window is reloaded. The result card claims 'videosAdded: 5' while the video grid still shows the old set вҖ” actively misleading.

**Evidence**

~~~text
export function useReconcile(): UseMutationResult<ReconcileResult, Error, void> {
  return useMutation({
    mutationFn: () => window.api.reconcile()
  })
}
~~~

**Fix**

Either fire this.notifier.notify('db-updated', { scope: ['all'] }) at the end of ReconcileDirectory.execute / executeForCreatorBatch, OR add onSuccess in useReconcile that invalidates creators.all, videos.all, cuts.all, collections.all, tags.all, search.all and stats.all. The push-based approach is more consistent with the rest of the codebase.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I read every cited file and the wiring. useReconcile (src/renderer/hooks/use-reconcile.ts:4-8) matches the quote exactly: a bare useMutation with only mutationFn, no onSuccess. ReconcileButton.handleReconcile (ReconcileButton.tsx:28-37) only setResult + toast on success вҖ” no queryClient invalidation. ReconcileController (lines 13-15) calls reconcileDirectory.execute(rootPath.value) directly. composition-root.ts:324-331 constructs ReconcileDirectory with (creatorRepo, videoRepo, cutRepo, fsReader, pathResolver, transactionScope) вҖ” NO notifier вҖ” and index.ts:122 registers that same instance for the IPC handler. ReconcileDirectory.ts contains zero notifier.notify calls (the class has no notifier field at all), even though execute/executeForCreatorBatch add creators/videos/cuts, mark entities missing, and recover them. The ONLY cache-invalidation mechanism is useDbListener (use-db-listener.ts) reacting to a db-updated push, and the ONLY place a reconcile-related db-updated fires is ProcessFileNotifications.ts:137 вҖ” the chokidar/auto path, which the manual Settings button does NOT traverse. So the push-based assumption recorded in audits/05-coverage.md:120 ("useReconcile relies on db-updated notification") is unfulfilled for the manual button. Result: after clicking Run reconcile, the result card shows e.g. videosAdded:5 while video/creator/cut lists, dashboard stats, collections, search, and tag autocomplete keep serving pre-reconcile cache until an unrelated chokidar event or a window reload occurs. This is a genuine stale-UI bug with a misleading result card. None of the common false-positive patterns apply вҖ” it is not handled elsewhere, the symbol/lines are accurate, and the suggested fix (notify db-updated scope:['all'] at end of execute/executeForCreatorBatch, or onSuccess invalidation in useReconcile) is correct.

**Verifier notes**

Confirmed real. Sharper repro: in Settings, with the watcher idle (or after it has already processed all on-disk state), manually delete a creator folder via the OS file explorer in a way the watcher misses, then click Run reconcile. The card reports creatorsMarkedMissing:1 but the creators grid, dashboard counts, and search still list the now-missing creator with no tombstone, until you reload (Ctrl+R) or trigger any other FS event. The manual button exists precisely for the case where the watcher has NOT kept the DB in sync, so the staleness window is the common case for this button, not the edge case. I down-grade high->medium only because: (a) the data IS correctly persisted in SQLite (this is a presentation-staleness bug, not data loss), and (b) in many real flows the same FS activity that motivates a reconcile also produces chokidar events that eventually fire db-updated scope:['all'], masking the issue. Preferred fix is the push-based one (add an INotifier to ReconcileDirectory's constructor and notify scope:['all'] at the end of execute / executeForCreatorBatch when result is non-empty) to stay consistent with every other mutating use case and so executeForCreator/Batch callers benefit too; the renderer-only onSuccess fix would not cover those other call sites. Note executeForCreator/executeForCreatorInternal are invoked from the granular path which is itself followed by the ProcessFileNotifications.ts:137 notify, so only the manual IPC entry point (ReconcileController) is actually unguarded.

### F14 вҖ” Migrations fresh-apply test asserts a table list that omits download_history вҖ” test is broken

- **Severity:** рҹҹ  MEDIUM
- **Category:** bug
- **Location:** `tests/main/framework-drivers/database/migrations.test.ts:48-80`
- **Confidence:** 0.9 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

Once better-sqlite3 is rebuilt for the current Node ABI (it is currently failing to load with NODE_MODULE_VERSION mismatch, masking this), this assertion fails: the actual publicTables now includes download_history. The migration contract test gives a false sense of coverage вҖ” the table-list guard is stale and will break CI as soon as the native module is fixed.

**Evidence**

~~~text
The test calls initializeDatabase(dbPath) on an on-disk temp file (so migrate() runs ALL 11 migrations, including 0011 which `CREATE TABLE download_history`), then asserts publicTables equals ['__drizzle_migrations','audit_log','collection_cuts','collection_videos','collections','creators','cuts','operations','settings','videos','videos_fts'].sort() вҖ” `download_history` is absent from the expected array.
~~~

**Fix**

Add 'download_history' to the expected publicTables array. Consider deriving the expected set from the schema module rather than a hardcoded list so adding a table updates the assertion automatically.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I read tests/main/framework-drivers/database/migrations.test.ts:47-80 and confirmed the cited assertion. The test calls initializeDatabase(dbPath) with an on-disk temp path (dbPath = join(tmpDir, 'klip-mig.db'), created in beforeEach), NOT ':memory:'. In src/main/framework-drivers/database/database.ts:32-37, the non-memory branch runs drizzle's migrate(db, { migrationsFolder }), applying every .sql in the migrations dir. The migrations folder contains 0000 through 0011 (11 migrations). 0011_slimy_blue_shield.sql is `CREATE TABLE download_history (...)` вҖ” a plain table, not sqlite_-prefixed and not containing '_fts_', so it survives the publicTables filter at line 59. The expected array at lines 64-76 lists 11 names and omits 'download_history'. Since the assertion is a strict `.toEqual` on sorted arrays, the actual result (12 names including download_history) will not equal the expected (11 names). The 0009 snapshot gap noted in project memory is irrelevant here вҖ” 0011 unconditionally creates download_history regardless. The reviewer is correct that this is currently masked: better-sqlite3 fails to load with a NODE_MODULE_VERSION ABI mismatch, so the test doesn't execute/pass meaningfully right now; once rebuilt, it fails.

**Verifier notes**

Confirmed test-only bug, no production impact, so medium is fair (it will break CI once the native module is rebuilt for the current Node ABI). Repro after fixing better-sqlite3: run vitest on migrations.test.ts; the 'applies every migration ... yields the expected tables' case fails with actual publicTables including 'download_history' (sorted, it lands right after 'cuts'/before 'operations'... actually after 'creators'/'cuts' вҖ” sorted position is between 'cuts' and 'operations'). Suggested fix is sound: add 'download_history' to the expected array, and ideally derive the expected set from the schema module (src/.../database/schema.ts) so future tables auto-update the guard. Note the same staleness risk applies to the trigger-count assertions and the idempotency test's hardcoded `triggers === 3` if trigger-bearing migrations are added later, but only the table-list assertion is currently wrong.
