### F15 вҖ” Startup blocks main-window creation on a synchronous full reconcile (2N directory syscalls before any UI)

- **Severity:** рҹҹ  MEDIUM
- **Category:** performance
- **Location:** `src/main/index.ts:194-231`
- **Confidence:** 0.7 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

reconcile.execute runs inside a synchronous better-sqlite3 transaction and is awaited (blocking) before createMainWindow(). Even in steady state with no new entities, ReconcileDirectory.reconcileVideos/reconcileCuts call this.fs.listDirectories(downloadsDir) and listDirectories(cutsDir) for every active creator (ReconcileDirectory.ts:303, :435) = 2N synchronous directory reads. At N=100 creators that is ~200 blocking syscalls on the main thread before the window paints; on a cold/network disk this is hundreds of ms to seconds of black-screen launch latency that scales linearly with creator count. First launches additionally do listFiles + readJsonFile per new video, all synchronous, pre-window.

**Evidence**

~~~text
// в”Җв”Җ Initial reconciliation (one-time full scan at startup) в”Җв”Җ
try {
  const result = container.useCases.reconcile.execute(rootPath)
  ...
}
...
container.ports.windowManager.createMainWindow()  // line 231, AFTER reconcile
~~~

**Fix**

Create the main window first (it can show a loading state), then run the initial reconcile after the window exists вҖ” the same way enrichMedia and backfillTranscriptIndex are already deferred as non-blocking. Reconcile already notifies db-updated, so the renderer refreshes when it completes.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I read src/main/index.ts (whenReady handler) and confirmed the ordering: container.useCases.reconcile.execute(rootPath) is called at line 196 and createMainWindow() is at line 231 вҖ” reconcile runs to completion BEFORE the window is created. ReconcileDirectory.execute (ReconcileDirectory.ts:88-90) wraps executeInternal in this.transaction.run(), a synchronous better-sqlite3 transaction, so the whole scan is synchronous and blocking. executeInternal (line 110) first does bulk DB reads (findAll x3) plus listDirectories(rootPath), then iterates every non-deleted DB creator (line 130) calling reconcileVideos and reconcileCuts. reconcileVideos calls this.fs.listDirectories(downloadsDir) at line 303 and reconcileCuts calls this.fs.listDirectories(cutsDir) at line 435 вҖ” so exactly 2 directory reads per active creator in steady state (the per-video listFiles/readJsonFile only fire for genuinely-new disk entries via upsertVideoFromDisk, not for already-indexed videos). NodeFileSystemReader.listDirectories uses readdirSync (line 28), and the class doc explicitly states 'All operations are synchronous'. So at N creators the main thread blocks on ~2N+1 synchronous readdir syscalls (plus DB work) before the first paint, scaling linearly with creator count. Crucially, the suggested fix pattern already exists in the same file: enrichMedia (line 203) and backfillTranscriptIndex (line 217) are deliberately deferred as async non-blocking promises, and reconcile is described as notifying db-updated, so deferring it after createMainWindow is viable. The finding's code-level claims all check out; only the magnitude ('hundreds of ms to seconds') is conditional on a cold/network disk вҖ” on a local SSD 2N readdir calls is closer to single-digit ms at N=100.

**Verifier notes**

Real and accurately located (index.ts:196 reconcile before :231 createMainWindow; listDirectories sync at ReconcileDirectory.ts:303 and :435; readdirSync at NodeFileSystemReader.ts:28). Sharper repro: with M active creators, steady-state startup blocks the main thread on exactly 2M+1 synchronous readdir syscalls inside a sync SQLite transaction before any window exists; first launch adds listFiles + readJsonFile (meta.json/cut-data.json) per new video/cut. Magnitude caveat: on local SSD this is small (~ms); the 'seconds of black screen' case needs a cold or network-mounted root folder. Fix is low-risk because the exact deferral pattern is already used two blocks below for enrichMedia and backfillTranscriptIndex, and reconcile emits db-updated so the renderer self-refreshes. Severity left at medium given conditional magnitude.

### F16 вҖ” Transcript list renders every segment unvirtualized; long videos mount thousands of DOM nodes

- **Severity:** рҹҹ  MEDIUM
- **Category:** performance
- **Location:** `src/renderer/components/features/videos/TranscriptTab.tsx:254-287`
- **Confidence:** 0.7 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

The transcript renders all segments at once inside a fixed-height ScrollArea with no windowing. A captioned 1-2h video can have thousands of caption segments; each becomes a <li> + <button> + per-segment renderSegmentText() call, and every segment also registers a ref into segmentRefs. This is the exact O(n) mount cost that VirtualAuditList in this same codebase was created to avoid (its doc comment says plain .map() 'dropped scroll performance to a crawl past ~500 entries'). On long videos opening the Transcript tab will jank and search re-highlighting re-runs renderSegmentText across the whole mounted tree.

**Evidence**

~~~text
<ScrollArea className="h-125 rounded border">
  <ul className="divide-border divide-y p-1">
    {segments.map((seg, segIdx) => (
      <li key={`${seg.startMs}-${seg.endMs}`} ref={(node) => { ... }} className="min-w-0">
        <button ...>{renderSegmentText(seg.text, segIdx)}</button>
~~~

**Fix**

Windowing this list with @tanstack/react-virtual (already a dependency, used by VirtualAuditList) вҖ” keying virtual rows by index and using measureElement, while keeping the search scroll-into-target working by scrolling the virtualizer to the matched segmentIndex instead of relying on a fully-mounted ref map.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I read TranscriptTab.tsx in full. Lines 254-287 confirm the claim exactly: a fixed-height `<ScrollArea className="h-125">` wraps a plain `<ul>` whose children are `segments.map((seg, segIdx) => <li ref={...} ><button>{renderSegmentText(seg.text, segIdx)}</button></li>)`. There is no windowing/virtualization. Every segment mounts a `<li>` + `<button>` + two `<span>`s, registers a ref into `segmentRefs` (lines 259-262), and runs `renderSegmentText` (line 281). On every search keystroke, `query`/`matches` change, re-rendering the whole mounted tree and re-invoking `renderSegmentText` for all segments вҖ” though `matchesBySegment.get(segIdx)` is O(1) and unmatched segments early-return the raw string (line 164), so the per-keystroke cost is bounded but still O(n) reconciliation.

The codebase already has the exact remedy: VirtualAuditList.tsx uses `@tanstack/react-virtual` with `measureElement`, and its doc comment (lines 10-17) explicitly states the prior plain `.map()` 'dropped scroll performance to a crawl past ~500 entries' вҖ” establishing both the dependency and the team's own threshold for when this matters. A 1-2h captioned video realistically yields 1,000-3,000 caption segments, well past that threshold.

The search scroll-to-match relies on a fully-mounted `segmentRefs` map (lines 124-125), which is why this wasn't trivially virtualized вҖ” the reviewer's suggested fix (scroll the virtualizer to the matched segmentIndex) correctly addresses that coupling. The finding is real and the suggested fix is sound.

**Verifier notes**

Confirmed and not handled anywhere вҖ” the plainText fallback branch (lines 292-296) is a single `<pre>` and fine; only the segmented branch is unvirtualized. Severity stays medium: the cost is gated behind opening one rarely-hot tab on long captioned videos (short videos, the common case, render fine), and the per-keystroke re-render is bounded by O(1) match lookups + early-return. It's a genuine localized jank issue that the codebase's own established VirtualAuditList pattern already exists to prevent, so the fix is low-risk (same dependency, same approach). Not critical/high: no correctness impact, no crash, no data issue вҖ” purely interaction smoothness on an edge-case content size. Sharper repro: open the Transcript tab on a 90+ min video with auto-captions (~2,000+ segments) and type in the search box; each keystroke reconciles the full mounted list.

---

### F17 вҖ” ffprobe argument injection + arbitrary-file probe via probe-media-file (no -- terminator, no root containment)

- **Severity:** рҹҹ  MEDIUM
- **Category:** security
- **Location:** `src/main/framework-drivers/ffprobe/FfprobeMediaProbe.ts:46-62`
- **Confidence:** 0.72 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

'probe-media-file' is exposed to the renderer (preload index.ts:23, window.api.probeMediaFile) and forwards an arbitrary string straight to ffprobe as a positional argument with no '--' terminator and no path-containment check. A compromised renderer can (a) inject ffprobe options (a leading-'-' value is parsed as an option; ffprobe accepts protocol/input options and can be pointed at arbitrary inputs), and (b) probe any absolute path on disk outside the configured root, leaking file existence and media metadata (container/stream info) via the returned MediaProbeResult. ffprobe has no '--exec' equivalent, so this is information-disclosure / option-abuse rather than RCE, hence MEDIUM. Note the parallel ffmpeg sink (FfmpegRenderBackend) is NOT affected because its sourcePath comes from sourceVideo.filePath (DB) and staging/final paths are server-derived from a generated cutId вҖ” none are renderer free-form.

**Evidence**

~~~text
const args = ['-v','error','-print_format','json','-show_format','-show_streams', filePath]
const proc = spawn(bin, args, { stdio: ['ignore', 'pipe', 'pipe'] })  // filePath is a trailing positional with no '--' separator. The 'probe-media-file' channel schema is z.tuple([z.string().min(1).max(4096)]) (ipc-schemas.ts:92) and ProbeMediaFile.execute only checks non-empty вҖ” no containment under rootPath, no scheme/option guard.
~~~

**Fix**

Prepend '--' before filePath in the ffprobe args array. Additionally, since legitimate callers always probe a file already tracked in the DB under rootPath, resolve the probe target through an entity reference (like ResolveMediaUrl) or realpath-contain it under rootPathRef before spawning вҖ” mirroring the containment already done in ShellController.open-path-in-shell.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I traced the full data flow and it matches the finding. Renderer window.api.probeMediaFile (preload/index.ts:23) -> channel 'probe-media-file' validated only by z.tuple([z.string()]) (ipc-schemas.ts:92 вҖ” note: NO .min/.max and NO containment; the reviewer's quoted ".min(1).max(4096)" is actually open-path-in-shell at line 215, a misquote that makes the real schema WEAKER than claimed) -> DownloadController.ts:35-36 forwards filePath verbatim -> ProbeMediaFile.execute (ProbeMediaFile.ts:17-23) only checks non-empty/trim -> FfprobeMediaProbe.probe (FfprobeMediaProbe.ts:16-39) calls statSync(filePath) and runFfprobe, which builds args = ['-v','error','-print_format','json','-show_format','-show_streams', filePath] (lines 46-60) and spawn(bin, args, {stdio:[...]}) (line 62). Confirmed: (1) no '--' terminator before the trailing positional, so a filePath beginning with '-' is parsed by ffprobe as an option (option-abuse / info-disclosure; ffprobe has no exec primitive, so no RCE вҖ” MEDIUM is the right ceiling); (2) no path containment under rootPath anywhere in the chain, so a compromised renderer can probe any absolute path on disk and learn file existence + container/stream metadata via the returned MediaProbeResult. spawn has no shell:true (object at line 62 sets only stdio), so this is option-injection/arbitrary-input-probe, NOT shell injection. The inconsistency is concrete: the sibling channel open-path-in-shell (ShellController.ts:50-57) realpath-contains its free-form path under rootPath, and the project's own ipc-schemas.ts header explicitly names renderer-XSS via stored YouTube content as the in-scope threat model вҖ” so the missing guard here is a genuine gap, not an out-of-scope concern.

**Verifier notes**

Real and exploitable under the project's stated threat model (renderer compromise via stored YouTube content). Repro from a compromised renderer: window.api.probeMediaFile('C:/Users/<victim>/AppData/.../some-secret.mp4') returns duration/resolution/fileSize, confirming existence + leaking media metadata of files outside rootPath; and window.api.probeMediaFile('-show_entries') (or any leading-'-' value) reaches ffprobe as an option rather than an input because there is no '--' terminator. No renderer caller of probeMediaFile currently exists (only openPathInShell was found in src/renderer), but it is still live on window.api, so the attack surface is present regardless. Two minor reviewer inaccuracies that do not weaken the finding: the schema citation (ipc-schemas.ts:92) is z.tuple([z.string()]) вҖ” the '.min(1).max(4096)' the reviewer quoted is open-path-in-shell at line 215; and the impact is info-disclosure/option-abuse only (correctly noted by the reviewer вҖ” no '--exec' equivalent). Fix as suggested: prepend '--' to the args array AND resolve/realpath-contain the target under rootPath, mirroring ShellController.open-path-in-shell. The ffmpeg sink (FfmpegRenderBackend) was not re-examined in depth but the reviewer's claim that its paths are DB/server-derived is plausible and out of scope for this finding.

---

### F18 вҖ” EditRecipe schema permits container 'mkv', which Chromium <video> rejects вҖ” produces an unplayable cut

- **Severity:** рҹҹ  MEDIUM
- **Category:** spec-violation
- **Location:** `src/shared/types/edit-recipe.ts:93-98`
- **Confidence:** 0.7 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

The codebase's own documented constraint (YtDlpDownloader.ts:428-438 and project memory) is that Chromium's HTML5 <video> rejects DocType=matroska outright with MEDIA_ERR_SRC_NOT_SUPPORTED. Yet the render recipe schema вҖ” the boundary validated at IPC, sidecar read, and DB read вҖ” accepts `mkv`. A recipe with container='mkv' (reachable from a future client or a compromised renderer over the validated IPC channel; the editor UI currently hardcodes 'mp4' in SaveCutDialog.tsx:76) renders a .mkv cut that is silently unplayable in-app. argv-builder.ts never validates container vs the playback constraint.

**Evidence**

~~~text
`output: z.object({ container: z.enum(['mp4', 'webm', 'mkv']), mode: z.enum(['copy', 'reencode']) }).strict()`. RenderCutFromVideo.ts:103-109 builds both finalPath and stagingPath as `${cutId}.${recipe.output.container}`, so container directly chooses the output extension/muxer, and the cut is later played via `<video src="klip-media://cut/...">` (PersistentPlayer/EditorView).
~~~

**Fix**

Drop 'mkv' from the container enum (`z.enum(['mp4', 'webm'])`) so the unplayable container can never enter the pipeline, matching the H.264+mp4/webm-never-mkv rule enforced on the download path. If mkv must stay in the type union for v2 export, gate it behind canRender()/buildFfmpegArgv with an explicit rejection.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I read the cited code and its enforcement path. edit-recipe.ts:95 indeed declares `container: z.enum(['mp4', 'webm', 'mkv'])`. This schema (editRecipeSchema, via renderCutRequestSchema) is the single canonical validator at all three trust boundaries: IPC (ipc-schemas.ts:272 'editor-start-render' вҶ’ renderCutRequestSchema вҶ’ editRecipeSchema), the on-disk sidecar read (ReconcileDirectory.ts:500 editRecipeSchema.safeParse(cutData?.editRecipe)), and the DB JSON column read (dto-mappers.ts:97). None of them strips 'mkv'.

The container value flows straight to the output filename: RenderCutFromVideo.ts:103 `fileName = ${cutId}.${recipe.output.container}` and :109 stagingPath `${cutId}.${recipe.output.container}`. ffmpeg in argv-builder.ts uses extension-driven muxer selection (`-y outputPath`), so a .mkv extension yields ffmpeg's matroska muxer, which writes DocType=matroska (both copy and reencode paths). 

The downstream guards do NOT cover container: FfmpegRenderBackend.canRender (FfmpegRenderBackend.ts:47-56) only checks isMvpSupportedRecipe (single trim op); buildFfmpegArgv (argv-builder.ts:24-29) only validates ops count/type. Neither validates container against the playback constraint.

The codebase's own documented constraint is explicit and corroborated in two places: YtDlpDownloader.ts:428-435 and KlipMediaProtocolHandler.ts:18-30 ("There is no MIME we can serve that makes Chromium accept a matroska-DocType file in <video>"; .mkv deliberately omitted from EXT_TO_MIME). Cuts are played via the klip-media:// protocol served by exactly that handler, so an .mkv cut serves an unrecognized/guessed MIME and a matroska-DocType file вҶ’ MEDIA_ERR_SRC_NOT_SUPPORTED, silently unplayable in-app.

So the schema genuinely permits an unplayable container, and nothing between the validated boundary and the muxer rejects it. The finding is real.

The mitigating context (which bounds severity): the only first-party producer, SaveCutDialog.tsx:76, hardcodes container:'mp4', so no current UI path can emit mkv. Exploitation requires a malicious/compromised renderer over IPC, a hand-edited cut-data.json sidecar, or a future client вҖ” exactly the threat model the multi-boundary Zod validation exists to defend against. The defense is incomplete for this one field.

**Verifier notes**

Refuted-not. Confirmed. Repro: send `editor-start-render` IPC with recipe.output.container='mkv' (or place a cut-data.json sidecar whose editRecipe.output.container='mkv' and let reconcile import it). The schema accepts it; RenderCutFromVideo writes <cutId>.mkv; ffmpeg muxes matroska (DocType=matroska); EditorView/PersistentPlayer load it via klip-media://cut/... and Chromium throws MEDIA_ERR_SRC_NOT_SUPPORTED. Fix as suggested: tighten the enum to z.enum(['mp4','webm']) in edit-recipe.ts:95 (cleanest вҖ” kills it at the boundary), and mirror in recipe-from-timeline.ts:138 / argv-builder.test.ts:12 type unions. If 'mkv' must survive in the type union for a v2 export feature, instead add a container check to FfmpegRenderBackend.canRender and/or buildFfmpegArgv that fails closed for in-app playback targets. Severity medium is fair: high data/UX impact (silently unplayable cut) but not currently reachable from first-party UI (SaveCutDialog hardcodes mp4); it is a real gap in the explicitly-defense-in-depth IPC/sidecar/DB validation layer, consistent with the project's documented never-mkv rule.

---

### F19 вҖ” Auto-created creators use folderName as id, diverging from RegisterCreator's UUID scheme

- **Severity:** рҹҹ  MEDIUM
- **Category:** weird-logic
- **Location:** `src/main/use-cases/DownloadVideo.ts:393-411`
- **Confidence:** 0.8 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

DownloadVideo.ensureCreator sets a new creator's id = folderName (the slug), while RegisterCreator sets id = idGenerator.generate() (UUID). The codebase now has two creator-id conventions living side by side. This is the root cause of the FK-mismatch finding above and is a latent trap for any code that assumes Creator.id is opaque/UUID (e.g. FetchChannelInfo returns creator.id, RefreshCreatorAvatar looks up by id). It also means a creator first seen via download (id=slug) and later 'registered' or reconciled cannot have a stable opaque id. The MEMORY note 'Creator.id is a UUID, separate from Creator.folderName' is contradicted by this write path.

**Evidence**

~~~text
if (!existing) { ... touched = { id: folderName, folderName, name: displayName, ... } ; this.creatorRepo.upsert(touched) }
~~~

**Fix**

Generate a UUID id for auto-created creators too (inject IIdGenerator into ensureCreator), keeping folderName as the disk key. Then write video.creatorId = creator.id consistently. This unifies the two creation paths and fixes the FK break.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I verified all cited code. DownloadVideo.ensureCreator (src/main/use-cases/DownloadVideo.ts:393-411) sets a new creator's `id: folderName` (the slug) at line 396. RegisterCreator.execute (src/main/use-cases/RegisterCreator.ts:67) sets `id: this.idGenerator.generate()` (a UUID), and returns that as creatorId at line 121. So the two creation paths genuinely use different id schemes for the same column. The schema (src/main/framework-drivers/database/schema.ts:55-57) declares videos.creator_id as a FK referencing creators.id with onDelete cascade, confirming creators.id is the join key вҖ” not folderName. The download path papers over this internally: video.creatorId is also written as `folderName` (line 256), so within a pure-download-created creator the FK is satisfied (folderName == id). But the divergence is real and contradicts the project's own documented invariant (the MEMORY note: "Creator.id вү  Creator.folderName; RegisterCreator uses UUID id with separate folderName; use findByFolderName for disk-keyed lookups, never findById"). Consumers that treat creator.id as opaque are affected: FetchChannelInfo (FetchChannelInfo.ts:50) returns `creator?.id`, which is a UUID or a slug depending on which path created the creator; RefreshCreatorAvatar.execute (RefreshCreatorAvatar.ts:25) does findById(creatorId), which only works if the caller's id matches whatever scheme created the row. A creator first auto-created via download (id=slug) can never acquire a stable opaque id. This is exactly the kind of two-convention trap the finding describes, and is the root cause of the related cross-path FK-mismatch (a creator registered via RegisterCreator with id=UUID, later downloaded under a matching slug, gets video.creatorId=folderName which does NOT equal the existing creator's UUID id).

**Verifier notes**

Confirmed at medium. The inconsistency is real and verified, but note the nuance the reviewer slightly understated: within the pure-download path it is self-consistent (both creator.id and video.creatorId equal folderName), so this finding alone does not produce a crash вҖ” it is a latent design-convention violation. Its concrete teeth come from the cross-path interaction (RegisterCreator UUID + later download writing video.creatorId=folderName), which is the separate FK-mismatch finding. Suggested fix is sound: inject IIdGenerator into ensureCreator, set creator.id = generate(), and write video.creatorId = creator.id (the resolved creator's id from findByFolderName in the existing branch, not folderName). That requires ensureCreator to return the Creator so line 256 can use creator.id instead of folderName. Repro for the latent trap: register a channel via RegisterCreator (id=UUID), then download a video from it whose slugified name matches folderName вҖ” findByFolderName hits the UUID creator, but video.creatorId is set to folderName вү  UUID, breaking the FK / orphaning the video from its creator in any id-based join.

---


## рҹҹЎ LOW

### F20 вҖ” Re-encode argv hardcodes libx264+aac regardless of output container (codec/container mismatch for webm)

- **Severity:** рҹҹЎ LOW
- **Category:** bug
- **Location:** `src/main/framework-drivers/ffmpeg/argv-builder.ts:52-69`
- **Confidence:** 0.6 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

If a recipe arrives with container='webm' and mode='reencode', ffmpeg is asked to mux H.264 video + AAC audio into a .webm container; the webm muxer rejects H.264/AAC and ffmpeg fails the render (exit non-zero), surfacing only the generic 'ffmpeg exited with code N' error. Not reachable from today's editor UI (container hardcoded to 'mp4' in SaveCutDialog.tsx:76 and copy mode is the default), so impact is latent, but it is a correctness gap the moment webm re-encode is offered.

**Evidence**

~~~text
In reencode mode the builder always emits `argv.push('-c:v', 'libx264', '-crf', '18', '-preset', 'medium'); argv.push('-c:a', 'aac', '-b:a', '192k')`, then `argv.push('-y', outputPath)`. `outputPath` carries the container extension (`${cutId}.${recipe.output.container}`), but `recipe.output.container` is never consulted when choosing codecs.
~~~

**Fix**

Select codecs from the container: mp4 -> libx264/aac (current), webm -> libvpx-vp9 (or libsvtav1)/libopus. Centralize the container->codec mapping in argv-builder and add a test asserting webm+reencode never emits libx264/aac.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I read argv-builder.ts directly. Lines 52-59 (reencode branch) unconditionally emit `-c:v libx264 -crf 18 -preset medium` and `-c:a aac -b:a 192k`, then line 69 writes `-y outputPath`. recipe.output.container is never consulted when choosing codecs вҖ” confirmed the quoted code is current. The output container schema (src/shared/types/edit-recipe.ts:95) is `z.enum(['mp4','webm','mkv'])` with `mode: z.enum(['copy','reencode'])`, and the schema's only superRefine checks `out > in` вҖ” there is NO cross-field guard preventing webm+reencode. canRender (FfmpegRenderBackend.ts:47-56) only validates ops via isMvpSupportedRecipe (single trim); it does not check container/codec compatibility, so it would NOT block a webm+reencode recipe. Therefore if a recipe with container='webm', mode='reencode' reached the backend, ffmpeg would be told to mux H.264/AAC into .webm; the webm/matroska-webm muxer rejects H.264/AAC and ffmpeg exits non-zero, surfacing only the generic 'ffmpeg exited with code N'. The reviewer is also correct that this is not reachable from today's UI: SaveCutDialog.tsx:76 hardcodes container:'mp4' (only mode is user-selectable via renderMode), so the codec set always matches the container in practice. The bug is real but latent. One refinement: mkv (also allowed by the enum) actually accepts H.264/AAC, so the true mismatch is webm specifically вҖ” the finding's framing is correct.

**Verifier notes**

Real but latent correctness gap. Confirmed unreachable today: container is hardcoded to 'mp4' in src/renderer/components/features/editor/SaveCutDialog.tsx:76 (only renderMode is user-tweakable). The schema (edit-recipe.ts:95) admits webm/mkv + reencode with no cross-field guard, and neither canRender nor argv-builder rejects an incompatible container/codec combo. Sharper repro: construct an EditRecipe with output={container:'webm', mode:'reencode'} and a single trim, call editorStartRender вҖ” ffmpeg fails with a non-descriptive exit code. mkv would NOT fail (it accepts H.264/AAC), so the mismatch is webm-specific. Suggested fix (container->codec map in argv-builder, e.g. webm->libvpx-vp9/libopus, plus a unit test) is appropriate; alternatively add a superRefine/canRender guard rejecting webm+H264. Severity low is justified given it is currently unreachable from the UI.

### F21 вҖ” FetchVideoDetail and EnrichMediaMetadata both full-row-upsert the same video, causing lost-update race

- **Severity:** рҹҹЎ LOW _(verifier corrected from medium)_
- **Category:** bug
- **Location:** `src/main/use-cases/EnrichAllVideos.ts:57-69`
- **Confidence:** 0.6 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

EnrichAllVideos funnels FetchVideoDetail through a dedicated async queue, and ProcessFileNotifications.runFlush concurrently fires EnrichMediaMetadata (ffprobe) without awaiting it. Both use cases do read-row, await, full-row upsert on the videos table. When they target the same newly-discovered video (the common case right after a download), the later upsert overwrites the earlier one's columns: ffprobe's duration/resolution/fileSize can erase FetchVideoDetail's viewCount/likeCount/transcriptText/detailFetchedAt, or vice-versa. No row-level optimistic-concurrency guard (no updatedAt CAS) prevents this.

**Evidence**

~~~text
await this.queue.enqueue(() => this.fetchDetail.execute(video.id))  // FetchVideoDetail: read row then this.videoRepo.upsert({...}) of full row
~~~

**Fix**

Make both writers column-scoped UPDATEs (probe columns vs. detail columns are disjoint, so scoped updates would compose cleanly), or serialize enrichment+detail per video, or add an updatedAt compare-and-set. The full-row upsert-on-read pattern is the root cause shared by both.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

The mechanical claim is correct. SqliteVideoRepository.upsert (lines 189-251) writes the FULL row via INSERT ... ON CONFLICT DO UPDATE, setting every column from excluded (the passed-in object). Both writers follow read -> await -> full-row upsert:

- FetchVideoDetail.execute (FetchVideoDetail.ts:95 findById, :105/:129 awaits, :162 upsert {...video, detail cols, detailFetchedAt, updatedAt}).
- EnrichMediaMetadata.execute (EnrichMediaMetadata.ts:25 findByProbeStatus('pending'), :32 awaits ffprobe, :33 upsert {...video, duration/resolution/fileSize, probeStatus, updatedAt}).

better-sqlite3 is synchronous, so each upsert().run() is atomic, but the read is separated from the write by an await. With two concurrent flows both reading the same video snapshot before either writes, the later upsert overwrites ALL columns from its own stale snapshot, clobbering the other's just-written intended columns even though the two intended-column sets are disjoint. There is no updatedAt CAS and no transaction spanning read+write. So a genuine lost-update is possible.

Concurrency is reachable: a newly-discovered video has detailFetchedAt=NULL (qualifies for findNeedingDetail, FetchVideoDetail.ts via EnrichAllVideos) AND probeStatus='pending' (qualifies for findByProbeStatus, EnrichMediaMetadata fired from ProcessFileNotifications.runFlush:142-151 without awaiting the flush). EnrichAllVideos's queue only serializes FetchVideoDetail calls among themselves, not against EnrichMediaMetadata.

However the reviewer's premise that this is "the common case right after a download" is wrong. enrichAllVideos has no auto-trigger; the only call site is the manual Settings button EnrichVideosButton.tsx (verified via grep of all renderer call sites). EnrichMediaMetadata auto-fires from file-watch reconciliation. So the race requires the user to manually click "Enrich all videos" while a file-watch reconcile is concurrently probing the same just-discovered video вҖ” a narrow, user-action-gated window. It also tends to self-heal: a lost FetchVideoDetail write reverts detailFetchedAt to NULL (re-fetched next pass) and a lost probe write can revert probeStatus to pending (re-probed next pass).

**Verifier notes**

Root cause confirmed: full-row upsert-on-read shared by both use cases (SqliteVideoRepository.upsert:189-251 writes every column from the snapshot). Suggested fix is sound вҖ” column-scoped UPDATEs would compose since the intended column sets are disjoint (probe: duration/resolution/fileSize/probeStatus; detail: viewCount/likeCount/dislikeCount/commentCount/category/tags/uploadDate/description/isShort/transcript*/detailFetchedAt). Downgraded from medium to low: trigger is NOT post-download (enrichAllVideos is a manual Settings button only вҖ” EnrichVideosButton.tsx; not auto-fired), so the window is narrow and user-gated, and both pending-flag mechanisms (detailFetchedAt NULL, probeStatus pending) cause clobbered rows to be re-enriched on a subsequent pass, limiting durable data loss. Sharper repro: download a new video, then while file-watch reconciliation is probing it (EnrichMediaMetadata via runFlush) click "Enrich all videos" in Settings; whichever of ffprobe/network resolves second overwrites the first's columns from its stale snapshot.

---

### F22 вҖ” MoveVideosToCreator is non-atomic: physical folder move and DB row update are not transactional per video, so a crash between them orphans the file from its DB row

- **Severity:** рҹҹЎ LOW _(verifier corrected from medium)_
- **Category:** bug
- **Location:** `src/main/use-cases/MoveVideosToCreator.ts:57-84`
- **Confidence:** 0.6 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

Each video: the folder is moved on disk first, then the DB row is rewritten. Unlike MigrateRootFolder/RenderCutFromVideo, there is no Operation record and no transaction wrapping the move+update, so if the process crashes after moveDirectory but before upsertWithPrevious, the file sits at the new creator's folder while the DB still says the old creatorId/filePath. There is no recovery sweep for this op type. Reconcile would eventually re-discover the file under the target folder and may create a phantom/duplicate row. Lower severity than the migrate bug because it is per-video and self-heals partially via reconcile, but it is a genuine non-atomic multi-write data-consistency gap.

**Evidence**

~~~text
if (this.fsReader.directoryExists(oldDir)) {
  this.fsWriter.moveDirectory(oldDir, newDir)
}
...
this.videoRepo.upsertWithPrevious(updated, video)
moved++
~~~

**Fix**

Wrap the move in the operations/transaction pattern already used elsewhere (persist an Operation with the move plan, do the rename, then the DB update inside transaction.run), or at minimum order DB-first only if the move is reversible. Given reconcile exists, recording an Operation row so a crash is recoverable is the consistent fix.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I read MoveVideosToCreator.ts in full. The reviewer's quote is accurate: per video the code (1) ensureDirectory(targetDownloads), (2) moveDirectory(oldDir, newDir) on disk, then (3) videoRepo.upsertWithPrevious(updated, video) to rewrite the DB row вҖ” with NO Operation record and no transaction spanning the FS move and the DB write. This contrasts with the established saga pattern: Operation.ts defines a saga log; RecoverOperations.ts handles 'migrate_root' (replays/reverses moves) and 'render_cut' (cleans staging/orphan rows) at startup. There is no 'move_creator' op type in OperationType, so RecoverOperations has no branch for it and a crash between step 2 and step 3 is unrecoverable by the saga. So the architectural inconsistency and the crash window are real and verified.

However the reviewer's stated consequence is partly wrong. I traced ReconcileDirectory.ts: after a crash, the file sits under the target creator's downloads while the DB row still has the old creatorId/filePath. Next reconcile marks the row 'missing' under the old creator (reconcileVideos), and the target creator's reconcileVideos sees the diskVideoId as 'new' (it's grouped by old creatorId) and calls upsertVideoFromDisk(...previous=null...). But that upsert keys on the video PRIMARY KEY (id = videoId) вҖ” AuditedVideoRepository.upsert delegates to inner.upsert (INSERT OR REPLACE semantics). So it OVERWRITES the existing row, setting creatorId=target and the corrected filePath. There is NO phantom/duplicate row. discoverVideos even has an explicit findById guard. So reconcile actually self-heals the linkage to the user's intended target. The real residual harm is milder: the overwritten row loses user metadata (tags reset to [], title falls back to meta.json, probeStatus reset to 'pending'), and the audit log records 'created' instead of 'updated'.

**Verifier notes**

Confirmed non-atomic multi-write gap, but reviewer overstates the impact. No orphaned files and NO duplicate/phantom rows вҖ” the id-keyed upsert in ReconcileDirectory.upsertVideoFromDisk overwrites the same primary key (videoId), self-healing the creator linkage to the user's intended target. Actual crash consequence is loss of user-set metadata on that one row (tags->[], title->meta.json fallback, probeStatus->pending) plus a misleading 'created' audit entry вҖ” a per-video, narrow-window, self-correcting inconsistency, hence low not medium. Sharper repro: crash (power loss / kill) in the loop in MoveVideosToCreator.ts after line 65 moveDirectory but before line 79 upsertWithPrevious, for a video that had user-applied tags. Suggested fix is sound in spirit (add a 'move_creator' OperationType + RecoverOperations branch, or do DB-first then move). If the user wants strict parity with the saga pattern used by migrate/render, the fix is justified; if relying on reconcile self-heal, document the metadata-loss-on-crash tradeoff.

---

### F23 вҖ” discoverVideos recovers a same-id video under a new creator without re-pointing creatorId/filePath

- **Severity:** рҹҹЎ LOW
- **Category:** bug
- **Location:** `src/main/use-cases/ReconcileDirectory.ts:328-346`
- **Confidence:** 0.55 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

The guard explicitly anticipates 'the same yt-dlp video ID was downloaded under a different creator folder previously' (comment at 333-335). But when such a row exists it only flips status to active and continues; it never updates creatorId, filePath or thumbnailPath to the folder currently on disk. The DB then claims the video belongs to creator A while the bytes live under creator B's folder, so the player loads a stale/wrong filePath. reconcileVideos (line 308) has the same shape: a video present on disk only has its status touched, never its filePath, so a file moved/renamed within the same id dir is not re-pointed.

**Evidence**

~~~text
const existing = this.videoRepo.findById(videoId)
      if (existing) {
        if (existing.status === 'missing') {
          this.videoRepo.updateStatus(videoId, 'active', null)
          result.videosRecovered++
        }
        continue
      }
~~~

**Fix**

When recovering an existing video found under a different creator folder (or whose on-disk media file path differs), re-derive filePath/thumbnailPath/creatorId from the current location via upsertVideoFromDisk with the previous row, instead of only flipping status.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I read ReconcileDirectory.ts:328-346 and confirmed the quoted code is current and exact: discoverVideos finds an existing row by global id, and if it's missing only flips status to 'active' (videoRepo.updateStatus) and `continue`s вҖ” it never re-derives creatorId/filePath/thumbnailPath from the folder now on disk. reconcileVideos (296-326) has the identical shape at 308-313: when diskVideoIds.has(video.id), only status is touched. schema.ts:54 confirms videos.id is the global primaryKey, so a single yt-dlp id can only ever map to ONE DB row even if its bytes appear under two different creator folders on disk вҖ” which is what makes the dedup guard's existence justified, but also what makes the stale-pointer possible. ResolveMediaUrl.ts:11-19 returns video.filePath verbatim with NO existence check or re-derivation, so a stale filePath does cause the player to load a vanished/wrong path (the generic codec/onerror failure the codebase repeatedly references). Concrete repro: user manually relocates <root>/A/downloads/<id>/ to <root>/B/downloads/<id>/ outside the app. In a full sweep, step 2 reconciles creator A and marks the <id> video 'missing' (its dir is gone from A); step 3 discovers new creator B, discoverVideos sees <id> as 'missing', flips it back to 'active', and continues вҖ” leaving creatorId=A and filePath pointing at A's vanished folder. Net: the row is 'active' but mislinked and unplayable. The reviewer's suggested fix (call upsertVideoFromDisk with the previous row instead of a bare status flip) is exactly right and matches how upsertVideoFromDisk already re-derives all paths from the current location.

**Verifier notes**

Real but narrow-trigger. The supported in-app way to move a video across creators is MoveVideosToCreator.ts, which atomically moves the directory AND rewrites creatorId/filePath/thumbnailPath/transcriptPath (lines 71-79) вҖ” so normal app usage stays consistent. The bug only manifests when the user relocates a download folder across creator dirs on disk OUTSIDE the app, then reconciles. If the bytes still exist under BOTH A and B, it is harmless dedup (A's pointer remains valid; B's copy is simply not catalogued, which is correct given the global PK). The claim's secondary leg (reconcileVideos doesn't re-point a media file renamed within the same id dir, e.g. a re-download landing a different extension) is also accurate but even narrower. Low severity is appropriate вҖ” arguably even info-level given it requires out-of-app filesystem manipulation. Sharper fix: in both discoverVideos (336-343) and reconcileVideos (308-313), when the row exists/needs recovery, call upsertVideoFromDisk(rootPath, creator, videoId, existing, result) so filePath/thumbnailPath/creatorId are re-derived from the folder currently on disk rather than only flipping status.

---

### F24 вҖ” migrate_root recovery marks op terminally rolled_back even when folders are stranded, with no automatic retry

- **Severity:** рҹҹЎ LOW _(verifier corrected from medium)_
- **Category:** bug
- **Location:** `src/main/use-cases/RecoverOperations.ts:190-231`
- **Confidence:** 0.66 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

When a folder fails to move back during migrate_root rollback, it is pushed to `stranded` and its move.status stays 'moved', but the op is STILL marked 'rolled_back' (a terminal status) at the end. RecoverOperations.execute() only re-picks status 'pending'/'in_progress' (lines 87-89), so a terminal rolled_back op is never revisited. The persisted payload sets partial:true and keeps the un-rolled-back move, but nothing ever reads it again. Result: a second crash (or a transient EBUSY/locked-folder on Windows) during root migration rollback permanently strands folders at the new root with the DB pointing at the old root, and recovery will never retry; only the log line records it.

**Evidence**

~~~text
stranded.push(move.folder) ... // move.status stays 'moved'
    ...
    const errorMsg = stranded.length === 0 ? ... : `...stranded at new root: ${stranded.join(', ')}`
    this.markRolledBack(op.id, errorMsg)
    return false
~~~

**Fix**

When stranded.length > 0, leave the operation in a non-terminal status (e.g. keep 'in_progress' or introduce a 'needs_retry' state that execute() also scans) so the next launch re-attempts the remaining moves, rather than marking it rolled_back. The per-folder status persistence is already in place to support a resumable retry.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I read RecoverOperations.ts (190-231), MigrateRootFolder.ts, Operation.ts, the tests, and grepped every findByStatus/partial consumer. The mechanics in the finding are accurate:

1. RecoverOperations.execute() (lines 87-89) only scans status 'pending' and 'in_progress'. OperationStatus = 'pending'|'in_progress'|'completed'|'failed'|'rolled_back' (Operation.ts:2), so 'rolled_back' is terminal and never re-scanned.

2. In recoverMigrateRootOp, when fsWriter.moveDirectory throws (lines 204-210) the folder is pushed to `stranded` but move.status is NOT flipped вҖ” it stays 'moved'. The catch is per-folder, so the loop continues and reaches the end.

3. Lines 212-222 persist the v2 payload with the stranded move still at status:'moved' and partial:true вҖ” the resumable per-folder state IS written.

4. Line 229 then calls markRolledBack -> updateStatus(id,'rolled_back') unconditionally, even when stranded.length > 0.

I confirmed there is no other reader of this state: findByStatus is only invoked with 'pending'/'in_progress' (RecoverOperations) and via the read-only IPC OperationController.get-operations-by-status (renderer history view, no retry). Nothing consumes payload.partial. The test 'skips rolled-back entries in v2 payload' (line 343) proves the resumable design only works while the op is still 'in_progress' (i.e. a crash before markRolledBack); once it's terminally 'rolled_back', the leftovers are unreachable. So a transient per-folder error (EBUSY / locked folder on Windows) during recovery strands folders at newRoot with the DB at oldRoot and no automatic retry вҖ” exactly as claimed.

One overstatement in the claim: it isn't 'only the log line' вҖ” the op's error column also records the stranded folder names (line 228, asserted in the test at line 318). And no user data is destroyed; folders still exist at newRoot. It's a recoverable FS/DB divergence needing manual cleanup.

**Verifier notes**

Real bug, but I'd downgrade medium -> low. The trigger is a failure-of-a-failure: it only fires during a migrate_root rollback (itself an error path) AND when a per-folder move-back throws non-fatally, leaving a stranded folder. No data loss (folders remain at newRoot); the worst case is a DB/FS divergence that is recorded in both the op error column and the log, but with no in-app remediation, requiring manual cleanup. The same dead-end exists for the inline rollback in MigrateRootFolder.ts: its comment (line 246) claims 'payload.partial is set so RecoverOperations can pick up the leftovers', but rollbackMovedFolders marks the op 'failed' (line 291), and execute() doesn't scan 'failed' either вҖ” so neither the inline nor the recovery partial state is ever picked up. The reviewer's suggested fix is sound: when stranded.length>0, leave the op in a status execute() scans (or add a 'needs_retry' state and scan it), since the per-folder resumable payload is already written. If implementing, also fix the inline 'failed' path / update the misleading comment for consistency.

---

### F25 вҖ” AddToCollectionDialog leaks stale search query across opens (no reset on dismiss)

- **Severity:** рҹҹЎ LOW
- **Category:** bug
- **Location:** `src/renderer/components/features/collections/AddToCollectionDialog.tsx:44-59,103-110`
- **Confidence:** 0.8 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

query is only cleared inside close(), which is called on the success paths (handleAdd / handleCreate) but not when the dialog is dismissed via Escape, overlay click, or the X вҖ” those go straight through onOpenChange={onOpenChange}. So if the user types a filter, then closes without selecting, the next time the dialog opens (for a possibly different entity) it reopens pre-filled with the old query, hiding most collections until they clear it. CommandPalette in the same feature area explicitly resets its query on close to avoid this; this dialog does not.

**Evidence**

~~~text
const [query, setQuery] = useState('')
...
const close = (): void => { setQuery(''); onOpenChange(false) }
...
<CommandDialog open={open} onOpenChange={onOpenChange} ...>
~~~

**Fix**

Wrap onOpenChange so a close clears the query: onOpenChange={(next) => { if (!next) setQuery(''); onOpenChange(next) }} (or reuse close()). Optionally also reset when `entity` changes.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

Verified against the actual file. query is component-internal useState (line 44). setQuery('') only runs inside close() (lines 56-59), which is invoked solely from the onSuccess handlers of handleAdd (line 69) and handleCreate (line 88). The CommandDialog's onOpenChange is wired straight to the parent prop (line 105), so Escape/overlay/X dismissals never touch close() and never clear the query. The component is permanently mounted at both call sites (cuts.tsx:273-279 and creators/$creatorId.tsx) вҖ” the parent only flips the `open` boolean via `open={addTarget !== null}` and clears addTarget on close; React does NOT unmount the dialog, so its useState survives across opens. Therefore a typed-but-not-selected filter persists into the next open, and cmdk filters the collection list against that stale query, hiding non-matching collections. The reviewer's comparison is accurate: CommandPalette.tsx:52-60 has an explicit effect that resets its query on close ('Reset the input when the palette closes so reopening starts fresh'), which this dialog lacks.

**Verifier notes**

Repro: open AddToCollectionDialog on entity A, type a non-matching filter, dismiss with Escape (or overlay/X), then reopen (for any entity) -> CommandInput is pre-filled with the old query and the existing-collections list is filtered down/empty until cleared. Suggested fix is sound; wrapping onOpenChange to clear on close, e.g. onOpenChange={(next) => { if (!next) setQuery(''); onOpenChange(next) }}, mirrors CommandPalette. Note CommandPalette defers the reset by 150ms to avoid a flicker during the close animation; matching that here would be slightly nicer but not required. Severity stays low: cosmetic/UX only, self-correcting, no data integrity impact.

---

### F26 вҖ” Editor scrub/mark shortcuts (i, o, comma, period, arrows) stay active behind the open Save dialog

- **Severity:** рҹҹЎ LOW
- **Category:** bug
- **Location:** `src/renderer/components/features/editor/EditorView.tsx:152-167`
- **Confidence:** 0.7 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

Only 'escape' is gated on !saveOpen. The i/o/comma/period/arrow shortcuts remain enabled while the Save dialog is open. useShortcut suppresses single-key shortcuts only when focus is in a text input. The dialog contains non-text focus targets (PrecisionToggle radio group, Cancel/Save buttons, TagInput chips). If focus lands there, pressing i/o re-marks in/out, and arrow/comma/period scrub the playhead of the timeline hidden behind the modal вҖ” mutating editor state the user can't see while saving.

**Evidence**

~~~text
useShortcut('i', handleMarkIn)
useShortcut('o', handleMarkOut)
useShortcut(',', handleFrameStepBack)
useShortcut('.', handleFrameStepForward)
useShortcut('arrowleft', handleArrowLeft)
useShortcut('arrowright', handleArrowRight)
...
useShortcut('escape', () => { window.close() }, { enabled: !saveOpen })
~~~

**Fix**

Pass `{ enabled: !saveOpen }` to the i/o/comma/period/arrow shortcuts too, or gate them all behind a single editorShortcutsEnabled = !saveOpen.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I verified all cited code. In EditorView.tsx:152-167 only the 'escape' shortcut is gated with `{ enabled: !saveOpen }`; the i/o/comma/period/arrowleft/arrowright shortcuts have no enabled gate and stay bound to a window keydown listener while the Save dialog is open.

In use-shortcut.ts (lines 119-153), single-key shortcuts are suppressed ONLY when `isTextInputActive()` is true. dom-helpers.ts:7-14 defines that as `document.activeElement.tagName` being INPUT/TEXTAREA/SELECT or contentEditable. The Radix Dialog modal traps Tab focus inside itself but does not stop keydown from reaching the window listener.

SaveCutDialog.tsx contains non-text focus targets: PrecisionToggle's `RadioGroupItem`s render as `<button role=radio>`, and the Cancel/Save `Button`s вҖ” none of which satisfy isTextInputActive(). The title Input gets `autoFocus` (line 109), so on open focus is in a text input and shortcuts are correctly suppressed; the bug only manifests after the user tabs/clicks to a button or radio item. Once focus is there, pressing i/o calls handleMarkIn/handleMarkOut (EditorView.tsx:84-94 вҶ’ setInPoint/setOutPoint), and arrows/comma/period call seekRelative (lines 111-119) which writes `<video>.currentTime` and setCursor вҖ” all mutating editor store state behind the modal.

Impact is more than cosmetic: handleSubmit reads `recipeFromTimeline(timeline, ...)` from the live store at submit time, so re-marking in/out via i/o while the dialog is open silently changes the region that actually gets rendered. The reviewer's evidence quotes match the file verbatim; the bug is real.

**Verifier notes**

Repro: open editor, mark a region, press Mod+Enter to open Save dialog, then Tab once (or click Cancel/Save/a precision radio) so focus leaves the title Input, then press i or o вҖ” the in/out region is silently re-marked from the current playhead, or press arrow/comma/period to scrub. Because handleSubmit projects the recipe from the live timeline at click time, an accidental i/o here changes the rendered output, not just the hidden cursor. Trigger is narrow (dialog autoFocuses the title input, so it only fires after focus moves to a non-text element), which keeps it at low severity. Suggested fix is correct: gate all editor shortcuts behind a single `editorShortcutsEnabled = !saveOpen` (also fold in the existing overlay/inFlight state if scrubbing during render should be blocked too).

### F27 вҖ” Save dialog has no form/Enter submit; autofocused title input ignores Enter

- **Severity:** рҹҹЎ LOW
- **Category:** bug
- **Location:** `src/renderer/components/features/editor/SaveCutDialog.tsx:93-145`
- **Confidence:** 0.75 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** yes

**Impact**

The dialog body is plain divs, not a <form>, and the title Input has no onKeyDown/submit binding. The title field is autoFocused, so the natural action (type a title, press Enter) does nothing вҖ” the user must mouse to the Save button. Mod+Enter fires via the editor-level shortcut, but plain Enter вҖ” the expected affordance in a single-field dialog вҖ” does not.

**Evidence**

~~~text
<Input id="cut-title" value={title} onChange={...} autoFocus maxLength={200} /> ... <Button onClick={handleSubmit} disabled={!canSubmit}>
~~~

**Fix**

Wrap the fields in <form onSubmit={(e) => { e.preventDefault(); handleSubmit() }}> with Save as type=submit, or add onKeyDown on the title Input to call handleSubmit when canSubmit and key === 'Enter'.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I read SaveCutDialog.tsx in full. The dialog body (lines 101-133) is a plain `<div className="flex flex-col gap-4">`, not a `<form>`. The title field (lines 104-111) is `<Input id="cut-title" ... autoFocus maxLength={200} />` with only `onChange` вҖ” no `onKeyDown`, no submit binding. The Save action (line 139) is `<Button onClick={handleSubmit} disabled={!canSubmit}>`, a plain button, not `type="submit"`, and there is no surrounding form for it to submit anyway. So pressing Enter in the autofocused title input does nothing вҖ” there is no native form-submit-on-Enter and no manual key handler. The user must mouse/tab to the Save button. Confirmed.

Two corrections to the reviewer's framing: (1) The reviewer says "Mod+Enter fires via the editor-level shortcut" as if it submits. It does NOT submit. In EditorView.tsx line 158-160 `useShortcut('mod+enter', () => { if (saveable) handleSave() })` and handleSave (line 96-97) only does `setSaveOpen(true)` вҖ” it OPENS the dialog. There is no Enter-based submit path anywhere, so the affordance gap is actually slightly worse than described: neither plain Enter nor Mod+Enter submits an open dialog. (2) The TagInput's own onKeyDown (TagInput.tsx line 84-95) intercepts Enter only while focus is in the tag field (and only to commit a tag), so it does not provide a dialog-submit path either.

The bug is genuine but purely a keyboard-affordance/UX gap: a single primary text field is autofocused yet its natural Enter action is dead. No crash, no data loss, mouse path works fine.

**Verifier notes**

Sharper repro: open editor with a saveable timeline, press Mod+Enter (or click Save in the toolbar) to open SaveCutDialog. The title Input is autofocused (autoFocus on line 109). Type a title, press Enter -> nothing happens (no form, no onKeyDown). You must Tab/click to the Save button. Note Mod+Enter is bound in EditorView only to OPEN the dialog, not submit it, so there is no Enter-based submit at all (the reviewer slightly overstated Mod+Enter as a working submit path). Suggested fix is correct: wrap fields in `<form onSubmit>` with Save as type=submit, or add onKeyDown on the title Input calling handleSubmit when canSubmit && key==='Enter'. Care needed so the TagInput field's Enter (commit tag) is not hijacked вҖ” a form-level onSubmit naturally avoids that since TagInput already calls preventDefault on its Enter.

### F28 вҖ” Soft delete/restore of video/cut/creator does not invalidate stats, collections, search, or tags

- **Severity:** рҹҹЎ LOW _(verifier corrected from medium)_
- **Category:** bug
- **Location:** `src/renderer/hooks/use-videos.ts:38-52`
- **Confidence:** 0.85 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

useDeleteVideo/useRestoreVideo (use-videos.ts:38-52), useDeleteCut/useRestoreCut (use-cuts.ts:37-51) and useDeleteCreator/useRestoreCreator (use-creators.ts:35-49) each invalidate only their own entity tree. The corresponding main handlers call repo.updateStatus directly with NO db-updated push (VideoController.ts:46-52, CutController.ts:29-35, CreatorController.ts:32-38 вҖ” none call notifier.notify). So the cross-cutting trees that the db-listener WOULD have refreshed (it explicitly invalidates collections.all on a videos/cuts scope 'because collection item DTOs embed video/cut DTOs вҖҰ so tombstones re-render with current status', plus stats.all, search.all, tags.all вҖ” use-db-listener.ts:46-71) never fire. Concrete impact: delete a video that is in a collection вҶ’ the collection's item list keeps showing it as active (no tombstone) until reload; the dashboard's library/storage stats and the command-palette search results stay stale; deleting a creator doesn't refresh stats. CollectionController items carry per-item status, confirming the stale-tombstone path is real.

**Evidence**

~~~text
export function useDeleteVideo(): UseMutationResult<void, Error, string> {
  const qc = useQueryClient()
  return useMutation({
    mutationFn: (id: string) => window.api.deleteVideo(id),
    onSuccess: () => qc.invalidateQueries({ queryKey: queryKeys.videos.all })
  })
}
~~~

**Fix**

Make these soft-delete/restore handlers emit notifier.notify('db-updated', { scope: ['videos'|'cuts'|'creators'] }) (matching how MoveVideosToCreator/RenderCutFromVideo already do), or broaden the renderer onSuccess to also invalidate stats.all, collections.all, search.all (and tags.all for videos/cuts). The push route is preferable for consistency and to also cover any other open window.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I read all cited files and confirmed every link in the chain.

1. Renderer hooks (use-videos.ts:38-52, use-cuts.ts:37-51, use-creators.ts:35-49): useDelete*/useRestore* each invalidate ONLY their own entity tree (queryKeys.{videos|cuts|creators}.all) in onSuccess. Verbatim match to the quoted evidence.

2. Main controllers (VideoController.ts:46-52, CutController.ts:29-35, CreatorController.ts:32-38): the soft-delete/restore handlers call repo.updateStatus(...) directly and do NOT inject or call a notifier вҖ” these controllers don't even receive an INotifier. Confirmed no db-updated push.

3. The push pattern is the established convention: ~20 mutating use cases fire notifier.notify('db-updated', { scope }) (MoveVideosToCreator ['videos','creators'], RenderCutFromVideo ['cuts'], MarkVideoMissing/Active ['videos'], RefreshCreatorAvatar ['creators'], all collection ops, etc.). The soft-delete/restore handlers are the exception because they bypass the use-case layer entirely.

4. use-db-listener.ts:46-71 explicitly documents the cross-cutting invalidations that WOULD fire on a videos/cuts scope: tags.all (46-48), search.all (52-54), collections.all (57-59 вҖ” "Collection item DTOs embed video/cut DTOs вҖҰ so tombstones re-render with current status"), stats.all (62-64). For a creators scope: search.all + stats.all. None of these fire on delete/restore because no push is emitted.

5. CollectionDto.ts confirms CollectionItemDto.entity is the full VideoDto|CutDto, and VideoDto/CutDto carry status: EntityStatus. So a soft-deleted video inside a collection keeps rendering with status:'active' (no tombstone) until invalidation. The stale-tombstone repro is real.

Net: the only path that refreshes collections/stats/search/tags after a delete/restore is the renderer onSuccess (entity tree only) вҖ” the push route is silent. The cross-cutting trees stay stale until a manual reload or any unrelated subsequent db-updated push. The finding accurately describes code and impact.

**Verifier notes**

Confirmed real and not handled anywhere. Sharpest repro: have a video that belongs to a manual collection, open the collection view in one pane and the dashboard/command-palette in another, soft-delete the video from the library; the videos list updates (videos.all invalidated) but the collection item keeps rendering active (no tombstone), and dashboard library/storage stats + palette search results stay stale until a reload or any later db-updated push. Same for restore, for cuts (collections/stats/search/tags) and for creators (stats/search).

Downgrading mediumвҶ’low because: (a) it is purely transient UI staleness, no data corruption вҖ” updateStatus persists correctly; (b) self-heals on next navigation/reload or any subsequent push; (c) the actively-deleted entity's own list DOES refresh, so the user gets immediate feedback on the primary surface. It is still a genuine consistency gap worth fixing.

Preferred fix matches the codebase convention: route delete/restore through use cases (or have the controllers emit notifier.notify('db-updated', { scope: ['videos'|'cuts'|'creators'] })) rather than broadening the renderer onSuccess вҖ” the push also covers other open windows and is consistent with MoveVideosToCreator/RenderCutFromVideo/MarkVideo*. Note these handlers currently bypass the use-case layer, so they also skip any audit-log append the use cases would do (out of scope for this finding but related).

---

### F29 вҖ” Breadcrumb renders raw UUIDs for detail routes (no ROUTE_KEYS entry)

- **Severity:** рҹҹЎ LOW
- **Category:** bug
- **Location:** `src/renderer/src/routes/__root.tsx:158-195`
- **Confidence:** 0.78 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

ROUTE_KEYS is keyed by exact pathname and only contains top-level routes. For detail routes the matched pathname is e.g. '/videos/3f9a2c8e-...', '/creators/<uuid>', or '/collections/<uuid>'. None match a ROUTE_KEYS entry, so the fallback `m.pathname.split('/').pop()` puts the bare entity UUID into the breadcrumb. The user sees a long opaque UUID as the current-page crumb instead of the entity name or a localized label.

**Evidence**

~~~text
const ROUTE_KEYS: Record<...> = { '/': 'library', '/dashboard': ..., '/collections': 'collections', ... }
...
const key = ROUTE_KEYS[m.pathname]
const label = key ? t(key) : m.pathname.split('/').pop() || ''
~~~

**Fix**

Special-case the detail segments: detect '/videos/$', '/creators/$', '/collections/$' and render a localized parent label (e.g. t('navigation:library')) plus the entity's display name from the loaded query, or hide the dynamic segment crumb entirely.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

The cited code at src/renderer/src/routes/__root.tsx:158-195 matches the quote exactly. ROUTE_KEYS is keyed by literal top-level pathnames ('/', '/dashboard', '/collections', etc.) and contains no entry for the dynamic detail routes. The detail routes exist as real file routes: videos.$videoId.tsx ('/videos/$videoId'), creators/$creatorId.tsx ('/creators/$creatorId'), collections/$collectionId.tsx ('/collections/$collectionId'). In TanStack Router, a match's `m.pathname` is the actual interpolated URL, not the route id, so when a user opens one of these, the iterated match has e.g. m.pathname = '/creators/<uuid>'. ROUTE_KEYS[m.pathname] is undefined, so the fallback `m.pathname.split('/').pop()` runs and the bare entity id becomes the crumb label, rendered via <BreadcrumbPage>{segment.label}</BreadcrumbPage> (line 210). The ids are genuinely opaque: navigation passes creatorId/collectionId = c.id (Creator.id is a UUID per the project's own findByFolderName note), and videoId = v.id / cut.videoId. Even the YouTube-style ids (yt-dlp json.id, ~11 chars) read as meaningless to users. No special-casing, no i18n label, and no entity-name lookup exists in AppBreadcrumb to rescue the dynamic segment. So the breadcrumb's current-page crumb shows a raw id, exactly as claimed. (Note: for /collections/<uuid> the parent '/collections' layout match still resolves to the localized 'collections' crumb, but the trailing UUID crumb still appears; for /videos and /creators there is no parent layout file, so the UUID stands alone.)

**Verifier notes**

Confirmed cosmetic/UX bug, correctly scoped as low. Repro: navigate to any video/creator/collection detail page (e.g. click a creator card on the library route -> navigate to /creators/$creatorId with creatorId = UUID). The header breadcrumb's final crumb renders the raw UUID instead of the entity name or a localized label. The suggested fix is reasonable; the cleanest option is to detect the dynamic leaf (match.routeId ending in $videoId/$creatorId/$collectionId) and substitute the loaded entity's display name from the route's query cache, falling back to a localized parent label, rather than printing pathname.split('/').pop().

### F30 вҖ” Global Escape/Backspace 'back' shortcut fires while a dialog is open, closing the dialog AND navigating away

- **Severity:** рҹҹЎ LOW _(verifier corrected from medium)_
- **Category:** bug
- **Location:** `src/renderer/src/routes/creators/$creatorId.tsx:44-45`
- **Confidence:** 0.72 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

The detail pages (creators/$creatorId, videos.$videoId, collections/$collectionId) register a global window keydown listener (useShortcut listens on window) that runs router.history.back() on Escape. These same pages open Radix dialogs (e.g. AddToCollectionDialog). Radix DismissableLayer handles Escape via its own document listener and calls preventDefault() but does not stopPropagation to the window listener, so a single Escape both closes the dialog AND navigates the user off the page. isTextInputActive() only suppresses the shortcut when focus is in an INPUT/TEXTAREA/contentEditable; right after a dialog opens, focus is typically on a button or the dialog content, so the guard does not apply. Result: opening a dialog then pressing Escape unexpectedly tears down the whole detail page.

**Evidence**

~~~text
useShortcut('escape', () => router.history.back())
useShortcut('backspace', () => router.history.back())
...
<AddToCollectionDialog  (lines 263, 436)
~~~

**Fix**

Guard the back-shortcut against open overlays: skip when document.querySelector('[data-state="open"][role="dialog"]') exists, or tie an `enabled` flag to dialog state, or rely on Radix's own Escape and only bind Backspace. At minimum, do not bind Escape globally on pages that host dialogs.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

The underlying mechanism is real. useShortcut binds window.addEventListener('keydown', onKeyDown) in the bubble phase (src/renderer/hooks/use-shortcut.ts:155) and the handler runs router.history.back() without checking event.defaultPrevented. Radix's dismiss logic (node_modules/@radix-ui/react-use-escape-keydown/dist/index.mjs) listens on document in CAPTURE phase and, on Escape, calls only event.preventDefault() (confirmed at react-dismissable-layer/dist/index.mjs:64) вҖ” it never calls stopPropagation(). Because preventDefault does not stop other listeners, the same Escape event still bubbles up to window and fires the klip back-shortcut. The back-shortcuts at creators/$creatorId.tsx:44-45 (and videos.$videoId.tsx:52-53, collections/$collectionId.tsx:27-28) are unconditionally enabled вҖ” the `enabled: ... && addTarget === null` flags on these pages belong to useListKeyboardNav, not to the back-shortcut. So a single Escape closing a dialog can also tear down the detail page. HOWEVER, the reviewer's repro is partly wrong: every dialog actually mounted on these pages autofocuses a TEXT INPUT on open вҖ” AddToCollectionDialog uses cmdk CommandInput (<input>), RenameCollectionDialog has an autoFocus Input, and BulkActionsBar's dialog has TagInput's <input> as its first focusable. So immediately after opening, document.activeElement is an INPUT, isTextInputActive() returns true (src/renderer/lib/dom-helpers.ts), and the back-shortcut is suppressed. The claim that focus 'is typically on a button right after a dialog opens' is false for these specific dialogs. The bug is genuinely reachable only once focus leaves the input вҖ” e.g. the user Tabs to Cancel/Save/Apply вҖ” at which point Escape both dismisses the dialog and navigates back.

**Verifier notes**

Real latent bug, flawed repro. Sharper repro: open AddToCollectionDialog (or Rename/Bulk dialog) on a creator detail page, press Tab once to move focus from the text input onto the Cancel/Save button, then press Escape вҖ” the dialog closes AND the page navigates back (router.history.back). The naive 'open then immediately Escape' path is incidentally safe because all three dialogs autofocus an <input>, so isTextInputActive() suppresses the shortcut. Severity lowered to low: the common path is safe by accident, and the failure mode (navigating back one entry) is recoverable, not destructive. The suggested fix is still sound вҖ” gating the Escape back-shortcut on the absence of an open [role=dialog][data-state=open] (or relying on Radix for Escape and binding only Backspace) would make the dismissal robust regardless of focus. Note the same window-vs-Radix non-stopPropagation interaction would also affect any future dialog whose default focus is not a text input.

---

### F31 вҖ” Backspace bound as a global back-navigation key on detail pages

- **Severity:** рҹҹЎ LOW
- **Category:** bug
- **Location:** `src/renderer/src/routes/videos.$videoId.tsx:52-53`
- **Confidence:** 0.6 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

Binding Backspace globally to history.back() revives the long-deprecated browser footgun where a stray Backspace press (when focus is not in a text field вҖ” e.g. on a button, card, tab, or after clicking empty space) silently navigates the user back. isTextInputActive() only covers INPUT/TEXTAREA/SELECT/contentEditable, so Backspace on any non-input focus target (buttons, the focused #main-content div, custom widgets) triggers an unexpected navigation. This is duplicated across all three detail routes (creators/$creatorId, videos.$videoId, collections/$collectionId).

**Evidence**

~~~text
useShortcut('escape', () => router.history.back())
useShortcut('backspace', () => router.history.back())
~~~

**Fix**

Drop the Backspace binding (Escape alone is the conventional 'go back' affordance for detail panes), or restrict it so it only fires when focus is on the page background, not interactive controls.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I read the actual code. videos.$videoId.tsx:52-53 binds both 'escape' and 'backspace' single-key shortcuts to router.history.back(). useShortcut (src/renderer/hooks/use-shortcut.ts) only suppresses single-key shortcuts when isTextInputActive() is true, and on a match it calls event.preventDefault() then the handler (lines 122, 149-152). isTextInputActive() (src/renderer/lib/dom-helpers.ts:7-14) returns true ONLY for INPUT/TEXTAREA/SELECT/contentEditable. So for any other focus target вҖ” a focused <Button> (after the user clicks Refresh, Play, HistoryButton, or a Tabs trigger), a focused div, card, or custom widget, or document.body вҖ” a stray Backspace press fires history.back() with no further guard. modifiersMatch also requires no ctrl/meta/alt, so a bare Backspace (the common accidental press) does match. This is exactly the deprecated-browser-Backspace footgun the finding describes. I confirmed it is duplicated verbatim in creators/$creatorId.tsx:45 and collections/$collectionId.tsx:28. The claim and its evidence both match the current code.

**Verifier notes**

Repro: open a video detail page, click the 'Refresh' Button (or any Tabs trigger / the Play button / HistoryButton) so it retains focus, then press Backspace вҖ” the app silently navigates back (preventDefault is also called, so it would even swallow a backspace meant for something else). Same on creator and collection detail pages. Severity is genuinely low: back-navigation is non-destructive and easily reversed, and the press must land while a non-input element holds focus. Note the codebase's own use-shortcut JSDoc frames single-key suppression around typing-hijack prevention only; nothing documents Backspace-as-back as intentional. Reasonable fixes: drop the backspace binding (Escape already covers 'go back' for detail panes), or gate it so it only fires when document.activeElement is body/the page background rather than an interactive control. Real but minor polish issue, not a correctness/data bug.

---

### F32 вҖ” Unused dependency react-router (app uses @tanstack/react-router)

- **Severity:** рҹҹЎ LOW
- **Category:** dead-code
- **Location:** `package.json:76`
- **Confidence:** 0.85 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

Routing in the renderer is entirely @tanstack/react-router (every `Link`/`useNavigate`/`useRouterState` import resolves to '@tanstack/react-router'). A grep for `from 'react-router'` / `require('react-router')` across src, css, config, tests, and the built out/ bundle returns nothing. Plain react-router v7 is an installed-but-unused package вҖ” likely a copy-paste leftover. It ships transitive weight and can confuse future contributors into importing the wrong router.

**Evidence**

~~~text
"react-router": "^7.15.0",
~~~

**Fix**

Remove "react-router" from package.json dependencies and run npm install to prune.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

package.json:76 declares `"react-router": "^7.15.0"` as a direct dependency. I grepped the entire repo for `from 'react-router'`, `require('react-router')`, and `from 'react-router-dom'` (anchored patterns that exclude the @tanstack/ scoped package) and got zero matches. Every routing symbol in the renderer вҖ” createFileRoute, useNavigate, useRouter, useRouterState, Link, RouterProvider, createRouter вҖ” imports from '@tanstack/react-router', a self-contained router that does not list plain react-router as a peer dependency (verified the package-lock entry for @tanstack/react-router has no react-router peer). The package also appears in src/routeTree.gen.ts and test mocks, all under the @tanstack scope. No config, CSS, or test file references bare react-router. The package is installed-but-unused.

**Verifier notes**

Genuine unused direct dependency. Removing `"react-router": "^7.15.0"` from dependencies and running `npm install` is safe вҖ” nothing imports it and it is not a peer of @tanstack/react-router. A pre-existing repo audit (audits/01-dead-code.md:57) reaches the identical conclusion, corroborating the finding. Severity low is appropriate (no runtime/security impact; only disk weight and contributor-confusion risk). Note plain react-router v7 is tree-shakeable / not bundled since it is never imported, so the actual shipped-bundle savings are zero; only node_modules disk and potential mis-import are affected.

### F34 вҖ” CommentsCache.invalidate() is never called вҖ” documented stale-data protection is unimplemented

- **Severity:** рҹҹЎ LOW
- **Category:** dead-code
- **Location:** `src/main/framework-drivers/comments-cache/CommentsCache.ts:42-48, 124-127`
- **Confidence:** 0.85 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

The method and its contract describe behavior (drop stale comments when a manual refresh fails) that is never wired up. FetchVideoComments only ever calls cache.write on success; on a failed re-fetch the prior cached payload survives its full 7-day TTL and GetCachedVideoComments keeps serving it. So the 'Refresh' affordance can silently keep showing old comments after a failed refresh вҖ” the exact scenario the comment says invalidate guards against. Either dead code or an unimplemented feature.

**Evidence**

~~~text
invalidate(videoId: string): void { if (!VIDEO_ID_RE.test(videoId)) return; this.safeDelete(this.pathFor(videoId)) }  вҖ” JSDoc: 'Used as a manual invalidator (e.g. when the user explicitly hits Refresh and the fresh fetch fails вҖ” we don't want to keep serving stale data).' A repo-wide search for `.invalidate(` on the comments cache returns zero call sites.
~~~

**Fix**

Call cache.invalidate(videoId) in the FetchVideoComments error path (or in the controller that handles an explicit Refresh failure), or delete the method and its doc if the intra-session staleness is acceptable.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I read CommentsCache.ts and confirmed the cited code is intact: ICommentsCache.invalidate is declared at line 48 with the JSDoc describing it as a manual invalidator for "when the user explicitly hits Refresh and the fresh fetch fails вҖ” we don't want to keep serving stale data," and the implementation lives at lines 124-127 (safeDelete of pathFor). A repo-wide grep for invalidate shows the comments cache's invalidate appears only at its own declaration (48) and definition (124) вҖ” zero call sites. Every other invalidate hit is React Query's unrelated qc.invalidateQueries.

I traced the consumers via composition-root.ts (lines 416-418): the single CommentsCache instance is injected only into FetchVideoComments and GetCachedVideoComments. FetchVideoComments.execute (src/main/use-cases/FetchVideoComments.ts) awaits this.downloader.fetchComments at line 37, then only on the success path calls this.cache.write at line 47 вҖ” if fetchComments throws, the error propagates and the prior cached file is left untouched for its full 7-day TTL. GetCachedVideoComments.execute simply returns this.cache.read. Neither path, nor any controller/IPC handler, calls invalidate.

The renderer corroborates the staleness: useFetchVideoComments (use-videos.ts:98-107) seeds the cache query via setQueryData only onSuccess with no onError, and useCachedVideoComments uses staleTime: Infinity / gcTime: Infinity вҖ” so a failed refresh leaves both the disk cache and the in-memory query holding old data. The exact scenario the JSDoc claims invalidate guards against is unhandled. This is genuine dead code / an unimplemented feature, not a false positive.

**Verifier notes**

Confirmed unwired. Repro: open a video's Comments tab (populates from disk cache), then trigger a refresh (useFetchVideoComments) while yt-dlp fails (e.g. HTTP 429 or network drop). fetchComments throws, FetchVideoComments never reaches cache.write, and the renderer's onSuccess-only seeding plus staleTime:Infinity means the stale comments keep showing вҖ” exactly what the JSDoc says invalidate prevents. Severity correctly low: the cache TTL is bounded (7 days), the data is non-destructive show-and-forget content, and it self-heals on the next successful fetch. Fix is as the reviewer suggests вҖ” either call cache.invalidate(videoId) in FetchVideoComments' error path (and clear/refetch the renderer query onError), or delete the method + JSDoc and accept intra-session staleness. Minor: deleting invalidate would also let the ICommentsCache interface shrink.

export function useCutById(id: string | undefined): UseQueryResult<CutDto | null, Error> {
  return useQuery({ queryKey: queryKeys.cuts.detail(id!), queryFn: () => window.api.getCutById(id!), enabled: !!id })

export function useCutsByTags(tags: string[]): UseQueryResult<CutDto[], Error> {

The cited line numbers in the reviewer's evidence are correct; only the audit doc's inline line refs (12/20) are slightly stale, which is immaterial.

**Verifier notes**

Low severity is appropriate: these are plausible forward-compat seams for a future /cuts/$cutId detail route or tag-browsing UI, with zero runtime, correctness, or security impact. The downstream getCutById/getCutsByTags preload invokers (preload/index.ts:53-54, typed in preload/index.d.ts:97-98) and queryKeys.cuts.detail/byTags are transitively dead too вҖ” if the hooks are deleted, those should be considered for removal as well (and presumably the corresponding main-process get-cut-by-id / get-cuts-by-tags IPC handlers). Recommended action stands: delete now, or annotate with a knip ignore + comment if a detail route is imminent so the signal stops recurring.

### F38 вҖ” Three IPC channels are fully wired but never called by the renderer (orphans)

- **Severity:** рҹҹЎ LOW
- **Category:** dead-code
