This is maintained dead surface: every channel must be kept in sync across six files and each is an extra attack-surface entry that contributes runtime cost (zod schema construction, contextBridge exposure) for no consumer. probe-media-file additionally carries the containment gap above; get-operation-by-id/get-operations-by-status return OperationDto whose payload field is documented to embed serialized old/new filesystem paths, so removing them also closes a latent DTO path-leak.

**Evidence**

~~~text
ProbeMediaFile: 'probe-media-file', ... GetOperationById: 'get-operation-by-id', GetOperationsByStatus: 'get-operations-by-status'
~~~

**Fix**

Remove the three channels (and their schema/contract/preload/controller entries) until a renderer consumer exists, or document them as intentional future surface. If kept, knip should be configured to flag renderer-unused IPC channels.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I independently verified all six layers. ipc-channels.ts lines 11/89-90 match the quoted names exactly. The three channels (probe-media-file, get-operation-by-id, get-operations-by-status) are fully wired: ipc-contract.ts:72/244/248, ipc-schemas.ts:92/250/251, preload/index.ts:23/103/104, preload/index.d.ts:67/147/148, controllers DownloadController.ts and OperationController.ts, and both controllers are actually registered in src/main/index.ts:123/180. A grep of src/renderer for probeMediaFile|getOperationById|getOperationsByStatus returns ZERO matches; a whole-src grep shows only definition/wiring sites, never a renderer consumer. The grep is reliable: the sibling read channels getAuditLogRecent/getAuditLogByEntity DO appear in src/renderer/hooks/use-audit-log.ts, exactly as the reviewer claimed. The only references outside the wiring are (a) main-process controller unit tests, (b) composition-root.test.ts, and (c) tests/renderer/helpers/test-utils.tsx where they exist as bare vi.fn() mocks padding out the full window.api surface вҖ” none is an actual renderer call. The plan file plans/plan-codebaseReview-planB-ipc-audit-cleanup.prompt.md is a proposed audit/cleanup document, not a consumer. So the core claim вҖ” three fully-wired-but-renderer-orphaned IPC channels вҖ” is real.

**Verifier notes**

Confirmed as maintained dead surface across 6 files plus duplicated mocks in tests/renderer/helpers/test-utils.tsx and dedicated controller tests (so removal would also drop those). Severity low is correct and should not be inflated: these are contract-bounded read channels that already pass through zod tuple validation at the handler boundary (ipc-schemas.ts), so the 'attack surface / runtime cost' framing is mild вҖ” the marginal cost is one zod tuple + one contextBridge entry each. Two reviewer sub-claims are weaker than the core finding and should not raise severity: (1) the 'probe-media-file containment gap above' is a cross-reference to a separate finding I did not evaluate; (2) the DTO path-leak claim is only partially supported вҖ” OperationDto.payload is typed `string` (an opaque serialized blob, dtos/OperationDto.ts:6); whether it actually embeds old/new filesystem paths was not verified at source and is speculative. The dead-code core stands on its own regardless of those two. Suggested fix is reasonable: delete the three channels and their test mocks until a consumer exists, or annotate as intentional future surface and add a knip rule for renderer-unused channels.

### F39 вҖ” Unused test helper createIpcMainStub (mockElectronIpc.ts) referenced by no test

- **Severity:** рҹҹЎ LOW
- **Category:** dead-code
- **Location:** `tests/main/helpers/mockElectronIpc.ts:1-30`
- **Confidence:** 0.85 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

createIpcMainStub / IpcInvokeHandler are exported but a grep for `createIpcMainStub`, `mockElectronIpc`, and `IpcInvokeHandler` across tests/ and src/ finds no reference outside this file's own definition. The intended consumers (controller tests using vi.mock('electron')) never import it. Dead test scaffolding.

**Evidence**

~~~text
export function createIpcMainStub(): {
  ipcMain: { handle: ReturnType<typeof vi.fn>; on: ReturnType<typeof vi.fn> }
  handlers: Map<string, IpcInvokeHandler>
  invoke: <T = unknown>(channel: string, ...args: unknown[]) => Promise<T>
}
~~~

**Fix**

Delete tests/main/helpers/mockElectronIpc.ts, or wire it into the controller registration tests it was written for.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I read tests/main/helpers/mockElectronIpc.ts (32 lines). It exports the type IpcInvokeHandler and function createIpcMainStub, a vitest fake of electron.ipcMain. A full-repo grep (including *.ts/*.tsx/*.js/*.json, excluding node_modules) for createIpcMainStub, mockElectronIpc, and IpcInvokeHandler returns only the file's own definition line вҖ” no importer, no string/dynamic reference, no config entry. The JSDoc says test files "use this with vi.hoisted + vi.mock('electron',...)" but no such test exists. To rule out a non-obvious import convention, I checked the sibling helper createTestDb.ts in the same directory: it is imported via standard relative paths (`./helpers/createTestDb`) by composition-root.test.ts and framework-drivers/database.test.ts, proving helpers here are consumed by ordinary imports вҖ” so the absence of any import for mockElectronIpc is meaningful, not a tooling blind spot. It is not a runtime/electron-vite entry point and appears in no config. This is dead test scaffolding written for controller-registration tests that were never created.

**Verifier notes**

Severity low is appropriate вҖ” it's a test-only file with no production impact, purely a cleanliness issue. The reviewer's suggested fix is correct: either delete the file or wire it into a controller registration test. Repro: from repo root, `grep -rn "createIpcMainStub" --include="*.ts" .` returns a single hit (the definition at mockElectronIpc.ts:10), and `grep -rn "mockElectronIpc" .` (excluding node_modules) returns nothing.

### F40 вҖ” 0009 migration snapshot is missing from migrations/meta

- **Severity:** рҹҹЎ LOW
- **Category:** other
- **Location:** `src/main/framework-drivers/database/migrations/meta/_journal.json:68-74`
- **Confidence:** 0.8 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** yes

**Impact**

Known pre-existing gap. The migrations apply cleanly (verified: 0010_snapshot.json already captures transcript_text from 0009 and edit_recipe_json from 0010, so the prevId snapshot chain is internally consistent), so runtime is unaffected. The risk is purely at authoring time: `drizzle-kit generate` walks snapshots, and a missing one can cause it to re-emit 0009's `ALTER TABLE videos ADD transcript_text` into the next generated migration, producing a duplicate-column failure at apply time on a fresh DB.

**Evidence**

~~~text
_journal.json lists entry idx 9 tag '0009_swift_silent_search', but the meta/ directory contains 0008_snapshot.json then jumps straight to 0010_snapshot.json вҖ” there is no 0009_snapshot.json. (Directory listing: 0008_snapshot.json, 0010_snapshot.json, 0011_snapshot.json.)
~~~

**Fix**

Reconstruct 0009_snapshot.json by taking 0010_snapshot.json and reverting the edit_recipe_json column + bumping the id/prevId to fit between 0008 and 0010, or regenerate the snapshot chain with drizzle-kit. Until then, hand-author any new migration's SQL and verify it does not re-ALTER existing columns.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I directly verified the directory and journal. meta/ contains 0000-0008, then 0010, 0011 вҖ” 0009_snapshot.json is genuinely absent, while _journal.json idx 9 (0009_swift_silent_search) and the SQL file 0009_swift_silent_search.sql both exist. The core fact of the finding is REAL and matches the standing MEMORY note.

However, two parts of the reviewer's justification are inaccurate:

1. "The prevId snapshot chain is internally consistent" is WRONG. Extracted ids: 0008.id = 2a46051d-6e39-4070-8225-1b16ee0a336d, 0010.id = e358e477..., 0011.prevId = e358e477..., and 0010.prevId = 2a46051d... = 0008's id. So the chain jumps 0008 -> 0010 directly, skipping 0009 as a node. It is an unbroken pointer chain only because 0009 was never inserted; it does NOT capture 0009's intermediate state.

2. Runtime-unaffected: CORRECT, but for a stronger reason than stated. database.ts:36 uses drizzle-orm/better-sqlite3/migrator migrate(), which applies the .sql files by journal tag tracked in __drizzle_migrations and never reads meta/*_snapshot.json. The 0009 SQL file exists and applies in order, so a fresh DB migrates fine.

3. The duplicate-column repro is OVERSTATED. 0009 SQL does ALTER TABLE videos ADD transcript_text. Grepped snapshots: 0008 has 0 occurrences of transcript_text; 0010 has it (count 2); 0011 has it. drizzle-kit generate diffs against the LATEST snapshot (0011), which already contains transcript_text, so it will NOT re-emit ADD transcript_text under the normal path. The duplicate-column failure would only arise via snapshot-walk / drizzle-kit up / regenerate operations that traverse the broken prevId chain and hit the missing node.

Net: the gap is real and authoring-time tooling integrity is genuinely compromised, but the specific "next generate re-emits the ALTER -> duplicate column on fresh DB" mechanism is unlikely as described. Severity low is appropriate.

**Verifier notes**

Confirmed with corrections. Where the reviewer is wrong: (a) the snapshot chain is NOT internally consistent вҖ” 0010_snapshot.json prevId = 2a46051d... = 0008's id, so the chain skips 0009; (b) runtime is unaffected because the better-sqlite3 migrator (database.ts:36) applies SQL by journal tag and never reads meta/*_snapshot.json, not merely because 0010 is self-consistent; (c) the duplicate-column repro is overstated: 0011_snapshot.json (the latest, what drizzle-kit generate diffs against) already contains transcript_text, so a normal generate won't re-emit 0009's ALTER. Genuine risk is narrower: any drizzle-kit op that walks the snapshot chain (regenerate / drizzle-kit up / integrity check) hits the prevId discontinuity and the missing 0009 node. The suggested fix (reconstruct 0009_snapshot.json between 0008 and 0010, fixing id/prevId so 0010.prevId points at it) is correct and should re-link the chain. Also note 0009 creates a virtual FTS5 table + triggers that drizzle snapshots don't track at all, so even a reconstructed snapshot won't represent videos_fts вҖ” hand-authoring FTS-touching migrations remains necessary regardless.

### F41 вҖ” pushSchema() omits the FK reverse-lookup indexes present in the real schema

- **Severity:** рҹҹЎ LOW
- **Category:** performance
- **Location:** `src/main/framework-drivers/database/database.ts:202-207`
- **Confidence:** 0.85 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

Another instance of in-memory/production schema drift. The reverse-lookup indexes (which the schema author deliberately added to avoid full-scanning the join tables on video/cut delete and on 'which collections contain X') do not exist in :memory: test DBs. Query plans exercised in tests therefore do not match production, and EXPLAIN-based or perf-sensitive tests would be misleading. Functionally harmless (queries still return correct rows) but defeats the purpose of testing against a faithful schema.

**Evidence**

~~~text
pushSchema creates only idx_collection_videos_position and idx_collection_cuts_position. schema.ts:224 and schema.ts:246 additionally define index('idx_collection_videos_video_id').on(table.videoId) and index('idx_collection_cuts_cut_id').on(table.cutId), with comments explaining they back the FK CASCADE / reverse lookups. Those two indexes are absent from pushSchema.
~~~

**Fix**

Add the two missing CREATE INDEX statements to pushSchema, or generate pushSchema DDL from the schema so indexes can't be forgotten.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I read pushSchema() (database.ts:46, index block at 185-207). It creates idx_collection_videos_position and idx_collection_cuts_position but NOT idx_collection_videos_video_id or idx_collection_cuts_cut_id. schema.ts:224 and :246 do define those two FK reverse-lookup indexes, with comments explaining they back the "which collections contain X?" reverse lookup and the FK CASCADE on delete, to avoid full-scanning the join tables. The production migration 0008_shallow_wild_child.sql actually emits both CREATE INDEX statements, and they persist in snapshots 0008/0010/0011 вҖ” so migration-driven production DBs have these indexes, while in-memory (:memory:) test DBs built via pushSchema() do not. This is genuine drift. AGENTS.md (lines 147, 169, 499, 613) explicitly states pushSchema() must match the production schema and is the source of truth for in-memory test DBs, so the drift contradicts a documented invariant rather than being intentional. The drift is functionally harmless (correct rows still returned; SQLite just full-scans the small join tables in tests), but it makes the test schema non-faithful and could mislead any EXPLAIN/query-plan/perf-sensitive test.

**Verifier notes**

Repro: open a createTestDb() in-memory DB and run `PRAGMA index_list(collection_videos)` / `index_list(collection_cuts)` вҖ” only the *_position indexes appear; the *_video_id / *_cut_id indexes present in production (from migration 0008) are missing. Fix: add the two CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS statements after database.ts:207 (idx_collection_videos_video_id ON collection_videos(video_id); idx_collection_cuts_cut_id ON collection_cuts(cut_id)). Better long-term fix per the reviewer: generate pushSchema DDL from the Drizzle schema so indexes can't be forgotten вҖ” this is the third such hand-maintained drift class. Severity low is fair (arguably info, but low is defensible since it violates a documented AGENTS.md invariant). Note also memory item project_drizzle_0009_snapshot_gap documents a related migration/snapshot maintenance gap in this same area.

---

### F42 вҖ” Audited upsert() without prior state still does a redundant findById; EnrichMediaMetadata hits this path

- **Severity:** рҹҹЎ LOW
- **Category:** performance
- **Location:** `src/main/interface-adapters/repositories/AuditedVideoRepository.ts:95-98`
- **Confidence:** 0.68 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** yes

**Impact**

Prior audit M1 is largely fixed: ReconcileDirectory now calls upsertWithPrevious with the row it already has. The plain upsert() path still does an extra PK SELECT per call, and it is hit by EnrichMediaMetadata.execute(), which calls videoRepo.upsert(...) / cutRepo.upsert(...) for every probed entity (EnrichMediaMetadata.ts:33,57) instead of upsertWithPrevious with the in-hand row. At 5K freshly-discovered entities that is 5K avoidable PK SELECTs during the post-reconcile enrich pass (~50ms). Not user-visible (async, off the window-paint path) but free to remove.

**Evidence**

~~~text
upsert(video: Video): void {
  // Caller didn't supply prior state; read it for the audit diff.
  this.upsertWithPrevious(video, this.inner.findById(video.id))
}
~~~

**Fix**

Have EnrichMediaMetadata pass the entity it already loaded: this.videoRepo.upsertWithPrevious({...video, ...probe}, video). The decorator then skips findById and goes straight to inner.upsert + audit append.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I read AuditedVideoRepository.ts:95-98 and the quoted code is exact: upsert(video) calls this.upsertWithPrevious(video, this.inner.findById(video.id)), performing a PK SELECT to fetch prior state. The inner Sqlite repos (SqliteVideoRepository:255, SqliteCutRepository:248) accept _previous but ignore it, so the findById cost lives entirely in the audit decorator and exists only to compute the audit diff. EnrichMediaMetadata.execute() (lines 25, 29-40, 53-64) loads pendingVideos/pendingCuts via findByProbeStatus вҖ” each iteration already holds a full Video/Cut entity (`video`, `cut`) вҖ” yet writes back through the plain upsert() at lines 33 and 57, not upsertWithPrevious. So for every probed entity the decorator re-reads a row that is already in hand: a genuinely redundant SELECT. The codebase has already adopted upsertWithPrevious as the convention everywhere else (BulkUpdateTags, DeleteTagGlobally, MoveVideosToCreator, RenameTagGlobally, ReconcileDirectory:422/523), so EnrichMediaMetadata is the lone holdout on the hot enrich path. The suggested fix (pass `video`/`cut` as the previous arg) is correct and idiomatic for this repo. Note one nuance for correctness if applied: the entity passed as `previous` should be the pre-probe row so the diff still produces the enrichment-only changeset that isEnrichmentOnly() suppresses вҖ” passing the original `video` (not the spread copy) achieves exactly that.

**Verifier notes**

Confirmed but firmly low/info. Real-world impact is tiny: the redundant findById is a single-row indexed PK lookup, runs async after reconcile off the window-paint path, and only at the (rare) moment of bulk first-discovery does it scale to thousands. The reviewer's ~50ms@5K figure is order-of-magnitude plausible but optimistic-to-pessimistic depending on page cache; in steady-state operation it is a handful of lookups. Fix is free and matches existing repo convention вҖ” worth doing as cleanup, not as a perf priority. When applying, pass the ORIGINAL in-hand entity (video/cut) as `previous`, not the spread-updated copy, so diffObjects still yields only enrichment fields and the existing isEnrichmentOnly() audit-suppression keeps working (otherwise behavior is unchanged anyway since the same row is read today).

### F43 вҖ” GetCollectionItems is N+1: one findById per collection item

- **Severity:** рҹҹЎ LOW
- **Category:** performance
- **Location:** `src/main/use-cases/GetCollectionItems.ts:13-34`
- **Confidence:** 0.7 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

For a collection with K items this issues K primary-key SELECTs (one per video/cut) on top of the getItems UNION query. Bounded by collection size (schema comment documents <500 items), so ~500 PK lookups ~5ms worst case вҖ” not a freeze. But it runs on every collection-detail render and the db-listener invalidates queryKeys.collections.all on *any* video or cut push (use-db-listener.ts:57-59), so a busy reconcile/enrich storm re-runs it per open collection. Defensive note, not user-visible at the documented scale.

**Evidence**

~~~text
const items = this.collectionRepo.getItems(collectionId)
return items.map((item) => {
  if (item.kind === 'video') {
    const video = this.videoRepo.findById(item.id)
    ...
  }
  const cut = this.cutRepo.findById(item.id)
  ...
~~~

**Fix**

Batch the two kinds: collect video ids and cut ids, then videoRepo.findByIds(ids) / cutRepo.findByIds(ids) (add inArray-based bulk getters) and stitch back by id, turning K+1 queries into 3.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

All factual claims hold up against the real code. GetCollectionItems.execute (src/main/use-cases/GetCollectionItems.ts:13-34) matches the quoted code exactly: it calls collectionRepo.getItems(collectionId) once, then maps over the result calling videoRepo.findById(item.id) or cutRepo.findById(item.id) per item. SqliteCollectionRepository.getItems (line 109) is a single UNION ALL query, and SqliteVideoRepository.findById (line 78) / the cut equivalent are single PK SELECTs (eq(videos.id, id) .get()). So for K items the call issues 1 UNION + K PK SELECTs = K+1 queries. I grepped the entire main/ tree: there is no findByIds / inArray bulk getter on any repo, so the suggested batching is not already implemented. The db-listener claim is also accurate: use-db-listener.ts:57-59 invalidates queryKeys.collections.all whenever a push includes 'videos' OR 'cuts', so an enrich/reconcile storm (which pushes video/cut scopes repeatedly) will re-run GetCollectionItems for every open collection-detail query. GetCollectionsPaginated.toDto also calls getItems per collection but only reads items.length (no per-item findById), so it is NOT subject to the N+1 and is fine. The reviewer's own framing вҖ” bounded by collection size, ~milliseconds, not a freeze, defensive note вҖ” is honest and correct.

**Verifier notes**

Real but minor. better-sqlite3 is synchronous and in-process, so each PK SELECT is on the order of microseconds, not network-RTT milliseconds; the reviewer's ~5ms-for-500-items worst case is the right order of magnitude and confirms this is not a perceptible freeze. The genuine amplifier is the invalidation fan-out at use-db-listener.ts:57-59 combined with multiple simultaneously-open/cached collection-detail queries during a reconcile storm вҖ” that is the only path where it could matter, and even then it is bounded. The suggested fix (add inArray-based findByIds to IVideoRepository/ICutRepository + their Sqlite impls, collect ids by kind, stitch by id вҶ’ 3 queries) is clean and correct; the only subtlety is preserving the position ordering from getItems when re-stitching, which a Map<id, dto> lookup over the original items array handles. Worth doing as a low-priority cleanup, not urgent. Note GetCollectionsPaginated is unaffected (uses only items.length).

---

### F44 вҖ” GetCollectionsPaginated runs an N+1: getItems() per collection just to read itemCount

- **Severity:** рҹҹЎ LOW _(verifier corrected from medium)_
- **Category:** performance
- **Location:** `src/main/use-cases/GetCollectionsPaginated.ts:18-29`
- **Confidence:** 0.85 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

For every collection on a page, toDto calls collectionRepo.getItems(c.id), which executes a UNION ALL over collection_videos + collection_cuts and fully materializes every member row only to read .length. With the schema's documented <500 items/collection and pageSize capped at 500 (ipc-schemas), a single Collections page can fire up to 500 of these UNION queries and allocate every membership row across the page, when all that is needed is a COUNT. This is a per-page query-count cliff that grows linearly with library size. The repository API has no countItems(collectionId) (or batched counts) method, which is the root cause.

**Evidence**

~~~text
private toDto(c: Collection): CollectionDto {
    const items = this.collectionRepo.getItems(c.id)
    return { ... itemCount: items.length, ... }
  }
~~~

**Fix**

Add a countItems(collectionId) (or batched countItemsByCollection(ids[])) method to ICollectionRepository that issues `SELECT COUNT(*)` against each join table (or one grouped query over both via UNION ALL + GROUP BY collection_id), and have toDto use it instead of getItems().length. Better: compute all item counts for the page's ids in a single query.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

Verified all three load-bearing claims against the real code. (1) GetCollectionsPaginated.ts:18-29 is exactly as quoted: toDto() calls this.collectionRepo.getItems(c.id) and uses only items.length for itemCount; execute() maps it over every collection on the page (page.data.map(c => this.toDto(c))). So it is one getItems() call per collection on the page. (2) SqliteCollectionRepository.getItems (lines 109-128) issues a UNION ALL over collection_videos + collection_cuts and fully materializes every membership row (SELECT ... id, position, addedAt) with an ORDER BY position вҖ” there is no LIMIT/COUNT path. (3) ICollectionRepository.ts has no countItems / batched count method; the only item-read is getItems(). The pageSize cap is confirmed at src/shared/ipc-schemas.ts:30 (z.int().min(1).max(500)). So the N+1 is real: a Collections page fires one full-materialization UNION query per collection, when a SELECT COUNT(*) (or a single grouped count over both join tables) would suffice. The suggested fix (countItems / batched countItemsByCollection(ids[]) returning grouped COUNTs) is sound and the root-cause attribution (missing count API) is correct. No guard, cache, or alternate path mitigates this вҖ” getItems is the sole source of itemCount.

**Verifier notes**

Confirmed but the worst-case framing overstates it. The same ipc-schemas comment the finding cites also documents that the UI never asks for >100 items and that collections hold <500 items each; a realistic Collections page is ~tens of collections, each with tens of member rows, so the actual cost is ~N small UNION queries + modest row allocation, not 500Г—500. It is a real per-page query-count cliff that grows linearly with the number of collections shown, and the fix is cheap and correct, but the bounded scale guards make it a low-priority perf cleanup rather than medium. Sharper repro: load the Collections route with pageSize near its 100 typical / 500 max and a few hundred populated collections; observe N getItems UNION queries per page render (one per row), each materializing full membership rows only to read .length. Fix: add ICollectionRepository.countItemsByCollection(ids[]) doing a single `SELECT collection_id, COUNT(*) ... GROUP BY collection_id` UNION ALL'd across both join tables, and have execute() prefetch counts for page.data ids before mapping toDto.

---

### F45 вҖ” Persistent player rAF reposition loop runs every frame for the entire detail session

- **Severity:** рҹҹЎ LOW
- **Category:** performance
- **Location:** `src/renderer/components/features/player/PersistentPlayer.tsx:207-258`
- **Confidence:** 0.5 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

In detail mode the component schedules an unconditional self-perpetuating requestAnimationFrame that calls getBoundingClientRect() every frame for as long as the detail view is mounted, even when nothing scrolls or resizes. The early-out only skips the four style writes, not the rAF churn or the layout read. getBoundingClientRect forces a layout flush each frame; with active video decoding this is measurable CPU/battery on laptops. The author acknowledges the cost in a comment but dismisses it.

**Evidence**

~~~text
let rafId = requestAnimationFrame(function tick() {
  update()
  rafId = requestAnimationFrame(tick)
})
...
const update = (): void => { const r = slotEl.getBoundingClientRect() ... }
~~~

**Fix**

Gate the rAF loop on motion: start it on the ScrollArea viewport scroll + window resize/ResizeObserver, run for a few frames after motion, then stop. Or stop re-arming after N idle frames and fall back to event-driven updates.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I read PersistentPlayer.tsx in full. The cited code is present and matches the quote. In the `mode === 'detail' && slotEl` branch of the useLayoutEffect (lines 197-258), the component starts a self-perpetuating rAF loop (lines 244-247): `let rafId = requestAnimationFrame(function tick() { update(); rafId = requestAnimationFrame(tick) })`. This re-arms unconditionally every frame for the entire lifetime of the detail-mode effect (cleanup only runs on mode/slotEl/mounted/corner change via the dep array at line 265, i.e. when leaving detail mode). `update()` (line 207) calls `slotEl.getBoundingClientRect()` (line 208) every frame. The early-out at lines 209-223 only guards the four `container.style.*` writes вҖ” it does NOT skip the getBoundingClientRect read or the rAF re-arm. So the reviewer's mechanical description is exactly correct: a per-frame layout read + rAF churn that runs even when nothing scrolls/resizes, on top of active video decoding. The author explicitly acknowledges and dismisses the cost in the comment at lines 227-243 ("a few floating-point reads per frame... the perf cost is invisible compared to video decoding happening anyway"). This is a real, accurately-described performance characteristic, though minor.

**Verifier notes**

Confirmed but correctly scoped at low вҖ” this is an informed, documented tradeoff, not an oversight. Mitigating factors the reviewer didn't mention: (1) rAF is automatically paused by the browser when the window is minimized/occluded/backgrounded, so the loop does not burn cycles when the app isn't visible; (2) at the top of a rAF callback, layout is usually already clean from the prior frame's render, so getBoundingClientRect often does not trigger a fresh forced reflow unless something else dirtied layout. The comment at lines 227-243 documents why event-driven alternatives were abandoned (Radix ScrollArea viewport scroll signals did not reliably reach window/ancestor listeners вҖ” a real prior bug noted in the user's memory: 'Radix ScrollArea scroll listeners are unreliable; use rAF'). The suggested fix (gate on scroll/resize + run N frames after motion, then idle out) is sound and would eliminate steady-state churn, but it reintroduces the exact Radix-viewport scroll-detection fragility the author deliberately worked around, so it is not a free win. A simpler mitigation: also pause the loop when the video is paused AND has had no recent layout change, or stop re-arming after K consecutive unchanged frames and rely on the already-present ResizeObserver (line 252) plus a scroll listener as the wake source. Sharper repro: open a video detail page, leave it playing and idle (no scrolling), profile with Chrome DevTools Performance вҖ” you'll see a getBoundingClientRect call on every animation frame indefinitely.

---

### F46 вҖ” PersistentPlayer runs a perpetual requestAnimationFrame loop whenever a video is mounted in detail mode

- **Severity:** рҹҹЎ LOW
- **Category:** performance
- **Location:** `src/renderer/components/features/player/PersistentPlayer.tsx:244-258`
- **Confidence:** 0.5 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

While the player is in detail mode the rAF loop is unconditional and never stops, calling slotEl.getBoundingClientRect() ~60x/sec for the lifetime of the mounted video even when nothing scrolls or resizes (paused video, static page). The author documents the tradeoff and the early-out skips style writes when the rect is unchanged, so the per-frame cost is a single getBoundingClientRect + four float compares. But it keeps the renderer from idling (continuous main-thread wakeups, prevents frame-rate power throttling) for as long as a video is open. Defensive/efficiency note, not user-visible.

**Evidence**

~~~text
let rafId = requestAnimationFrame(function tick() {
  update()
  rafId = requestAnimationFrame(tick)
})
~~~

**Fix**

Drive reposition from scroll/resize plus the already-wired ResizeObserver/IntersectionObserver and only spin a short-lived rAF during an active scroll, and/or gate the loop on document.hidden / visibilitychange so it stops when backgrounded.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I read the full file. Lines 244-247 contain exactly the quoted self-perpetuating rAF loop:

  let rafId = requestAnimationFrame(function tick() {
    update()
    rafId = requestAnimationFrame(tick)
  })

This is established inside the useLayoutEffect's `mode === 'detail' && slotEl` branch (lines 197-258). There is no gating on scroll activity, document.hidden, or playback state вҖ” once detail mode is mounted with a slot, the loop runs every frame for the lifetime of that effect, calling update() which always invokes slotEl.getBoundingClientRect() (line 208). So the finding's core claim is accurate: ~60 reads/sec continuously, regardless of whether anything is moving.

Mitigations the reviewer already acknowledges are real and present:
- The early-out (lines 209-223) compares the new rect against last-applied top/left/width/height and only writes the four style props on change, so the steady-state per-frame cost is one getBoundingClientRect + four float comparisons (no style writes / layout invalidation when static).
- Cleanup is correct: cancelAnimationFrame + ro.disconnect() on effect teardown (lines 255-258), and the effect re-runs on [mode, slotEl, mounted, corner], so leaving detail mode (e.g. switching to mini, which uses only a resize listener, lines 182-195) genuinely stops the loop. It is strictly a detail-mode cost, not a mini-mode one.
- The author extensively documents the tradeoff and the reason rAF was chosen over scroll listeners (lines 227-243): radix ScrollArea's viewport scroll signal did not reliably reach window/ancestor scroll listeners, so the rAF read sidesteps enumerating motion sources.

The downside the reviewer names вҖ” the renderer cannot fully idle / frame-rate power-throttle while a detail-mode video is open вҖ” is a genuine consequence of an unconditional rAF loop. It is real but tiny and not user-visible, especially since a decoding video is already keeping the compositor busy. This is a legitimate efficiency/defensive note, not a false positive (it is not handled elsewhere вҖ” there is no visibilitychange gate or scroll-scoped short-lived rAF anywhere in this component).

**Verifier notes**

Confirmed and correctly scoped at low. Repro: open a video detail route, pause it, leave the tab/window idle вҖ” the rAF tick fires ~60x/sec indefinitely (verifiable by a counter inside tick), each doing getBoundingClientRect on slotEl even with zero motion; only style writes are skipped via the NaN-seeded last* early-out. The suggested fix is sound but optional: a `document.hidden`/visibilitychange gate (pause the loop when backgrounded) is the cheapest improvement and would not regress the radix-scroll behavior the author worked around, since a backgrounded window isn't scrolling. A fully event-driven rewrite is riskier given the documented history of radix viewport scroll signals not propagating, so the visibility gate is the better-value change. Note this is detail-mode only; mini mode already avoids the loop.

---

### F47 вҖ” Unconditional console logging in the persistent <video> load lifecycle in production builds

- **Severity:** рҹҹЎ LOW _(verifier corrected from info)_
- **Category:** performance
- **Location:** `src/renderer/components/features/player/PersistentPlayer.tsx:601-612`
- **Confidence:** 0.55 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

Unconditional console.log on every media load in a shipping build, firing on every queue advance and every player open. Negligible perf impact (serialization/devtools overhead only); flagged as cleanup, not a cliff.

**Evidence**

~~~text
onLoadStart={() => { console.log('[PersistentPlayer] <video> loadstart', { videoId, mediaKind, src }) }}
onLoadedMetadata={(e) => { ... console.log('[PersistentPlayer] <video> loadedmetadata', {...}) }}
~~~

**Fix**

Gate the diagnostic logs behind a debug flag (import.meta.env.DEV or a runtime toggle) so production playback doesn't log on every load.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

Lines 601-612 of PersistentPlayer.tsx match the quoted code exactly: onLoadStart and onLoadedMetadata each call an unconditional console.log with no DEV/debug gating. I verified electron.vite.config.ts has no terser/esbuild drop_console or pure_funcs config for the renderer, so esbuild's default minifier preserves these calls in production builds. A repo-wide grep confirms console.log appears in renderer source only here (2x) and in logger.ts. The video element is rendered whenever a player is open, so these handlers fire on every player open and every queue advance (each new src triggers a fresh loadstart + loadedmetadata). The claim is factually accurate.

One important nuance the reviewer missed: src/renderer/src/logger.ts globally monkey-patches console.log to ALSO call electron-log's log.info(...), which serializes the payload and ships it over IPC to main, where it is written to the shared on-disk log file. So the cost is not merely "serialization/devtools overhead" вҖ” every load also incurs an IPC message and a log-file write in production. This raises the real-world impact slightly above the reviewer's framing, but it still fires only on discrete load events (not a high-frequency hot path like timeupdate), so it remains a low-severity cleanup item, not a performance cliff.

**Verifier notes**

Confirmed. Repro: open the player / advance the queue in a production build вҖ” each load emits two console.log calls. Sharper than the reviewer stated: because of the console.log monkey-patch in src/renderer/src/logger.ts (lines 43-46), each call also fires an IPC round-trip to main and a write to the shared electron-log file, so this pollutes the persistent log file on every media load, not just DevTools. Suggested fix stands: gate behind import.meta.env.DEV (or route through a dedicated debug logger). Note onError at lines 588-598 is legitimate console.error and should stay. Bumped severity info->low to reflect the IPC+disk amplification, though it is still not hot-path frequency.

---

### F48 вҖ” TranscriptTab renders every VTT segment unvirtualized with a per-segment ref callback

- **Severity:** рҹҹЎ LOW _(verifier corrected from medium)_
- **Category:** performance
- **Location:** `src/renderer/components/features/videos/TranscriptTab.tsx:254-287`
- **Confidence:** 0.6 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

All transcript segments are mounted at once. A 1-2 hour video produces hundreds to low-thousands of segments; each is a button with a ref callback and per-row match highlighting via renderSegmentText. Bounded by video length (not the 5K library), but opening the transcript of a long video and typing in the in-transcript search recomputes matches/matchesBySegment and re-renders the whole list on each keystroke. Measurable jank on long transcripts, not a hard freeze.

**Evidence**

~~~text
<ScrollArea className="h-125 rounded border">
  <ul className="divide-border divide-y p-1">
    {segments.map((seg, segIdx) => (
      <li key={`${seg.startMs}-${seg.endMs}`} ref={(node) => { if (node) segmentRefs.current.set(segIdx, node) else segmentRefs.current.delete(segIdx) }} ...>
        <button ... onClick={() => handleSeek(seg.startMs)}>
          ... {renderSegmentText(seg.text, segIdx)}
~~~

**Fix**

Virtualize the segment list (react-virtual, same as VirtualAuditList). The scroll-to-match logic can use the virtualizer's scrollToIndex instead of the segmentRefs Map.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

Read TranscriptTab.tsx in full. Lines 254-287 match the quoted code exactly: ScrollArea > ul > segments.map renders one <li> per segment with a per-row ref callback writing into segmentRefs Map (lines 259-262), a button (265-283), and renderSegmentText per row (281). No virtualization is present. Segments come from useTranscriptSegments -> window.api.getTranscriptSegments, which returns VTT caption cues (TranscriptSegment[]); VTT cues are short (a few words to a sentence each), so a 1-2h video realistically yields ~1000-2500 segments, all mounted at once. The search path is real jank: `matches` (lines 89-104) scans every segment's text and recomputes on every `query` change; `matchesBySegment` (106-114) derives from it; both feed renderSegmentText (162-186) which is called inside the map for all rows. Because the map closure references matchesBySegment and currentMatch, every keystroke re-renders the entire unvirtualized list and rebuilds the highlight nodes for matched rows. The suggested fix is sound and low-friction: the project already ships VirtualAuditList.tsx using a virtualizer, and the scroll-to-match effect (lines 120-126) reads segmentRefs.current.get(...).scrollIntoView, which would need to switch to virtualizer.scrollToIndex since a virtualized Map only holds visible rows. So the finding's repro and fix are both correct.

**Verifier notes**

Confirmed, but I'd dial severity from medium to low. The cost is gated behind two simultaneous conditions: viewing a long (1-2h) video's transcript AND actively typing in the in-transcript search. Initial render of a long transcript is also heavier than ideal but is a one-time mount, not per-keystroke. It is bounded by video length, never the 5K-item library, and produces jank rather than a freeze or crash. Mitigating debounce/throttle on the query input would blunt the keystroke path without full virtualization, but virtualization (react-virtual, already a dep via VirtualAuditList.tsx) is the clean fix and also addresses the mount cost. Sharper repro: open the transcript tab of a 90+ min video, type a common letter (e.g. 'e') and observe per-keystroke layout/recompute lag as matches[] is rebuilt over ~1-2k segments and the whole list re-renders. Note the fix must replace segmentRefs/scrollIntoView (lines 124-125) with virtualizer scrollToIndex.

### F49 вҖ” Bundled-binary SHA256 verification is scaffolded but disabled (every pinned hash is null)

- **Severity:** рҹҹЎ LOW
- **Category:** security
- **Location:** `scripts/download-binaries.ts:41-49, 213-238`
- **Confidence:** 0.9 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** yes

**Impact**

The integrity-verification machinery from baseline F8 (verifyBinaryHash, KLIP_SKIP_BINARY_VERIFY escape hatch, delete-then-throw on mismatch) is fully implemented, but every entry in SHASUMS is null, so verifyBinaryHash short-circuits to a warning and installs the binary unverified. The net effect today is identical to having no verification at all: a compromised GitHub/ffbinaries release artifact (maintainer-account takeover) would be downloaded, marked +x, and shipped. This is defense-in-depth only under the stated single-user/HTTPS-trusted threat model (hence LOW), but the audit's F8 exit criterion ('verify after download') is not actually met despite the code looking like it is.

**Evidence**

~~~text
const SHASUMS: Record<string, string | null> = {
  'yt-dlp.exe': null, 'yt-dlp_macos': null, 'yt-dlp_linux': null,
  'ffprobe.exe': null, ffprobe: null, 'ffmpeg.exe': null, ffmpeg: null }
...
if (!expected) { console.warn(`  вҡ  No SHA256 pinned for ${outputName} вҖ” skipping verification ...`); return }
~~~

**Fix**

Fill in the real SHA256 for each pinned platform binary at the current YT_DLP_VERSION / FFMPEG_VERSION and make hash-bumping part of the version-bump checklist. Until hashes are filled, consider failing closed (or printing a louder release-blocking warning) in CI/release builds rather than silently warning.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I read scripts/download-binaries.ts in full. The reviewer's quotes are exact and current. SHASUMS (lines 41-49) has every entry set to null. verifyBinaryHash (lines 213-238) is fully implemented вҖ” it computes a SHA256, compares against the pinned value, honors KLIP_SKIP_BINARY_VERIFY as an escape hatch, and does unlinkSync(filePath)+throw on mismatch вҖ” but line 215 `if (!expected)` short-circuits to a warning and returns whenever the pinned hash is null/empty. Since all entries are null, every real install path hits that early return. downloadBinary (line 262) calls verifyBinaryHash before chmod, exactly as designed, but with all-null hashes the call is a no-op, so the binary is then chmod 0o755 (line 266) and installed unverified. Net effect today is identical to no verification. The script is wired as `npm run setup` (package.json line 35: `tsx scripts/download-binaries.ts`), confirming it is the live setup entry point, not dead code. The download path uses pinned-version HTTPS URLs to github.com / ffbinaries releases with redirect-following, so the residual risk is upstream artifact compromise (maintainer-account takeover) вҖ” real but pre-existing and only meaningful as defense-in-depth under a single-author/HTTPS-trusted model. The finding is a genuine, accurate observation: the integrity check looks complete but is inert.

**Verifier notes**

Confirmed. This is a build/dev-time setup script (npm run setup), not runtime or shipped code, which is why LOW is correct вҖ” the parent process must already be trusted to run the setup at all, and downloads go over HTTPS to version-pinned release URLs. One nuance softening the 'looks done but isn't' framing: the source comments (lines 33-39) are explicitly honest that null 'skips verification with a warning вҖ” useful only while introducing the pinning workflow' and say 'Aim to fill in every entry before the next public release,' and I found no AGENTS.md/doc that actually claims the F8 'verify after download' criterion is met. So nothing is falsely asserting completeness вҖ” the gap is self-documented as TODO. The suggested fix is sound: fill in real SHA256 values per platform at the current YT_DLP_VERSION/FFMPEG_VERSION, add hash-bumping to the version-bump checklist, and consider failing closed (or a release-blocking error) when a hash is null in CI/release builds rather than silently warning. Repro: with resources/bin empty, run `npm run setup`; output shows 'вҡ  No SHA256 pinned for <name> вҖ” skipping verification' for all three binaries, yet each is installed and chmod +x'd.

---

### F50 вҖ” will-navigate hardening does not cover will-redirect

- **Severity:** рҹҹЎ LOW
- **Category:** security
- **Location:** `src/main/framework-drivers/electron/security-hardening.ts:86-97`
- **Confidence:** 0.5 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

Defence-in-depth gap. In this app the renderer is loaded from file:// / klip-media:// and external links are intercepted, so a redirect chain to an attacker origin is unlikely in normal operation. But if a renderer compromise initiated a navigation that 30x-redirects to https://evil/, will-navigate fires for the initial URL (allowed only if internal) while the subsequent will-redirect to the cross-origin target is not guarded by isInternalNavigation. Electron's own security guidance recommends gating both events identically.

**Evidence**

~~~text
hardenContents wires `contents.on('will-navigate', ...)` and `contents.setWindowOpenHandler(...)` but registers no `will-redirect` listener. A server-side or meta/JS redirect that occurs after a navigation begins is delivered via will-redirect, not will-navigate.
~~~

**Fix**

In hardenContents, also register `contents.on('will-redirect', (event, url) => { if (!isInternalNavigation(url)) { event.preventDefault(); maybeOpenExternal(url) } })`, reusing the same predicate as will-navigate.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

Read security-hardening.ts:86-97. hardenContents registers exactly two guards: contents.on('will-navigate', ...) gated by isInternalNavigation, and contents.setWindowOpenHandler(...). There is no contents.on('will-redirect', ...). Grep for 'will-redirect' across src returns zero matches, so the event is not handled anywhere else. In Electron, will-redirect is a distinct event fired for server-side (30x), meta-refresh, and renderer-initiated redirects that occur after a navigation has begun; the will-navigate listener does not catch these. Electron's own security guidance recommends gating navigation events (will-navigate AND will-redirect) identically. So the predicate isInternalNavigation does not protect against a redirect chain that lands on a cross-origin attacker URL after an initially-internal navigation. The reviewer correctly frames this as defence-in-depth: exploitation presupposes a renderer compromise (renderer runs from file:// / klip-media:// with sandbox/contextIsolation/webSecurity per the module's own docstring) and external links are already intercepted, so it is not exploitable in normal operation. The suggested fix (mirror the will-navigate handler with the same isInternalNavigation predicate + maybeOpenExternal) is correct and consistent with existing behavior.

**Verifier notes**

Real gap, correctly scoped as low/defence-in-depth. The fix should reuse the exact will-navigate body: contents.on('will-redirect', (event, url) => { if (isInternalNavigation(url)) return; event.preventDefault(); maybeOpenExternal(url) }). Note maybeOpenExternal already double-guards (http(s) + EXTERNAL_HOST_ALLOWLIST), so even the forwarded redirect target is constrained to youtube hosts вҖ” consistent with current will-navigate handling. Repro is theoretical: requires a compromised sandboxed renderer to begin an internal navigation that then 30x/meta/JS-redirects to https://evil/; will-navigate allows the initial internal URL, will-redirect (unguarded) would let the cross-origin hop proceed in-window.

---

### F51 вҖ” probe-media-file accepts an arbitrary renderer path with no rootPath containment

- **Severity:** рҹҹЎ LOW _(verifier corrected from medium)_
- **Category:** security
- **Location:** `src/main/use-cases/ProbeMediaFile.ts:17-23`
- **Confidence:** 0.7 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

The 'probe-media-file' channel is exposed end-to-end (contract -> ipc-schemas z.tuple([z.string()]) with no .max() -> preload -> DownloadController). Its handler passes the renderer-supplied path straight into ProbeMediaFile, which statSyncs it and spawns ffprobe against it. Unlike every other path-accepting channel (open-path-in-shell realpath-validates containment under rootPath; reveal-creator-folder does too), this one has NO containment check. Under the codebase's own documented threat model (renderer compromised via stored YouTube content/XSS invoking window.api.* with arbitrary payloads, per the ipc-schemas.ts header comment), a compromised renderer gets an arbitrary-file existence + size + duration/resolution oracle over the whole filesystem (e.g. probe C:/Users/<name>/... to confirm files exist and their sizes). The path is passed as a spawn arg array (not a shell), so there is no command injection, which bounds severity. No file contents leak. ffprobe error strings (e.g. 'No such file or directory') are also surfaced.

**Evidence**

~~~text
async execute(filePath: string): Promise<MediaProbeResult> {
    if (!filePath || filePath.trim().length === 0) {
      throw new Error('File path is required')
    }
    return this.mediaProbe.probe(filePath.trim())
  }  // FfprobeMediaProbe.probe then does statSync(filePath) and spawn('ffprobe', [..., filePath]) on the raw path
~~~

**Fix**

Either delete the channel (it is unused by the renderer вҖ” see the dead-channel finding) or add a realpath/prefix containment check against rootPathRef in the controller/use-case exactly like ShellController.open-path-in-shell does, and cap the schema string length (z.string().min(1).max(4096)).

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I independently verified the full chain. ipc-contract.ts:72, ipc-channels.ts:11, and ipc-schemas.ts:92 (`'probe-media-file': z.tuple([z.string()])` вҖ” no .min/.max) define the channel; preload/index.ts:23 exposes `probeMediaFile: createTypedInvoker('probe-media-file')`; DownloadController.ts:35 registers a handler that calls `probeMediaFile.execute(filePath)` with the renderer-supplied path verbatim. ProbeMediaFile.ts:17-23 only guards against empty/whitespace, then forwards the trimmed raw path to `mediaProbe.probe`. FfprobeMediaProbe.ts:27 does `statSync(filePath)` (file-existence + size oracle) and FfprobeMediaProbe.ts:34/46-62 spawns ffprobe with `-show_format -show_streams` against that path (duration/resolution oracle), and on non-zero exit rejects with `ffprobe failed (code N): <stderr>` (FfprobeMediaProbe.ts:75-77), surfacing messages like "No such file or directory" to the renderer. The asymmetry the reviewer cites is real: ShellController.ts:50-66 (`open-path-in-shell`) and :106-127 (`reveal-creator-folder`) both realpath-validate containment under `rootPath`, whereas this path-accepting channel has none. The command-injection concern is correctly ruled out вҖ” `spawn(bin, args, ...)` passes filePath as a discrete argv element with no `shell:true`, so there is no shell evaluation, and only metadata (not file contents) leaks. This bounds the impact to a filesystem-wide existence/size/media-metadata oracle reachable from a compromised renderer, which is precisely the threat model documented in ipc-schemas.ts:5-15.

**Verifier notes**

Confirmed but I'd downgrade mediumвҶ’low: (1) the channel is genuinely unused by the renderer вҖ” grep for `probeMediaFile`/`window.api.probe` across src/renderer returns zero matches, so it is dead surface area, not a live path; (2) the leak is metadata-only (existence, byte size, duration, WxH, codec) plus ffprobe stderr вҖ” no file contents, no write, no injection. It is still a real arbitrary-path oracle reachable under the codebase's own stored-XSS threat model, so it shouldn't be dismissed. Cleanest fix is the reviewer's first option: delete the channel (contract/channels/schema/preload/controller/use-case) since nothing calls it. If kept, add the same realpathSync containment check against rootPath that ShellController.open-path-in-shell uses (ProbeMediaFile would need a RootPathRef injected, or do the check in the controller), and tighten the schema to z.string().min(1).max(4096) to match open-path-in-shell. Note ProbeMediaFile.ts has no rootPath dependency today, so adding containment is a small wiring change in composition-root.ts.

---

### F52 вҖ” Preload re-exports the full @electron-toolkit electronAPI surface to the renderer

- **Severity:** рҹҹЎ LOW
- **Category:** security
- **Location:** `src/preload/index.ts:171-172`
- **Confidence:** 0.4 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** yes

**Impact**

Alongside the tightly-typed `window.api`, the preload exposes the toolkit's `electronAPI` (ipcRenderer send/invoke/on wrappers, process/versions info, webFrame helpers) as `window.electron`. This widens the renderer-reachable surface beyond the validated typed-invoker bridge: `window.electron.ipcRenderer.invoke(<channel>, ...)` lets a compromised renderer call channels directly, and while createTypedHandler's zod validation still gates every handler, the generic send/on wrappers also let the renderer emit on arbitrary channels and attach unbounded listeners. The hardening elsewhere (sandbox:true, contextIsolation:true, full IPC zod coverage) is strong, so this is a defense-in-depth narrowing rather than an exploitable hole; it was noted as acceptable in the baseline but the editor/render additions increase the channel count it transitively reaches.

**Evidence**

~~~text
contextBridge.exposeInMainWorld('electron', electronAPI)
contextBridge.exposeInMainWorld('api', api)
~~~

**Fix**

Expose only the specific toolkit helpers the renderer actually consumes (e.g. process.platform) instead of the whole electronAPI object, or drop the `window.electron` export entirely if unused. Confirm via grep that no renderer code depends on window.electron.* before removing.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

Lines 171-172 of src/preload/index.ts match the cited code exactly: `contextBridge.exposeInMainWorld('electron', electronAPI)` is present alongside the typed `window.api`. I grepped the entire renderer for `.electron`, `electron.ipcRenderer`, `electron.process` and found ZERO consumers, so the `window.electron` export is genuinely unused вҖ” the suggested-fix precondition ("confirm via grep nothing depends on it") holds. The export does widen the renderer-reachable surface: @electron-toolkit's electronAPI bundles generic `ipcRenderer.invoke/send/sendSync/on/once/removeListener`, `process`/`versions`, and `webFrame` helpers, none gated by the typed-invoker pattern. A compromised renderer (the threat model the codebase itself acknowledges in create-typed-handler.ts: "XSS via stored YouTube content") could call `window.electron.ipcRenderer.invoke(<channel>, ...)` directly instead of going through window.api. That said, this is correctly characterized as defense-in-depth narrowing, not an exploitable hole: every invoke handler is registered exclusively via createTypedHandler, which zod-validates rawArgs before dispatch (I confirmed only ipcMain.handle is used вҖ” there are no ipcMain.on listeners anywhere in src/main), so direct invoke still hits the same validation wall. The send/on portion of the claim is weaker than stated: with no ipcMain.on listeners, generic `send` has nothing to reach in main; the residual risk is webFrame access and unbounded listener attachment on push channels. The reviewer's own confidence (0.4) and "acceptable in baseline" framing are honest.

**Verifier notes**

Real but minor. The export is dead from the renderer's perspective (no consumers found), so removing `contextBridge.exposeInMainWorld('electron', electronAPI)` is a safe, zero-cost surface reduction. The strongest residual concern is webFrame helpers, not the ipcRenderer.invoke path (which remains zod-gated) nor send (no ipcMain.on listeners exist to target). Suggested fix is sound: drop window.electron entirely, or expose only process.platform if anything ever needs it. Note: the comment block at lines 161-170 discusses the deleted non-isolated fallback but does not justify keeping the electronAPI export, so this isn't documented-as-intentional in a way that refutes the finding.

---

### F53 вҖ” get-cuts-by-tags schema lacks the array/length caps applied to every sibling channel

- **Severity:** рҹҹЎ LOW
- **Category:** security
- **Location:** `src/shared/ipc-schemas.ts:140`
- **Confidence:** 0.62 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

Every other tag/array channel in this file is explicitly bounded with the stated DoS rationale: tagArraySchema = z.array(tagSchema).max(64), idArraySchema = ...max(5000), collection items .max(5000), bulk-update ids capped, etc. get-cuts-by-tags accepts an unbounded array of unbounded strings. The handler (CutController) forwards it to cutRepo.findByTags(tags), which builds a query from the array. The channel IS used by the renderer (src/renderer/hooks/use-cuts.ts), so a renderer-XSS payload (the documented threat) could pass a multi-megabyte tag array / a single huge string and amplify into an oversized SQL IN-list or string scan вҖ” the same class of issue the file's own comments justify capping against. Lower severity than the probe issue because it only stresses a read query.

**Evidence**

~~~text
'get-cuts-by-tags': z.tuple([z.array(z.string())]),
~~~

**Fix**

Use the existing tagArraySchema (or at least z.array(z.string().min(1).max(64)).max(64)) so it matches the documented cap convention.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I read src/shared/ipc-schemas.ts:140 and the quote is exact: 'get-cuts-by-tags': z.tuple([z.array(z.string())]) вҖ” an unbounded array of unbounded strings. The file's header comment (lines 5-21, 25-27, 47-52) explicitly establishes the threat model: a renderer compromised via stored-YouTube-content XSS can invoke window.api.* with arbitrary payloads, and every other array/tag channel is bounded against exactly that DoS: tagArraySchema = z.array(tagSchema).max(64) with tagSchema = z.string().min(1).max(64) (line 50-52); idArraySchema .max(5000) (51); move-videos videoIds .max(5000) (132); collection-reorder items .max(5000) (190); search-transcripts query .max(1024) (203); rename-tag-globally/delete-tag-globally use tagSchema (233-234). get-cuts-by-tags is the lone tag-array channel with no element cap and no per-string cap. The channel is genuinely wired and renderer-reachable: src/renderer/hooks/use-cuts.ts:32 calls window.api.getCutsByTags(tags); preload/index.ts:54 bridges it; CutController.ts:25-26 forwards directly to cutRepo.findByTags(tags) with no validation. In SqliteCutRepository.findByTags (lines 140-160) the tags build an IN (...) list via sql.join of one bound parameter per element against json_each(c.tags). The query is parameterized (sql`${t}`), so this is NOT SQL injection вҖ” it is the same DoS-amplification class the file's own comments cap against: a multi-megabyte tag array or a single huge string passed from an XSS'd renderer produces an oversized bound-parameter IN-list / large value scan. This is a real, self-consistent gap in the file's documented convention.

**Verifier notes**

Confirmed but correctly scoped as low. It is a read-only query, fully parameterized (no SQLi вҖ” see SqliteCutRepository.ts:143-159 using sql.join + sql`${t}`), and only exploitable from an already-compromised renderer, which is precisely the file's stated threat model. SQLite would also reject an absurd IN-list once it exceeds SQLITE_MAX_VARIABLE_NUMBER rather than truly OOM, so impact is bounded CPU/memory churn, not crash-by-design. The suggested fix is exactly the convention the file already uses elsewhere: replace z.array(z.string()) with the existing tagArraySchema (z.array(z.string().min(1).max(64)).max(64)) at line 140. Note the contract type at ipc-contract.ts:123 is string[], and the existing test tests/main/shared/ipc-schemas.test.ts:126 only asserts accept [['a','b']] / reject [[42]] вҖ” tightening to tagArraySchema won't break the contract type but the test should gain a max-length reject case.

---

### F54 вҖ” Schema table count is wrong: AGENTS.md says '9 tables', schema.ts defines 10

- **Severity:** рҹҹЎ LOW
- **Category:** spec-violation
- **Location:** `AGENTS.md:117-129`
- **Confidence:** 0.97 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

The spec's table inventory is stale вҖ” the `download_history` table (added for the persistent finished-downloads list feature) is neither in the count nor in the table. A reader trusting AGENTS.md as authoritative would not know download_history exists or what its purpose/columns are.

**Evidence**

~~~text
AGENTS.md line 117: '**9 tables** total:' and the table lists 9 rows. schema.ts has 10 `sqliteTable(...)` definitions: creators(14), videos(51), cuts(97), settings(140), operations(150), collections(185), collectionVideos(205), collectionCuts(228), auditLog(252), downloadHistory(281).
~~~

**Fix**

Update line 117 to '10 tables' and add a `download_history` row to the table describing it (soft-FK to videos.id, status success|error, retryable flag, finished_at).

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

AGENTS.md:117 reads "**9 tables** total:" and the markdown table on lines 119-129 enumerates exactly 9 rows (creators, videos, cuts, settings, operations, collections, collection_videos, collection_cuts, audit_log). schema.ts contains 10 sqliteTable definitions: creators(14), videos(51), cuts(97), settings(140), operations(150), collections(185), collectionVideos(205), collectionCuts(228), auditLog(252), and downloadHistory(281). The 10th table, download_history, is missing from both the count and the inventory. I read its definition (lines 281-304): it is a real table with a soft FK to videos.id (deliberately no references() so history survives video deletion), status text ('success'|'error'), error_retryable boolean default true, finished_at timestamp, plus youtube_url/video_title/thumbnail_url/creator_folder_name. It was added by the recent persistent finished-downloads feature (commit f8e471d). The spec is genuinely stale; this is not handled or documented elsewhere.

**Verifier notes**

Genuine doc-vs-code drift, not a runtime/security defect, so low is correct. Fix: change line 117 to "10 tables" and add a download_history row, e.g. "Persistent finished-downloads history. Soft FK вҶ’ videos.id (no ON DELETE; ListDownloadHistory filters out deleted videos on read). status = success|error, error_retryable flag, finished_at." Cited lines still match the quoted text exactly.

### F55 вҖ” Controller list in AGENTS.md is missing 3 shipped controllers (Stats, Editor, DownloadHistory)

- **Severity:** рҹҹЎ LOW
- **Category:** spec-violation
- **Location:** `AGENTS.md:101`
- **Confidence:** 0.96 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

Three shipped IPC controllers are undocumented in the authoritative spec. EditorController alone registers 5 IPC channels (editor-open-window/start-render/cancel-render/get-session/find-session-by-source). A contributor relying on AGENTS.md to discover the IPC surface would miss the entire editor + stats + download-history feature areas.

**Evidence**

~~~text
AGENTS.md:101 enumerates 13 controllers: 'ReconcileController, DownloadController, CreatorController, VideoController, CutController, TagController, SearchController, CollectionController, ShellController, SettingsController, AuditLogController, OperationController, UpdaterController.' The folder actually contains 16: also StatsController.ts, EditorController.ts, DownloadHistoryController.ts.
~~~

**Fix**

Add StatsController, EditorController, DownloadHistoryController to the line-101 list (and the parallel composition-root/use-case listings).

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

AGENTS.md:101 lists exactly 13 controllers: ReconcileController, DownloadController, CreatorController, VideoController, CutController, TagController, SearchController, CollectionController, ShellController, SettingsController, AuditLogController, OperationController, UpdaterController. The controllers/ folder (excluding node_modules) actually contains 16 files: the 13 listed plus StatsController.ts, EditorController.ts, DownloadHistoryController.ts. A contributor using AGENTS.md to discover the IPC surface would indeed miss the editor, stats, and download-history feature areas.

**Verifier notes**

Confirmed as a documentation drift / spec-accuracy gap, not a runtime bug, so low severity is appropriate. The fix should cover both the controllers list (AGENTS.md:101) AND the use-cases listing (AGENTS.md:92-98), which omits the same three feature areas' use cases (GetStorageStats, GetLibraryStats, RenderCutFromVideo, CancelRender, ListDownloadHistory, RetryDownload). Evidence trail: src/main/index.ts:19-21 (imports), :156-165 (registrations); src/main/interface-adapters/controllers/EditorController.ts:34-50 (5 channels); src/main/composition-root.ts:471-505 (stats + editor use-case wiring).

### F59 вҖ” PersistentPlayer position-tracking spec is stale: doc says 'capture-phase scroll listeners', code uses a rAF loop (which it explicitly abandoned scroll listeners for)

- **Severity:** рҹҹЎ LOW
- **Category:** spec-violation
- **Location:** `AGENTS.md:43-44`
- **Confidence:** 0.9 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

The spec documents the exact implementation strategy the code's own comments say was tried and discarded because Radix ScrollArea's viewport doesn't reliably surface scroll events (consistent with the project's documented Radix-ScrollArea-rAF gotcha). A reader fixing a player-position bug per the spec would re-add the broken scroll-listener approach.

**Evidence**

~~~text
AGENTS.md:44 'Detail mode tracks a route-owned slot rect via ResizeObserver + capture-phase scroll listeners'. PersistentPlayer.tsx:227-247 comment: 'Why a rAF loop instead of scroll/resize listeners: ... Earlier attempts to listen on window (capture phase) ... still left the player visibly stationary ... The rAF approach sidesteps the question' followed by `requestAnimationFrame(function tick() { update(); rafId = requestAnimationFrame(tick) })`. Only a ResizeObserver remains; the scroll listener was removed.
~~~

**Fix**

Reword line 44 to 'tracks a route-owned slot rect via a requestAnimationFrame loop reading getBoundingClientRect(), plus a ResizeObserver for synchronous resize updates' вҖ” remove the capture-phase scroll-listener claim.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

AGENTS.md line 43 (finding cites 43-44; the spec sentence is actually on line 43) states: "Detail mode tracks a route-owned slot rect via `ResizeObserver` + capture-phase scroll listeners". The real implementation in PersistentPlayer.tsx (lines 227-258) uses a `requestAnimationFrame` loop reading `getBoundingClientRect()` every frame, plus a `ResizeObserver` вҖ” and there is NO scroll listener. More damning, the code comment at lines 227-243 explicitly documents that the capture-phase scroll-listener approach was tried and discarded: "Earlier attempts to listen on `window` (capture phase) ... both still left the player visibly stationary while the content scrolled underneath ... radix's viewport implementation has bitten us here before. The rAF approach sidesteps the question entirely". This is also consistent with the project's documented Radix-ScrollArea-rAF gotcha in user memory. So the spec documents the exact strategy the code abandoned. A reader fixing a player-position bug per the spec would re-add the broken scroll-listener approach. The finding is real; the "capture-phase scroll listeners" half of the spec sentence is stale and actively misleading.

**Verifier notes**

Severity low is appropriate вҖ” it is a doc-vs-code drift, not a runtime bug. Minor correction to the finding: the quoted spec sentence is on AGENTS.md line 43, not line 44. The ResizeObserver part of the spec is still accurate (it remains in code at line 252 for synchronous resize updates); only the "capture-phase scroll listeners" clause is wrong and should be replaced with "a requestAnimationFrame loop reading getBoundingClientRect()" as the reviewer suggests.

### F60 вҖ” klip-media protocol privileges in AGENTS.md omit stream:true (required for <video>)

- **Severity:** рҹҹЎ LOW
- **Category:** spec-violation
- **Location:** `AGENTS.md:63`
- **Confidence:** 0.85 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

The doc's privilege object is missing `stream: true` (and `standard: false`). Per the project's own hard-won note, a custom scheme without `stream: true` makes <video> fail with SRC_NOT_SUPPORTED even with correct MIME/codecs вҖ” the rendered player at line 84 reads klip-media://video/<id>/file. A contributor copying the spec's snippet into a refactor would silently break video playback.

**Evidence**

~~~text
AGENTS.md:63 shows `protocol.registerSchemesAsPrivileged([{ scheme: 'klip-media', privileges: { secure: true, supportFetchAPI: true } }])`. index.ts:47-57 actually registers `{ standard: false, secure: true, supportFetchAPI: true, stream: true }`.
~~~

**Fix**

Update the line-63 snippet to include `standard: false` and `stream: true` to match index.ts, and note in the CSP/protocol section that stream:true is load-bearing for <video>.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I read both cited locations. AGENTS.md:63 literally documents the privilege object as `protocol.registerSchemesAsPrivileged([{ scheme: 'klip-media', privileges: { secure: true, supportFetchAPI: true } }])` вҖ” omitting both `standard: false` and `stream: true`. The actual registration in src/main/index.ts:47-57 is `{ standard: false, secure: true, supportFetchAPI: true, stream: true }`. So the doc snippet is genuinely incomplete relative to the code.

This matters because AGENTS.md:84 itself states the rendered `<video>` element reads from `klip-media://video/<id>/file` "handled as a privileged secure scheme." Per the project's own hard-won memory note (feedback_custom_protocol_stream_privilege.md), a custom scheme without `stream: true` causes `<video>` to fail with SRC_NOT_SUPPORTED even with correct MIME/codecs. A contributor copying the line-63 snippet verbatim into a refactor would silently break video playback while thumbnails/images (which don't need range streaming) keep working вҖ” a subtle, hard-to-diagnose regression.

This is a documentation/spec drift, not a runtime bug вҖ” the live code is correct. So it's an accuracy defect in AGENTS.md, not in the application.

**Verifier notes**

Confirmed but it is purely a doc-accuracy issue (the running code at src/main/index.ts:47-57 is correct), so 'low' is the right severity вҖ” no user-facing defect today. Sharper repro/fix: update the AGENTS.md:63 inline snippet to `privileges: { standard: false, secure: true, supportFetchAPI: true, stream: true }` and add a one-line note in the CSP/protocol section (around line 84) that `stream: true` is load-bearing for `<video>` range requests, cross-referencing the existing rationale. The reviewer's evidence quotes are accurate to the current files.
