### F61 вҖ” getItems performs no renumber-on-read despite AGENTS spec and schema comments claiming it does

- **Severity:** рҹҹЎ LOW
- **Category:** spec-violation
- **Location:** `src/main/interface-adapters/repositories/SqliteCollectionRepository.ts:109-128`
- **Confidence:** 0.8 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

AGENTS.md line 131 states the unified position invariant is enforced '... with a defensive renumber-on-read in getItems', and schema.ts line 175 repeats 'defensive renumber-on-read in getItems'. The actual getItems only SELECTs ordered by position; it never renumbers or repairs gaps/collisions. If positions ever become duplicated or sparse (e.g. a future raw-SQL writer, a partial reorder, or a bug in the two-phase shift), getItems silently returns them in an unstable order (ORDER BY position with ties is not deterministic across kinds) and the documented self-healing does not happen. Today the write paths keep the invariant, so impact is limited, but the safety net the spec promises does not exist.

**Evidence**

~~~text
getItems(collectionId: string): CollectionItem[] {
    // ... we render straight from the array ...
    const rows = this.db.all(sql`... UNION ALL ... ORDER BY position ASC`) as Array<...>
    return rows
  }
~~~

**Fix**

Either implement the renumber-on-read (detect non-contiguous/duplicate positions and rewrite 0..n-1, mirroring reorderItems), or update AGENTS.md line 131 and schema.ts line 175 to remove the 'defensive renumber-on-read in getItems' claim so the docs match reality. Also add a secondary ORDER BY (e.g. addedAt, id) tiebreaker so ties are deterministic.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I read SqliteCollectionRepository.ts:109-128. getItems builds a UNION ALL across collection_videos and collection_cuts, applies a single `ORDER BY position ASC`, and returns the rows unchanged. There is no detection of duplicate/sparse positions and no rewrite вҖ” it is a pure read. AGENTS.md:131 states the invariant is enforced "...with a defensive renumber-on-read in `getItems`" and schema.ts:174-175 repeats "(with a defensive renumber-on-read in `getItems`)". Neither matches the implementation; the actual self-healing/renumbering logic lives only in reorderItems (two-phase shift, lines 154-203), not getItems. So the docs over-promise a safety net that does not exist. The determinism sub-point is also real: getItems has no secondary sort key, whereas the sibling findPaginated (line 66) deliberately adds `desc(collections.id)` as a tiebreaker and comments on why вҖ” so ties on position are not deterministically ordered in getItems. Impact is genuinely low: today's only write paths (AddToCollection / ReorderCollection via transactionScope.run + the two-phase shift) keep positions unique and contiguous, so duplicates/gaps don't arise in practice. This is a doc-vs-code spec violation, not a live bug.

**Verifier notes**

Two valid remediations, matching the reviewer's suggestion: (1) implement the renumber-on-read in getItems (detect non-contiguous/duplicate positions, rewrite 0..n-1 mirroring reorderItems), or (2) the lighter fix вҖ” strike "with a defensive renumber-on-read in `getItems`" from AGENTS.md:131, schema.ts:174-175, and the misleading reference at schema.ts:181 ("the existing renumber-on-read ... in reorderItems" вҖ” reorderItems renumbers on WRITE, not read). Independently worth adding a secondary ORDER BY tiebreaker (addedAt, id) to getItems for deterministic ordering on position ties, consistent with findPaginated which already does this. Note schema.ts:177-183 (AUDIT-2026-05-02) already acknowledges the only real exposure is a future raw-SQL/multi-process writer, reinforcing low severity.

---

### F62 вҖ” Transcript writes bypass the audited video repository and mutate videos.updated_at directly

- **Severity:** рҹҹЎ LOW
- **Category:** spec-violation
- **Location:** `src/main/interface-adapters/repositories/SqliteVideoTranscriptIndex.ts:86-91`
- **Confidence:** 0.7 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

AGENTS.md rule #10 (line 496) requires all mutations on `videos` to go through the audited repository decorators. setTranscriptText issues a raw UPDATE on the videos table (writing transcript_text and bumping updated_at) directly on the better-sqlite3 handle, outside any AuditedVideoRepository wrapper and outside ITransactionScope. The FTS triggers still fire (so search stays consistent), but the audit_log gets no entry and updated_at moves underneath the audited repo's view of state. If a use case reads `previous` via the audited repo and later upserts, the bumped updated_at is invisible to the diff (updatedAt is skipped anyway), so the practical harm is only the missing/ungoverned mutation path, not data corruption.

**Evidence**

~~~text
setTranscriptText(videoId: string, text: string | null): void {
    const stmt = this.raw.prepare(`UPDATE videos SET transcript_text = ?, updated_at = ? WHERE id = ?`)
    stmt.run(text, new Date().toISOString(), videoId)
  }
~~~

**Fix**

Route transcript_text writes through an IVideoRepository method (e.g. videoRepo.updateTranscriptText) wrapped by the audited decorator, or explicitly document this table as an audit-exempt secondary index in AGENTS.md so the rule and code agree.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I read SqliteVideoTranscriptIndex.ts:86-91 and the cited code is exactly as quoted: setTranscriptText runs `UPDATE videos SET transcript_text = ?, updated_at = ? WHERE id = ?` directly on the injected better-sqlite3 handle (`this.raw`), with no ITransactionScope.run wrapper and no audit_log append. AGENTS.md rule #10 (line 496) does state "All mutations on `creators`, `videos`, and `cuts` go through audited repository decorators, which automatically write to the `audit_log` table." This is a genuine mutation on the videos table outside the AuditedVideoRepository decorator (AuditedVideoRepository.ts wraps every IVideoRepository mutation in transaction.run + auditLog.append; this index is a separate port not covered by it). So the spec violation is real.

I confirmed transcript_text is genuinely a videos column with a second, audited write path: it is part of the Video entity (Video.ts:26) and is written through SqliteVideoRepository.upsert (lines 214, 244) via the audited decorator. So two paths mutate the same column, and only this one (the index/backfill path) escapes auditing. transcript_text is NOT in ENRICHMENT_ONLY_FIELDS, so an audited transcript change would normally produce an "updated" audit entry вҖ” meaning this path does omit an audit entry the governed path would emit.

The reviewer's harm analysis is accurate and appropriately modest: updatedAt is filtered out of audit diffs (diffObjects skips it, per AuditedVideoRepository.ts:13 comment), so the bumped updated_at causes no diff corruption; the FTS triggers fire on the raw UPDATE so search stays consistent. The only real consequences are (a) the rule-vs-code mismatch and (b) a missing audit_log entry. The sole caller is BackfillTranscriptIndex (a boot-time, system-initiated operation), so the missing audit entry is arguably acceptable noise-reduction rather than a defect вҖ” which is why this is low, not higher.

**Verifier notes**

Confirmed. Cited lines still match verbatim. Sole caller: src/main/use-cases/BackfillTranscriptIndex.ts:41 (boot-time backfill). The same column is also written through the audited path (SqliteVideoRepository.ts:214/244 via upsert), so there are two write paths; only the index path is unaudited. No data-corruption risk (FTS triggers fire; updatedAt is filtered from audit diffs per AuditedVideoRepository.ts:13). Real issue is the AGENTS.md rule #10 vs code mismatch plus a missing audit entry. The reviewer's suggested fix is reasonable: either route through an audited IVideoRepository.updateTranscriptText, or вҖ” given backfill is system-initiated вҖ” document the FTS index as an audit-exempt secondary writer in AGENTS.md so rule and code agree. Lean toward the documentation fix since auditing system backfill adds little value.

---

### F63 вҖ” OperationDto.payload leaks serialized filesystem paths across the IPC boundary

- **Severity:** рҹҹЎ LOW
- **Category:** spec-violation
- **Location:** `src/shared/dtos/OperationDto.ts:2-11`
- **Confidence:** 0.6 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

AGENTS.md (klip-media design, lines 69-82) states DTOs must not expose raw filesystem paths and only flag presence; the dto-mappers.ts header restates this. OperationController.ts returns the domain Operation entity verbatim (no DTO mapping), and Operation.payload is documented in src/main/domain/entities/Operation.ts as 'JSON-serialized operation-specific data (old/new paths, progress checkpoints)'. For a migrate_root / rename_folder operation, payload therefore carries absolute source/destination paths to the renderer вҖ” the exact path leakage the design forbids. Impact is currently latent because the two operation channels are not consumed by any renderer code (see orphan finding), but the surface is exposed and a future operations UI would surface raw paths.

**Evidence**

~~~text
export interface OperationDto {
  id: string
  type: string
  status: string
  payload: string  // OperationController returns operationRepo.findById(id) directly; Operation.payload is 'JSON-serialized operation-specific data (old/new paths, progress checkpoints)'
~~~

**Fix**

If the channels are kept, map through a real DTO that redacts/omits payload (or returns only the structured progress fields the UI needs) instead of returning the entity directly; otherwise delete the channels.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I read OperationDto.ts, Operation.ts, OperationController.ts, MigrateRootFolder.ts, dto-mappers.ts, ipc-contract.ts, the preload bridge, and grepped renderer consumers. The finding holds: (1) OperationDto.payload is a raw `string` (the JSON-serialized Operation.payload). (2) OperationController.registerOperationController returns `operationRepo.findById(id)` and `findByStatus(status)` verbatim вҖ” there is NO DTO mapper for operations (the Operation entity and OperationDto are structurally identical, so the entity passes the type check unchanged). (3) MigrateRootFolder builds `MigrateRootPayload { oldRoot, newRoot, folders, moves[] }` where oldRoot/newRoot are absolute filesystem paths and serializes it into Operation.payload via JSON.stringify (lines 107-126, 145, 283-288). So a `get-operation-by-id` for a migrate_root operation would return those absolute paths to the renderer. (4) dto-mappers.ts header (lines 9-14) explicitly states the boundary mappers strip filesystem paths and that 'the renderer never holds a raw filesystem path'; the operation channels bypass that mapper entirely, contradicting the stated invariant. (5) No renderer code calls getOperationById/getOperationsByStatus (grep of src/renderer returned zero hits), confirming the exposure is currently latent. Two caveats that bound severity: the cited AGENTS.md range (lines 69-82) is the Local Media Protocol section, which targets attacker-controlled metadata paths (filePath/thumbnailPath/profileImagePath) served via klip-media://, not operation saga payloads вҖ” so the exact citation is slightly mismatched, though the general DTO-strips-paths principle (line 82 + dto-mappers header) does apply. And the leaked paths are user-chosen root directories, not attacker-controlled, so this is an architectural-consistency / information-hygiene issue rather than an exploitable path-traversal vector.

**Verifier notes**

Real but latent and low-impact. Repro: invoke window.api.getOperationById(<id of a migrate_root op>); the returned OperationDto.payload is JSON containing absolute oldRoot/newRoot paths. The leak is purely in the unmapped controller вҖ” every other read controller maps through dto-mappers.ts which strips paths; operations were never given a mapper because OperationDto === Operation shape. Severity stays low: (a) no renderer consumes these two channels today, (b) the paths are user-selected root dirs, not attacker-controlled, so there's no traversal escalation. Fix per reviewer is sound: either add toOperationDto that omits/redacts payload (or surfaces only structured progress fields), or delete the orphan channels. Note the AGENTS.md line citation (69-82) points at the Local Media Protocol section rather than a generic DTO rule; the load-bearing reference is dto-mappers.ts:9-14 plus the design principle at AGENTS.md:82.

---

### F64 вҖ” AppUserModelID ('com.electron') diverges from the electron-builder appId ('com.electron.app')

- **Severity:** рҹҹЎ LOW
- **Category:** weird-logic
- **Location:** `src/main/index.ts:82`
- **Confidence:** 0.7 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

On Windows the AppUserModelID must match the installed app's identity for taskbar pinning and toast notifications to attribute correctly to the app. Setting it to 'com.electron' while the NSIS-installed app registers 'com.electron.app' means notifications (including the auto-update ready toast surfaced via OS-level paths) and taskbar grouping can be mis-attributed. Cosmetic/identity issue, not a crash, and the boilerplate default was simply never updated to the real appId.

**Evidence**

~~~text
index.ts: `electronApp.setAppUserModelId('com.electron')` vs electron-builder.yml line 1 `appId: com.electron.app` (also documented in AGENTS.md line 705 as 'app ID is `com.electron.app`').
~~~

**Fix**

Call electronApp.setAppUserModelId('com.electron.app') (or, better, app.getName()/the appId from build config) so the runtime model id matches the installer appId. Also consider giving the app a non-placeholder appId before release.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I read all three cited locations and they match the reviewer's quotes exactly. src/main/index.ts:82 (inside app.whenReady, with the comment "Set app user model id for windows") calls electronApp.setAppUserModelId('com.electron'). electron-builder.yml:1 declares appId: com.electron.app. AGENTS.md:705 documents the app ID as com.electron.app. So the runtime AppUserModelID ('com.electron') genuinely diverges from the installed/NSIS app identity ('com.electron.app'). On Windows the AUMID governs taskbar grouping/pinning and toast-notification attribution, and Microsoft's guidance is that it must match the app's registered identity. The mismatch means notifications and taskbar grouping can be attributed to a phantom 'com.electron' identity rather than the real app. This is not handled anywhere else вҖ” it is the only setAppUserModelId call (the @electron-toolkit boilerplate default was left unchanged), and there is no compensating logic. The auto-updater is present (electron-builder.yml publish block + AGENTS.md:706), so an OS-surfaced update toast would inherit the wrong AUMID. Confirmed as a genuine cosmetic/identity defect, not a false positive.

**Verifier notes**

Repro: build the NSIS installer (registers AUMID com.electron.app), run the app, and trigger a Windows toast or pin to taskbar вҖ” Windows keys off the runtime AUMID 'com.electron' set at index.ts:82, which does not match the installed identity, so grouping/attribution is wrong. Fix: setAppUserModelId('com.electron.app') or derive it from the build appId. Note the appId itself is still the placeholder 'com.electron.app' (flagged in AGENTS.md and worth a real reverse-DNS id before release), but that is a separate concern from the divergence this finding correctly identifies. Severity low is right вҖ” no crash, purely identity/cosmetic.

---

### F65 вҖ” get-operations-by-status casts an unvalidated string to OperationStatus at the boundary

- **Severity:** рҹҹЎ LOW
- **Category:** weird-logic
- **Location:** `src/main/interface-adapters/controllers/OperationController.ts:17-19`
- **Confidence:** 0.6 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

The zod schema for this channel is z.tuple([z.string()]) вҖ” any string passes validation вҖ” and the controller then `status as OperationStatus`-casts it, defeating the 'malformed payloads reject before reaching the use case' invariant the whole createTypedHandler/ipc-schemas design exists to enforce. An arbitrary status string reaches the repository query. Impact is benign today (an unknown status just yields an empty result and the channel is unused), but it is an unsound cast that contradicts the file-wide validation contract and would matter if findByStatus ever branched on the value.

**Evidence**

~~~text
createTypedHandler('get-operations-by-status', async (_event, status) => {
    return operationRepo.findByStatus(status as OperationStatus)
  })
~~~

**Fix**

Tighten the schema to z.tuple([z.enum(['pending','in_progress','completed','failed','rolled_back'])]) so the cast becomes sound, mirroring how entityStatusSchema and the kind enums are handled elsewhere.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

Verified all cited facts against the real code. OperationController.ts:17-19 reads exactly `createTypedHandler('get-operations-by-status', async (_event, status) => { return operationRepo.findByStatus(status as OperationStatus) })`. The channel schema in src/shared/ipc-schemas.ts:251 is `'get-operations-by-status': z.tuple([z.string()])`, so any string passes validation, and the controller then casts that unvalidated string to OperationStatus. OperationStatus (src/main/domain/entities/Operation.ts:2) is a strict 5-member union ('pending' | 'in_progress' | 'completed' | 'failed' | 'rolled_back'), so the cast is genuinely unsound вҖ” an arbitrary status reaches findByStatus. The reviewer's consistency argument holds: the same file validates every other status/kind field with z.enum (entityStatusSchema = z.enum(['active','deleted','missing']) at line 23; z.enum(['video','cut']) at lines 75, 169, 212, 223), so this channel is the lone unsound boundary. Impact is correctly characterized as benign today: findByStatus (SqliteOperationRepository.ts:31-38) passes the value into a parameterized Drizzle `eq(operations.status, status)` query вҖ” no SQL injection вҖ” and an unknown status simply returns []. The channel is wired through preload (preload/index.ts:104, preload/index.d.ts:148) but I found no renderer code actually invoking getOperationsByStatus, so it's effectively unused application-side. The fix (z.tuple([z.enum([...5 values...])])) would make the cast sound and matches existing patterns.

**Verifier notes**

Confirmed but correctly low-impact. No injection risk: findByStatus uses Drizzle's parameterized `eq(operations.status, status)`; an unknown status yields an empty array, not an error. Channel is exposed via preload but I found no renderer call site, so the unsound path is latent. The value of fixing is contract-consistency (every sibling status/kind field in ipc-schemas.ts already uses z.enum) and future-proofing if findByStatus or callers ever branch on the value. Suggested fix is correct; could DRY by reusing a shared operationStatusSchema = z.enum([...]) mirrored from the OperationStatus union.

### F66 вҖ” findPaginated computes count and rows as two unsynchronized queries; total can disagree with the returned page

- **Severity:** рҹҹЎ LOW
- **Category:** weird-logic
- **Location:** `src/main/interface-adapters/repositories/SqliteVideoRepository.ts:345-365`
- **Confidence:** 0.5 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

Every findPaginated (videos, cuts, creators, collections) issues a separate COUNT(*) and a separate SELECT, neither wrapped in a transaction/snapshot. better-sqlite3 is synchronous and single-threaded so a single findPaginated call cannot interleave with another writer mid-method; the realistic risk is only that total reflects a slightly different instant than the rows when interspersed with background writes across calls. Impact is cosmetic (a page total that's momentarily off by a row, possibly an empty last page). Documenting rather than alarming вҖ” it is not a data-loss or crash issue.

**Evidence**

~~~text
const [{ count }] = this.db.select({ count: sql<number>`count(*)` }).from(videos).where(where).all()
    ...
    const rows = this.db.select().from(videos).where(where).orderBy(...).limit(params.pageSize).offset(offset).all()
~~~

**Fix**

Acceptable as-is for a single-process sync driver; if exactness matters, run both selects inside one transactionScope.run() so they observe the same snapshot. No change strictly required.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I read SqliteVideoRepository.ts:326-366. The cited code is exact: findPaginated issues a standalone COUNT(*) via `.all()` (lines 345-349) and a separate SELECT via `.all()` (lines 356-363), with no transactionScope/transaction wrapper (grep for transaction in this file returns nothing). So the two queries are not snapshot-synchronized. The reviewer's technical framing is correct and unusually honest: better-sqlite3 is synchronous and single-threaded, so a single findPaginated invocation cannot be interleaved by another writer mid-method вҖ” there is no race within the call. The only real effect is that if a background write commits between the COUNT and the SELECT, `total` can reflect a slightly different instant than `rows` (e.g. a deleted/inserted row), yielding a total off by one or a momentarily empty last page. This is cosmetic, not a data-loss or crash issue. The pattern repeats across the other repositories' findPaginated methods as claimed. The suggested fix (wrap both in one transactionScope.run() if exactness matters; otherwise leave as-is) is sound and the reviewer correctly states no change is strictly required.

**Verifier notes**

Confirmed but genuinely minor вҖ” effectively an info/documentation note, and the reviewer already presents it that way with 0.5 confidence. No transaction wrapper exists anywhere in this method (verified by grep). The cosmetic symptom requires a concurrent write to land in the tiny window between the two synchronous .all() calls, which for a single-process desktop Electron app is rare. Keeping at low rather than promoting; could equally be info. If the user wants exactness, the fix is trivial: wrap both selects in one transactionScope.run() so they observe the same SQLite snapshot.

---

### F67 вҖ” Duplicate detection only fires for status==='active'; recoverable/missing duplicates re-download into a fresh row

- **Severity:** рҹҹЎ LOW
- **Category:** weird-logic
- **Location:** `src/main/use-cases/DownloadVideo.ts:180-208, 252-283`
- **Confidence:** 0.55 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

The dedupe guard is deliberately narrow (active + file present) so missing/deleted rows can be repaired by re-download вҖ” that part is fine. But when an existing row is 'missing' or 'deleted' (different creator slug than before), the fall-through upsert keys solely on videos.id (=videoId) and rewrites creatorId to the CURRENT download's folderName. If the user re-downloads under a different creator name, the video silently jumps creators and the old creator loses it, with no audit/move trail. Combined with the FK finding, if the original creator was UUID-keyed the rewrite can also break the FK. Worth confirming intended behavior for the cross-creator re-download case.

**Evidence**

~~~text
const existing = this.videoRepo.findByYoutubeVideoId(videoId); if (existing && existing.status === 'active' && this.fsReader.fileExists(existing.filePath)) { ... status: 'duplicate' ... return } ... later unconditionally: const video: Video = { id: videoId, creatorId: folderName, ... status: 'active' }; this.videoRepo.upsert(video)
~~~

**Fix**

On the recovery/upsert path, preserve the existing row's creatorId (don't let a re-download silently reassign creator), or route the change through the explicit move-videos flow so it is audited.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I read DownloadVideo.ts, SqliteVideoRepository.ts, schema.ts, RegisterCreator.ts, and the DownloadVideo tests. The quoted code is accurate and current.

1) Dedupe guard (line 181) fires only for `existing.status === 'active' && fileExists`. The comment (lines 176-179) and tests ("proceeds with download when the existing video is missing/deleted") confirm the narrowness is an intentional recovery design. That part is fine.

2) On the fall-through, lines 254-283 build the Video with `creatorId: folderName` (slugify of the CURRENT download's creatorName) and call `videoRepo.upsert(video)`.

3) SqliteVideoRepository.upsert (lines 221-224) uses `onConflictDoUpdate({ target: videos.id, set: { creatorId: sql\`excluded.creator_id\`, ... } })`. So a re-download of a `missing`/`deleted` row under a DIFFERENT creator name keys on videos.id (=videoId) and overwrites creatorId. The video silently jumps creators; the old creator loses it. Confirmed.

4) FK angle is also real: schema.ts line 55-57 makes videos.creator_id reference creators.id (onDelete cascade). DownloadVideo always writes the slug as creatorId, but RegisterCreator.ts line 67 sets creator.id = idGenerator.generate() (UUID) with folderName as a separate field. So for a registered-then-downloaded creator, the slug the upsert writes is NOT a valid creators.id and the FK can break. This is the SAME pre-existing folderName-vs-UUID mismatch already acknowledged as out-of-scope in ensureCreator's own comment (lines 371-377), so this finding stacks on a known issue rather than being wholly new.

One correction to the claim: it is NOT true that there is "no audit trail." DownloadVideo is wired with AuditedVideoRepository (composition-root.ts line 308/358), whose upsert writes a field-level diff inside a transaction. The creatorId change WOULD be captured as a generic update diff вҖ” just not as a semantic "move" event. So the auditing gap is about semantics/move-flow routing, not a total absence of a trail.

**Verifier notes**

Repro: have video V (id=abc123) under creator "Alice" (folderName alice). Mark it missing/deleted (e.g. file removed + reconcile, or soft-delete). Re-paste the same URL but type creator name "Bob". Dedupe is skipped (status != active), download proceeds, and upsert rewrites videos.creator_id from 'alice' to 'bob'. V now belongs to Bob; Alice's library loses it, with only a low-level field-diff audit entry (not a move event).

Severity 'low' is appropriate: the path requires an uncommon user action (re-downloading an already-known-but-missing/deleted video while deliberately typing a different creator name), and the FK-break sub-case only triggers for RegisterCreator-created (UUID-keyed) creators, which is the separately-tracked, already-acknowledged folderName-vs-UUID issue (CLAUDE memory: "Creator.id != Creator.folderName").

Suggested fix stands: on the recovery/upsert path, preserve existing.creatorId (read `existing` is already in scope at line 180) instead of hardcoding folderName, OR route a deliberate creator change through an explicit, audited move-videos flow. The reviewer's claim of "no audit/move trail" should be softened to "no semantic move trail."

---

### F68 вҖ” Cancelled download leaves partial .part file and output dir with no cleanup or history of the file

- **Severity:** рҹҹЎ LOW
- **Category:** weird-logic
- **Location:** `src/main/use-cases/DownloadVideo.ts:301-318`
- **Confidence:** 0.55 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

On cancel, performDownload records a non-retryable history row and returns, but the partially-written <outputDir>/<videoId>.part (and the empty download dir) are left on disk with no DB row referencing them. yt-dlp's --continue/--no-overwrites means a later identical download resumes the .part (intended), but a cancel the user never resumes accumulates orphaned partial files under <root>/<creator>/downloads/<videoId>/. Reconciliation keys on completed media, so these partials are not surfaced or GC'd. String-matching error.message === 'Download cancelled' is also brittle (any wrapped/re-thrown error loses the exact string and would fall through to the generic error path).

**Evidence**

~~~text
if (error instanceof Error && error.message === 'Download cancelled') { this.appendHistory({ ... status: 'error', errorMessage: 'Download cancelled.', errorRetryable: false }); return }  вҖ” no fsWriter cleanup of outputDir/.part.
~~~

**Fix**

Either best-effort remove the empty output dir on cancel (when no completed media exists) or have reconciliation sweep stale .part-only download dirs. Consider signalling cancellation via a typed error/flag rather than message string-matching.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

Read DownloadVideo.ts:301-318, YtDlpDownloader.ts:430-515, and ReconcileDirectory.ts in full. The chain holds: (1) yt-dlp is invoked with `--continue --no-overwrites` (YtDlpDownloader.ts:456-457) and `-o ${outputDir}/${videoId}.%(ext)s` (line 465), where outputDir = <root>/<folderName>/downloads/<videoId> (DownloadVideo.ts:217-223). An interrupted run leaves `<videoId>.<ext>.part`. (2) On cancel the process is SIGTERM'd and the driver rejects with literally `new Error('Download cancelled')` (line 500), so the string compare at DownloadVideo.ts:303 matches today. (3) The cancel branch (303-318) only calls appendHistory({status:'error', videoId:null, errorRetryable:false}) and returns вҖ” there is no fsWriter call, no removal of outputDir or the .part file. (4) Reconciliation does not GC it: upsertVideoFromDisk returns early when no final muxed media file exists (`if (!mediaFile) return`, line 390; the regex FINAL_FILE_RE excludes `.part`), and reconcileVideos/discoverVideos only ever add or recover dirs that contain a final media file вҖ” they never delete `.part`-only dirs. So a cancel-without-retry leaves an orphaned partial dir with no DB row referencing the file, never surfaced and never collected. The brittleness claim is also valid: the guard is a raw message-string equality, so any wrap/re-throw of the cancellation error loses the exact string and falls through to the generic error path (which would mislabel the cancel as a real failure and possibly mark it retryable via classifyDownloadError).

**Verifier notes**

Confirmed but genuinely low-impact and partly intended. The leftover .part is the designed resume artifact for --continue, and it's bounded: one .part per cancelled-and-never-retried video, reused if the user re-downloads the same video. A cancel DOES leave a download_history row (just with videoId:null / no file path), so it's not invisible to the user. Net cost is bounded orphaned disk usage, not corruption or a crash. Sharper repro: download a video, cancel mid-download, never retry that exact URL вҖ” `<root>/<creator>/downloads/<videoId>/<videoId>.<ext>.part` (plus possibly .info.json/.jpg sidecars from --write-info-json/--write-thumbnail) remain forever; run reconcile and confirm videosAdded does not count it (upsertVideoFromDisk early-returns at line 390). Suggested fixes are reasonable: best-effort remove the output dir on cancel when no completed media exists, or have reconcile sweep media-less downloads/<id> dirs; and replace the message-string match with a typed CancellationError / sentinel flag so a wrapped error can't fall through to the retriable-error path. Note the cancel branch also re-slugifies creatorName for creatorFolderName instead of reusing the already-computed folderName, a minor secondary smell.

### F69 вҖ” Cut with no media file is catalogued with filePath = cutDir (a directory), permanently failing probe

- **Severity:** рҹҹЎ LOW
- **Category:** weird-logic
- **Location:** `src/main/use-cases/ReconcileDirectory.ts:488-519`
- **Confidence:** 0.58 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

Unlike upsertVideoFromDisk (which returns early at line 390 when no media file is present, deliberately refusing to catalogue a not-yet-complete download), upsertCutFromDisk inserts the cut anyway with filePath pointing at the cut DIRECTORY when no .mp4/.mkv/.webm exists. EnrichMediaMetadata then runs ffprobe against a directory path, which fails and sets probeStatus='failed' forever; reconcileCuts only touches status (line 440-445) so it never re-flips to 'pending' when the real media file later lands. The cut row also points at an unplayable path. This is the exact mid-write race the video path guards against, left open for cuts.

**Evidence**

~~~text
const mediaFile = files.find((f) => /\.(mp4|mkv|webm)$/i.test(f)) ?? null
    ...
      filePath: mediaFile ? this.path.join(cutDir, mediaFile) : cutDir,
~~~

**Fix**

Mirror the video path: if no media file is found, either skip cataloguing (return early) or leave probeStatus so a later reconcile re-probes once the rendered file appears. Don't store a directory as filePath.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

Verified the asymmetry directly. In upsertVideoFromDisk, line 390 `if (!mediaFile) return` deliberately refuses to catalogue a directory with no final media file (extensively commented as the mid-download race guard). In upsertCutFromDisk, line 514 `filePath: mediaFile ? this.path.join(cutDir, mediaFile) : cutDir` instead inserts the row with the cut DIRECTORY as filePath, probeStatus:'pending' (line 516). EnrichMediaMetadata.execute (line 56) then calls mediaProbe.probe(cut.filePath) against that directory; ffprobe throws and line 71 sets probeStatus='failed'. The re-probe gate is permanent: EnrichMediaMetadata only queries findByProbeStatus('pending') (line 26), never 'failed'. And reconcileCuts (lines 440-451) / discoverCuts (lines 465-472) only call updateStatus for existing cut rows and `continue` on findById hits вҖ” they never re-upsert from disk, so neither filePath nor probeStatus is ever refreshed once the rendered file lands. Net: the cut is permanently catalogued with an unplayable directory path and a stuck 'failed' probe. One refinement to the reviewer's framing: the dominant cut-creation path is the in-app render (RenderCutFromVideo), which inserts the Cut row up front (line 177) BEFORE the file lands, so discoverCuts sees the row and skips upsertCutFromDisk entirely вҖ” that path is NOT affected. The directory-as-filePath bug is reachable only for SIDELOADED cut folders (a folder with cut-data.json but no media yet) or a watcher firing mid-sideload-copy. Sideloading is an explicitly supported convention (the code itself comments on 'manual sideload convention' at line 489 and 'a sideloaded folder produced by an older klip' at line 497), so the path is genuinely reachable, just narrower than the video analogue.

**Verifier notes**

Confirmed but correctly scoped as low. Repro: drop a cut folder into <root>/<creator>/cuts/<cutId>/ containing only cut-data.json (no .mp4/.mkv/.webm) вҖ” e.g. mid-copy during a manual sideload, or a partially-copied folder. Reconcile's discoverCuts finds no DB row, calls upsertCutFromDisk, which sets filePath=cutDir. EnrichMediaMetadata probes the directory, fails, sets probeStatus='failed' forever. Even when the real media file is later copied in, no code path re-upserts the row (reconcile only updateStatus's existing rows; Enrich only re-scans 'pending'), so filePath stays pointing at the directory and the cut is unplayable + never re-probed. Not reachable via the in-app render path (RenderCutFromVideo inserts the row up front at finalPath, so discoverCuts skips it). Suggested fix stands: mirror the video early-return (`if (!mediaFile) return`) in upsertCutFromDisk so an incomplete sideload is left for a later reconcile pass once the rendered file appears, and never store a directory as filePath. Severity low because (a) the only trigger is manual sideloading mid-copy, not the primary editor flow, and (b) impact is a single stuck/unplayable cut row, no data loss or crash.

---

### F70 вҖ” RemoveFromCollection leaves position gaps and never renumbers вҖ” diverges from the documented renumber-on-read invariant

- **Severity:** рҹҹЎ LOW
- **Category:** weird-logic
- **Location:** `src/main/use-cases/RemoveFromCollection.ts:12-25`
- **Confidence:** 0.55 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

Removing the item at position 2 from positions [0,1,2,3] leaves [0,1,3]; nothing renumbers the survivors and getItems (SqliteCollectionRepository.getItems) returns raw positions ordered by position, so the gap persists indefinitely. AddToCollection then computes max+1, so ordering and the cross-table uniqueness invariant are not broken (no correctness bug), but the use-case prompt's stated 'renumber-on-read' invariant is not actually implemented anywhere вҖ” getItems returns the stored, gapped positions verbatim. Any future code that assumes positions are a dense 0..n-1 sequence (e.g. index-based logic) would be wrong.

**Evidence**

~~~text
if (request.kind === 'video') {
  this.collectionRepo.removeVideo(request.collectionId, request.id)
} else {
  this.collectionRepo.removeCut(request.collectionId, request.id)
}
~~~

**Fix**

Either compact positions on remove (renumber survivors inside a transaction) or implement the documented renumber-on-read in getItems so callers always see dense 0..n-1 positions. At minimum, correct the spec/comment to state positions are sparse-but-monotonic.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I read RemoveFromCollection.ts (lines 12-25), AddToCollection.ts, ReorderCollection.ts, and SqliteCollectionRepository.ts. RemoveFromCollection deletes the join row via removeVideo/removeCut with zero position compaction, so removing position 2 from [0,1,2,3] does leave a sparse [0,1,3]. SqliteCollectionRepository.getItems (lines 109-128) is the decisive evidence: it runs a UNION ALL with `ORDER BY position ASC` and returns the rows verbatim вҖ” there is NO renumber-on-read. Yet AGENTS.md:131 and schema.ts:174-175,181 both explicitly assert "a defensive renumber-on-read in getItems". That documented invariant is simply not implemented. So the reviewer's central claim вҖ” gaps persist and the documented renumber-on-read does not exist anywhere вҖ” is correct against the actual code. I also confirmed the reviewer's own caveat that this is NOT a correctness bug: AddToCollection computes position = max+1 (so no collision/duplicate), and ReorderCollection re-densifies positions to 0..n-1 via index-based map. Uniqueness (the real enforced invariant) holds; only density drifts, and current consumers don't rely on density. The substantive defect is documentation/code drift (a false claim that getItems renumbers), which is real and low severity.

**Verifier notes**

Sharper framing: the bug is in the docs, not really in RemoveFromCollection. The unified-position invariant documented in AGENTS.md is about *cross-table uniqueness*, which IS preserved everywhere (Add uses max+1, Reorder densifies via two-phase shift in reorderItems). What does NOT exist is the claimed "defensive renumber-on-read in getItems" вҖ” getItems (SqliteCollectionRepository.ts:109-128) returns stored positions verbatim ordered by position. Both AGENTS.md:131 and schema.ts:174-175 (and 181) make this false claim. Repro: addVideo x4 (positions 0..3), removeVideo the position-2 item, getItems returns positions [0,1,3] вҖ” gap never closes until a full ReorderCollection. Cheapest correct fix is to amend the two comments to say positions are sparse-but-unique-and-monotonic (no renumber-on-read), OR actually implement densification in getItems if any consumer ever needs dense 0..n-1. No functional change to RemoveFromCollection is required for correctness.

---

### F71 вҖ” Frame-step uses a hardcoded 1/30s; misaligns with real frame rate on 24/25/60fps sources

- **Severity:** рҹҹЎ LOW
- **Category:** weird-logic
- **Location:** `src/renderer/components/features/editor/EditorView.tsx:36-39, 123-128`
- **Confidence:** 0.55 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** yes

**Impact**

The comma/period 'nudge one frame' shortcut always advances 33.3ms regardless of the source frame rate. On 24fps one frame is 41.7ms, on 60fps 16.7ms, so the step skips frames (60fps) or lands mid-frame (24fps), and repeated presses drift relative to real frame boundaries. For a cut tool whose value is exact in/out points, 'step one frame' that does not step one frame is a real precision gap. Author documents it as a known fallback pending a probe frameRate field.

**Evidence**

~~~text
const FRAME_DURATION_SEC = 1 / 30
...
const handleFrameStepBack = useCallback(() => { seekRelative(-FRAME_DURATION_SEC) }, [seekRelative])
const handleFrameStepForward = useCallback(() => { seekRelative(FRAME_DURATION_SEC) }, [seekRelative])
~~~

**Fix**

Plumb frameRate through the existing ffprobe pipeline (MediaProbeResult) and compute FRAME_DURATION = 1/frameRate per source; fall back to 1/30 only when unknown.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

The cited code is accurate and current. EditorView.tsx:39 defines `const FRAME_DURATION_SEC = 1 / 30`, and lines 123-128 wire it into handleFrameStepBack/Forward via seekRelative(ВұFRAME_DURATION_SEC), bound to ',' and '.' (lines 154-155). seekRelative (lines 111-121) simply adds the delta to el.currentTime, so the comma/period shortcut always moves exactly 33.3ms irrespective of the source's real frame rate. I confirmed the author's stated justification by reading src/shared/types/media-probe.ts: MediaProbeResult exposes only `duration`, `resolution`, `fileSize` вҖ” there is genuinely no frameRate field, and grep for frameRate/r_frame_rate/fps across the codebase finds no probe-side capture (only ffmpeg progress-parsing of `fps=` in argv-builder/tests, unrelated). So the claim's mechanism is real: on 24fps a true frame is 41.7ms (step lands mid-frame), on 60fps 16.7ms (step skips ~2 frames), and repeated presses drift from real frame boundaries. The author documents it as a deliberate fallback (lines 35-38) pending a frameRate probe field.

**Verifier notes**

Severity correctly low: (1) the author explicitly documents this as a known fallback, not an oversight; (2) the precision-critical operations вҖ” Mark In (handleMarkIn) and Mark Out (handleMarkOut) вҖ” read the raw el.currentTime, not a frame-quantized value, so saved in/out points are not corrupted by this; the frame-step is purely a keyboard nudge convenience. The suggested fix is sound: plumb r_frame_rate through ffprobe into MediaProbeResult and compute 1/frameRate per source, falling back to 1/30. Sharper repro: open a 24fps source, press '.' three times вҶ’ cursor at 0.1s (frame ~2.4) instead of the 3rd frame boundary at 0.125s; on a 60fps source, each '.' advances 2 frames so half the frames are unreachable via the shortcut. Not a correctness/data bug, just a UX precision gap in the editor preview.

---

### F72 вҖ” App version is hardcoded in two places instead of read from package.json

- **Severity:** рҹҹЎ LOW
- **Category:** weird-logic
- **Location:** `src/renderer/components/features/layout/AppSidebar.tsx:99`
- **Confidence:** 0.7 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

The version string '0.0.1' is hardcoded here and again in routes/about.tsx (`<Badge variant="secondary">v0.0.1</Badge>`). It currently matches package.json (0.0.1), but on the next version bump both literals will silently go stale, showing the wrong version in the sidebar footer and About page. Maintenance footgun, not a present-day defect.

**Evidence**

~~~text
<p className="text-xs text-muted-foreground">{t('version', { version: '0.0.1' })}</p>
~~~

**Fix**

Expose the app version through a single source (e.g. an env value injected from package.json at build time, or an IPC getAppVersion) and reference it in both spots.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I read all cited code. AppSidebar.tsx:99 contains `{t('version', { version: '0.0.1' })}` вҖ” the version is a hardcoded string literal passed into the i18n interpolation, not read from any dynamic source. about.tsx:27 contains `<Badge variant="secondary">v0.0.1</Badge>` вҖ” also a hardcoded literal. Both currently match package.json `"version": "0.0.1"`. A repo-wide grep for getAppVersion / app.getVersion / VERSION env confirms there is NO mechanism in the renderer that pulls the real version; the only place `app.getVersion()` is used is the main process (ElectronAutoUpdater.ts), proving the canonical source exists but the UI does not consume it. So on the next version bump in package.json, both UI literals go stale silently. This is a genuine maintenance footgun, not a present-day defect вҖ” exactly as the reviewer characterized it.

**Verifier notes**

Two stale-prone literals: AppSidebar.tsx:99 (`version: '0.0.1'`) and about.tsx:27 (`v0.0.1`). Repro: bump package.json version вҶ’ both UI surfaces keep showing 0.0.1. Clean single-source fix is straightforward since electron-vite/Vite can inject `import.meta.env` from package.json at build time, or an IPC getAppVersion bridging the main process's already-present `app.getVersion()`. Severity low is correct вҖ” cosmetic/maintenance, no functional or security impact.

### F73 вҖ” Mini-player drag onDrop compares against a stale `corner` between drop and settings-query refetch

- **Severity:** рҹҹЎ LOW
- **Category:** weird-logic
- **Location:** `src/renderer/components/features/player/PersistentPlayer.tsx:348-366`
- **Confidence:** 0.4 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

corner is captured from the render closure and derived from the async settings query. After a drop, persistCorner.mutate writes the setting, but until the query refetch lands and the effect re-runs, corner still holds the pre-drag value. A second immediate drag compares snapped against the stale corner and may skip a needed persist or persist redundantly. The visible position is correct (set imperatively), but the persisted corner can lag by one drag.

**Evidence**

~~~text
onDrop: () => {
  ...
  const snapped = nearestCorner(centerX, centerY)
  ...
  if (snapped !== corner) {
    persistCorner.mutate({ key: SETTING_KEYS.miniPlayerCorner, value: snapped })
  }
}
~~~

**Fix**

Compare against the freshly-read setting at drop time (read via queryClient/getState) rather than the closed-over corner, or always persist on drop and let the mutation dedupe.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I read PersistentPlayer.tsx (lines 168-368), use-settings.ts, and query-keys.ts.

The `corner` value (line 170-172) is derived from `useSetting(SETTING_KEYS.miniPlayerCorner)`, whose query key is `['settings','detail','miniPlayerCorner']`. `useSetSetting` (use-settings.ts:24-31) has NO optimistic update / onMutate вҖ” it only invalidates `queryKeys.settings.all` = `['settings']` in onSuccess. Because TanStack invalidateQueries uses prefix matching by default, that DOES eventually refetch the detail query, so `corner` is not permanently stale вҖ” it refreshes after the IPC write + refetch round-trip, and the effect (deps `[mode, mounted, corner, persistCorner]`, line 368) re-wires the draggable with a fresh closure. So the steady-state behavior is correct.

However, the onDrop handler (lines 348-366) closes over `corner` and uses `snapped !== corner` purely as a dedup guard around `persistCorner.mutate`. Between a drop and the time the invalidation/refetch lands and re-runs the effect, the closure's `corner` is stale. Concrete repro: persisted=BR (corner closure=BR). Drag 1 вҶ’ snap TL: `TL !== BR` true вҶ’ writes TL. Before the refetch updates `corner`, Drag 2 вҶ’ snap back BR: closure still sees `corner=BR`, so `BR !== BR` is false вҶ’ the persist is SKIPPED. Persisted setting stays TL while the player is visually at BR (set imperatively at line 356-358). On next mount, cornerToPosition(corner=TL) restores the player to the wrong corner.

So the reviewer's claim вҖ” the persisted corner can lag the visible position by one drag when a second drag beats the refetch вҖ” is accurate. Visible position is always correct (imperative), only persistence is affected.

**Verifier notes**

Real but minor. Requires a second drag completed faster than the setSetting IPC write + settings query refetch вҖ” a tight but achievable window with rapid dragging. Impact is purely cosmetic: the mini player restores to the wrong corner on next mount/session; the live position is always correct. Note the reviewer's mention of 'persist redundantly' is not actually possible (the guard only ever skips, never duplicates). Simplest fix: drop the `snapped !== corner` guard and always call persistCorner.mutate on drop вҖ” the write is idempotent and cheap, eliminating the stale-closure comparison entirely. The reviewer's alternative (read the fresh value via queryClient.getQueryData at drop time) also works. Severity low is correct.

---

### F74 вҖ” CommentsTab 'Copy all' ignores the active comment filters

- **Severity:** рҹҹЎ LOW
- **Category:** weird-logic
- **Location:** `src/renderer/components/features/videos/CommentsTab.tsx:170-178,293-296`
- **Confidence:** 0.55 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

When the user has narrowed the visible comments with the username/text/pinned filters (filteredThreads), the Copy button still serializes `threads` (the full unfiltered set). The visible match-count UI tells the user a subset is shown, so copying silently produces a much larger payload than what is on screen. This is defensible if 'Copy all' is meant to be literal, but it is a likely surprise given the filter UI directly above it.

**Evidence**

~~~text
const handleCopyAll = async (): Promise<void> => {
  if (!data) return
  ... navigator.clipboard.writeText(buildClipboardText(threads)) ...
}
<Button ... onClick={handleCopyAll} ...>{tc('actions.copyAll')}</Button>
~~~

**Fix**

Copy filteredThreads when anyFilterActive (or relabel the button to make the 'all, ignoring filters' semantics explicit).

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

The code facts are exactly as claimed. handleCopyAll (CommentsTab.tsx:170-178) calls buildClipboardText(threads) вҖ” the full unfiltered ThreadGroup[]. The rendered list at line 363 maps filteredThreads, and lines 341-348 show a match-count badge ("filterMatchCount" with shown=filteredThreads.length, total=threads.length) whenever anyFilterActive. So with username/text/pinned filters narrowing the view, the Copy button does serialize the full set, not the visible subset. The early guard `if (!data) return` (line 171) means it copies whatever is in data.comments regardless of filter state.

That said, this is a genuine UX judgment call, not a correctness defect: (1) the button label resolves to "Copy All" (en common.json:20 "Copy All", es "Copiar todo", pt-BR "Copiar tudo"), which arguably signals "all comments, ignoring filters" by design; (2) the Copy button lives in the top global toolbar row (lines 292-301) alongside Reload, visually separated from the filter controls which live in a lower block gated by `threads.length > 0`; (3) the summary header just above it reports data.totalFetched (the full count), reinforcing an "all" mental model. No data loss, crash, or wrong computation вҖ” just a potential expectation mismatch when filters are active.

**Verifier notes**

Confirmed at the code level but it is a defensible-design UX nit, so 'low' (even 'info') is appropriate вҖ” the reviewer's own 0.55 confidence reflects this. Sharper repro: load comments, type a username in the username filter (or check "Pinned only"); the match-count badge shows e.g. "3 of 480"; click Copy All; clipboard contains all 480 threads, not the 3 visible. Cleanest fix is the reviewer's: copy filteredThreads when anyFilterActive. Alternatively relabel to make "all, ignoring filters" explicit, or add a second "Copy visible" action when a filter is active. Note the button is also `disabled={loadingMore}` but never disabled on empty/no-filter, which is fine.

### F75 вҖ” useDateFormat treats settings query loading/error state as the default preset (transient 'auto' flash)

- **Severity:** рҹҹЎ LOW
- **Category:** weird-logic
- **Location:** `src/renderer/hooks/use-date-format.ts:35-46`
- **Confidence:** 0.55 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

useSetting fires its own query (queryKeys.settings.detail), and on first mount setting.data is undefined until the IPC round-trip resolves. isDateFormatPreset(undefined) is false, so format falls back to DEFAULT_DATE_FORMAT ('auto'). If the user picked e.g. yyyy-MM-dd, every date on the page renders in locale 'auto' format for the first frame(s) and then snaps to the chosen preset once the query settles вҖ” a visible flicker on every cold navigation, unlike useOnboardingState which deliberately gates on isLoading. Not a correctness bug (it self-corrects) but a UX papercut on a feature the audit prompt calls out (configurable date-format).

**Evidence**

~~~text
const setting = useSetting(SETTING_KEYS.dateFormat)
const format: DateFormatPreset = isDateFormatPreset(setting.data)
  ? setting.data
  : DEFAULT_DATE_FORMAT
~~~

**Fix**

Expose isLoading from useDateFormat (or have callers suspend) so date cells can render a neutral placeholder until the preset resolves, instead of formatting with the wrong preset and re-rendering. Alternatively seed the settings query from a synchronous source at startup.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

The cited lines match exactly. useSetting (src/renderer/hooks/use-settings.ts:17-22) is a bare useQuery with queryKey settings.detail(key) and queryFn window.api.getSetting(key) вҖ” no initialData, no placeholderData. So on first mount setting.data is undefined until the async IPC round-trip resolves. isDateFormatPreset(undefined) returns false (src/shared/types/date-format.ts:32 checks membership in the preset array), so format collapses to DEFAULT_DATE_FORMAT = 'auto'. formatDate then renders the 'auto' branch (Intl locale ordering) for the first frame(s), and re-renders into the persisted preset once the query settles. The two outputs genuinely differ (e.g. en-US 'auto' вҶ’ 09/15/2026 vs chosen 'yyyy-MM-dd' вҶ’ 2026-09-15), so the flash is visible. Both real callers вҖ” FinishedDownloadsList.tsx:61 and videos.$videoId.tsx:45 вҖ” destructure only formatDate and render immediately with no isLoading gate, unlike the reviewer's cited useOnboardingState pattern. The hook also does not expose isLoading, so callers cannot gate even if they wanted to. So the mechanism, the missing seed/placeholder, and the lack of gating are all as described.

**Verifier notes**

Confirmed but correctly scoped as a self-correcting UX papercut, not a correctness bug. Mitigating factor the reviewer didn't mention: query-client.ts sets a default staleTime of 30_000, so after the first cold fetch the dateFormat setting stays cached/fresh and the flash only recurs after gcTime eviction (TanStack default 5 min of no observers) or a true cold app start. So it's a once-per-cold-load flicker on date cells, not every navigation. Repro: clear cache / fresh launch with a non-'auto' preset persisted, navigate to a video detail page or the finished-downloads list, and the upload/finished dates render in locale 'auto' order for the first paint before snapping to the chosen preset. Cleanest fix matching the codebase: seed the dateFormat query at startup (queryClient.setQueryData / prefetch) since useSetSetting already manages the cache, or expose setting.isLoading from useDateFormat so cells can render 'вҖ”' until resolved. Severity unchanged at low.

---

### F76 вҖ” Mark in/out silently does nothing when it would invert the region вҖ” no user feedback

- **Severity:** рҹҹЎ LOW _(verifier corrected from medium)_
- **Category:** weird-logic
- **Location:** `src/renderer/hooks/use-editor-store.ts:123-160, 161-192`
- **Confidence:** 0.85 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** yes

**Impact**

The HP-5 fix (stop clobbering the other endpoint) replaced silent data-destruction with a silent no-op. When the user presses I past the existing out-point (or O before the existing in-point), the store returns {} and only emits a console.warn. EditorView's handleMarkIn/handleMarkOut get no return value and render no toast, so the user presses the key, sees nothing change, and has no idea why. The boundary case (mark-in at the very end of the clip) is equally invisible.

**Evidence**

~~~text
if (existingOut !== null && clamped >= existingOut) {
  console.warn('[klip:editor] setInPoint refused вҖ” would invert the region; clearRegion() to reset')
  return {}
}
...
if (clamped >= outSec) {
  console.warn('[klip:editor] setInPoint refused вҖ” no room for an out-point past the mark')
  return {}
}
~~~

**Fix**

Have the store mutators report failure (return a boolean or set a transient error field) and surface a toast from handleMarkIn/handleMarkOut, e.g. 'In-point is past the out-point вҖ” clear the region first.'

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

Read use-editor-store.ts:123-192 and the caller EditorView.tsx. The quoted code is current and accurate. On the refuse paths, setInPoint (lines 135-140, 148-151) and setOutPoint (lines 171-176, 180-183) call console.warn and return {} to zustand's set, which is a no-op state update. Crucially, the return value flows to zustand's set, NOT to the component вҖ” handleMarkIn (EditorView.tsx:84-88) does setInPoint(el.currentTime) and discards everything; same for handleMarkOut (90-94). Both are bound to the I/O keyboard shortcuts (useShortcut('i'...), 'o', lines 152-153) and the Mark In/Out toolbar buttons (217, 225). Grep for toast|sonner|useToast in EditorView.tsx returns zero matches, so there is no error-surfacing path. Therefore pressing I past the out-point, O before the in-point, or I at the very end of the clip produces only a DevTools console.warn that an end user never sees; the keypress visibly does nothing. The reviewer's claim is correct in every detail. I did NOT find the concern handled anywhere вҖ” no boolean return is consumed, no transient error field exists on the store, no toast is rendered.

**Verifier notes**

Confirmed but I'd downgrade medium->low. This is a feedback/UX gap, not a correctness or data-loss bug вҖ” the HP-5 fix correctly prevents creating an inverted/collapsed region, and the failure mode is safe and recoverable (the user can hit clear-region). The harm is purely confusion: no visible change on keypress. Repro: open editor, mark out at t=5s, then move cursor to t=8s and press I вҖ” region stays {in: old, out:5}, nothing changes, only a console.warn fires. Suggested fix stands: have the mutators report failure (boolean return or a transient store error field) and surface a toast from handleMarkIn/handleMarkOut. Note EditorView already uses i18n (t('controls.markIn')) so a message key would fit the existing pattern, and sonner/toast is not yet imported in this file so it'd be a new dependency for the view.

### F77 вҖ” markChildrenMissing receives an unused _creatorId parameter masking intent

- **Severity:** в„№пёҸ INFO
- **Category:** dead-code
- **Location:** `src/main/use-cases/ReconcileDirectory.ts:529-546`
- **Confidence:** 0.7 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

`_creatorId` is passed at both call sites (lines 146 and 245) but never used inside the method; children are taken entirely from the pre-fetched videos/cuts arrays. Not a correctness bug, but the parameter implies a per-creator query that doesn't happen, and could let a caller pass a creatorId that doesn't match the supplied arrays without any check.

**Evidence**

~~~text
private markChildrenMissing(
    _creatorId: string,
    videos: Video[],
    cuts: Cut[],
    result: ReconcileResult
  ): void {
~~~

**Fix**

Drop the parameter, or assert that the passed videos/cuts all belong to _creatorId to guard against a future caller mismatch.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I read ReconcileDirectory.ts. The method signature at lines 529-534 matches the quote exactly: `markChildrenMissing(_creatorId: string, videos: Video[], cuts: Cut[], result: ReconcileResult)`. The body (lines 535-545) iterates only over the passed `videos` and `cuts` arrays вҖ” `_creatorId` is never referenced. Both call sites are real: line 146-151 passes `creator.id` plus the pre-fetched `videosByCreator.get(creator.id) ?? []` / `cutsByCreator`, and line 245-250 passes `existing.id` plus `this.videoRepo.findByCreatorId(existing.id)` / `cutRepo`. So the parameter is genuinely unused dead data. The author already marked it `_creatorId` (the TS/ESLint convention for an intentionally-unused param), so the unused state is acknowledged, not an oversight. The reviewer's secondary concern вҖ” that a caller could pass a creatorId not matching the arrays with no check вҖ” is technically true but purely hypothetical; at both current call sites the id and the arrays are derived from the same creator, so there is no actual mismatch and no correctness impact.

**Verifier notes**

Factually confirmed but cosmetic. The `_` prefix already documents the param as intentionally unused, so this is closer to a style nit than a defect. The cleaner fix is simply to drop the parameter (it conveys no information the body uses); the reviewer's alternative вҖ” asserting all videos/cuts belong to _creatorId вҖ” would add a per-element guard for a precondition the two callers already satisfy by construction, which is likely over-engineering for an internal private helper. No correctness, security, or behavior issue. Severity rightly left at info.

### F78 вҖ” Mini-player drag effect lists `mounted` as a dependency but never reads it

- **Severity:** в„№пёҸ INFO
- **Category:** dead-code
- **Location:** `src/renderer/components/features/player/PersistentPlayer.tsx:325-368`
- **Confidence:** 0.6 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

The drag-to-snap effect body references mode, corner, persistCorner, and the two refs, but never mounted. Including mounted in the deps tears down and re-creates the draggable() wire-up whenever mounted flips (detail<->mini transitions), needlessly re-registering pragmatic-drag-and-drop listeners. Harmless but wasteful and misleading; the early-return already gates on mode !== 'mini'.

**Evidence**

~~~text
useEffect(() => {
  const container = containerRef.current
  const handle = dragHandleRef.current
  if (!container || mode !== 'mini') return
  ...
}, [mode, mounted, corner, persistCorner])
~~~

**Fix**

Drop `mounted` from the dependency array (keep [mode, corner, persistCorner]).

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I read PersistentPlayer.tsx lines 280-399. The drag-to-snap useEffect at lines 325-368 has dependency array `[mode, mounted, corner, persistCorner]` (line 368), but its body (326-367) references only container, handle, mode, corner, persistCorner, and the refs вҖ” `mounted` is never read inside it. The early-return on line 328 gates on `mode !== 'mini'`. So `mounted` in the dep array is genuinely dead/misleading: it's not consumed by the effect. This matches the reviewer's evidence verbatim. The finding (dead/unused dependency) is real.\n\nOne correction to the reviewer's stated *harm*: line 113 defines `const mounted = mode === 'detail' || mode === 'mini'`, i.e. `mounted` is derived purely from `mode`. Any time `mounted` toggles, `mode` has necessarily changed too, and `mode` is already in the dep array. So `mounted` causes ZERO extra effect tear-downs/re-registrations beyond what `mode` already triggers вҖ” the 'needlessly re-registering pragmatic-drag-and-drop listeners' framing overstates the cost. The real issue is that it's a redundant, misleading dependency (clarity/dead-code), not wasted work. That is consistent with info severity.

**Verifier notes**

Confirmed at src/renderer/components/features/player/PersistentPlayer.tsx:325-368. `mounted` (defined line 113 as `mode === 'detail' || mode === 'mini'`) is never referenced in the effect body and is fully derived from `mode`, which is already a dep. Suggested fix is correct: deps should be `[mode, corner, persistCorner]`. Note: because `mounted` is derived from `mode`, removing it changes nothing at runtime (no behavioral difference, no extra re-registration avoided) вҖ” this is a pure clarity/dead-code cleanup, so the reviewer's 'wasteful re-registration' rationale is slightly off but the cleanup itself is valid.

### F81 вҖ” Unused exported consts MINI_PLAYER_CORNER_VALUES and DEFAULT_THEME

- **Severity:** в„№пёҸ INFO
- **Category:** dead-code
- **Location:** `src/shared/types/mini-player.ts:16`
- **Confidence:** 0.65 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

Both constants are defined and re-exported through src/shared/types/index.ts but have no consumer anywhere in src/ вҖ” they appear only at their definition site and in the barrel re-export. They are runtime values (not just types), so they are emitted but never read. Minor: a single array / string each, no transitive bloat. Lower priority than the files/deps above; included for completeness.

**Evidence**

~~~text
export const MINI_PLAYER_CORNER_VALUES = ['TL', 'TR', 'BL', 'BR'] as const satisfies readonly MiniPlayerCorner[]
// and src/shared/types/preferences.ts:19  export const DEFAULT_THEME: Theme = 'system'
~~~

**Fix**

Drop the `export` (and the barrel re-export) if not part of a deliberate public API, or wire MINI_PLAYER_CORNER_VALUES into the settings UI that validates corner values.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I read the three cited files and grepped the full repo. The quoted lines are accurate: src/shared/types/mini-player.ts:16 defines `export const MINI_PLAYER_CORNER_VALUES = ['TL','TR','BL','BR'] as const satisfies readonly MiniPlayerCorner[]`, and src/shared/types/preferences.ts:19 defines `export const DEFAULT_THEME: Theme = 'system'`. **Verifier notes**

Real dead code, correctly scoped as info. Trivial footprint (one 4-element array, one string). Fix options: (a) delete both consts + their barrel re-export lines (index.ts:89 and :102), or (b) wire MINI_PLAYER_CORNER_VALUES into a corner-picker/validator if that UI is planned. Worth confirming DEFAULT_THEME isn't intended as the theme fallback that should be plumbed into the appearance/theme-resolution path the way DEFAULT_LANGUAGE is in detect.ts вҖ” if so, the cleaner fix is to *use* it rather than delete it.

### F84 вҖ” Verified: '/'-while-typing palette hijack is correctly guarded (no defect)

- **Severity:** в„№пёҸ INFO
- **Category:** other
- **Location:** `src/renderer/hooks/use-shortcut.ts:119-124`
- **Confidence:** 0.55 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

The single-key '/' that opens the command palette IS suppressed when focus is in a text input via isTextInputActive(), so the classic 'pressing / while typing opens search' hijack is avoided. Modifier shortcuts (mod+k) intentionally bypass the guard as documented. i18n key coverage was also verified: all 18 namespaces have identical key paths across en/es/pt-BR (deep diff reports zero missing/extra keys), and no hardcoded user-facing strings were found in the routes. Reporting as info to record what was checked; no defect found here.

**Evidence**

~~~text
if (parsed.kind !== 'modifier' && !allowInInputs && isTextInputActive()) {
  return
}
~~~

**Fix**

No change needed.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I read use-shortcut.ts (lines 119-124 match the quoted evidence verbatim) and traced the actual call site. The '/' palette shortcut is registered at src/renderer/src/routes/__root.tsx:67 as `useShortcut('/', openPalette)` with no `allowInInputs` option, so it parses as kind 'single' (parseSpec, line 63: no space, no '+'). The onKeyDown guard at lines 122-124 вҖ” `if (parsed.kind !== 'modifier' && !allowInInputs && isTextInputActive()) return` вҖ” therefore fires for '/': any '/' keystroke while focus is in a text-entry surface is dropped before the match logic. isTextInputActive() (src/renderer/lib/dom-helpers.ts:7-14) returns true for INPUT, TEXTAREA, SELECT, and contentEditable elements, which covers the classic 'press / while typing' hijack. The sibling `useShortcut('mod+k', togglePalette)` parses as kind 'modifier' and is intentionally exempted, matching the documented behavior in the file's doc comment (lines 10-12) and in dom-helpers.ts (lines 1-5). So the reviewer's substantive claim вҖ” the '/' hijack is correctly guarded and is a non-defect вҖ” is accurate for the cited code. I independently confirmed the guard and call site; I did not re-run the full i18n deep-diff across all 18 namespaces (that part of the note is unverified by me but is tangential to the cited location and does not affect the verdict).

**Verifier notes**

No defect. The guard is real and reaches the '/' shortcut: __root.tsx:67 registers it as a single-key spec without allowInInputs, and use-shortcut.ts:122-124 early-returns when isTextInputActive(). dom-helpers.ts:7-14 covers INPUT/TEXTAREA/SELECT/contentEditable. mod+k bypass is by design (kind 'modifier'). One nuance worth recording: isTextInputActive only checks document.activeElement.tagName/isContentEditable вҖ” a custom widget that captures text without using a native input or contentEditable would NOT be protected, but no such case exists at the cited call sites. The i18n key-coverage assertions in the finding were not re-verified by me; they are outside the cited file and do not change the verdict for this location.

### F85 вҖ” editRecipe schema permits container 'mkv', which Chromium <video> cannot play вҖ” only the hardcoded UI default ('mp4') keeps it unreachable

- **Severity:** в„№пёҸ INFO
- **Category:** other
- **Location:** `src/shared/types/edit-recipe.ts:93-98`
- **Confidence:** 0.5 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

RenderCutFromVideo derives the output filename directly from recipe.output.container (fileName = `${cutId}.${recipe.output.container}`). The schema accepts 'mkv', and per the project's own known-issue (Chromium <video> rejects DocType=matroska), a cut rendered to .mkv would be uneditable/unplayable in-app. Today the only client (SaveCutDialog) hardcodes container:'mp4', so this is not reachable from the UI, but the validation boundary that is supposed to fail-closed actually accepts a container the player can never display. Flagging as info/forward-compat hazard, not a live bug.

**Evidence**

~~~text
output: z
  .object({
    container: z.enum(['mp4', 'webm', 'mkv']),
    mode: z.enum(['copy', 'reencode'])
  })
~~~

**Fix**

Drop 'mkv' from the renderer-facing output container enum (keep webm/mp4), or add a canRender rejection for mkv in the ffmpeg backend so the fail-closed contract matches the player's real capabilities.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

Verified all four legs of the chain. (1) src/shared/types/edit-recipe.ts:95 does accept container: z.enum(['mp4','webm','mkv']) exactly as quoted. (2) src/main/use-cases/RenderCutFromVideo.ts:103 and :109 build the staging/final filenames as `${cutId}.${recipe.output.container}`, so the container value flows straight to the output extension with no remapping вҖ” ffmpeg would muxer-select by extension and write a real .mkv. (3) The supposed fail-closed boundary, FfmpegRenderBackend.canRender (lines 47-56), ONLY gates on isMvpSupportedRecipe (single trim op). It never inspects recipe.output.container, so an mkv recipe passes canRender and renders. (4) The lone client, SaveCutDialog.tsx:76, hardcodes container:'mp4' (with a comment that container becomes user-tweakable in v2). So the reviewer is correct: mkv is schema-valid and renderable, and the only thing making it unreachable is the UI default, not the validation contract. Given the project's documented known-issue (Chromium <video> rejects DocType=matroska), an mkv cut would be unplayable/uneditable in-app. This is a genuine forward-compat hazard, not a live bug вҖ” confirming at info severity as the reviewer rated it.

**Verifier notes**

Not reachable from current UI (SaveCutDialog hardcodes mp4), so no live impact вҖ” info is the right level. Sharper repro for v2: the moment the editor exposes a container picker (the SaveCutDialog comment explicitly anticipates this) or any non-SaveCutDialog client calls editorStartRender with container:'mkv', the IPC schema accepts it, canRender returns ok, ffmpeg writes <cutId>.mkv, and the resulting cut is unplayable in the in-app <video>. The doc comment at edit-recipe.ts:13-15 claims backends MUST canRender-reject what they can't handle, but FfmpegRenderBackend only rejects unsupported ops, not unsupported containers вҖ” so the fail-closed contract is genuinely incomplete on the container axis. Note tests/main/shared/ipc-schemas.test.ts:373 only asserts that an out-of-enum container ('avi') is rejected; there is no test asserting mkv is refused, consistent with mkv being intentionally(?) in the enum. Suggested fix stands: either drop 'mkv' from the enum (webm/mp4 are both Chromium-playable) or add a player-capability rejection in canRender.
