### F86 вҖ” klip-media protocol handler serves any HTTP method without restriction

- **Severity:** в„№пёҸ INFO
- **Category:** security
- **Location:** `src/main/framework-drivers/electron/KlipMediaProtocolHandler.ts:80-148`
- **Confidence:** 0.4 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

Not exploitable for write/SSRF (file:// upstream is read-only and the path is entity-keyed + realpath-contained), but the handler is method-agnostic where a media GET endpoint should only honour GET/HEAD. Minor hardening / least-surprise improvement; flagged at info because there is no concrete harm given the locked-down upstream.

**Evidence**

~~~text
handle() logs request.method but never checks it; a POST/PUT/DELETE to klip-media://video/<id>/file follows the same parseвҶ’resolveвҶ’statвҶ’net.fetch path and returns the file body. net.fetch on a file:// URL ignores the method for writes, so no data is mutated.
~~~

**Fix**

Early-return 405 for any method other than GET/HEAD before resolving, so the contract is explicit and HEAD can be answered without a body.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I read the full handler at src/main/framework-drivers/electron/KlipMediaProtocolHandler.ts. The code matches the finding exactly: handle() logs request.method on lines 82-84 but never branches on it. There is no method guard anywhere; a POST/PUT/DELETE/PATCH to klip-media://video/<id>/file would follow the identical parse (parseKlipMediaUrl) -> resolve (IResolveMediaUrl.resolve) -> containment (checkPathInsideRoot) -> statSync -> net.fetch(file://...) path and return the file body. The reviewer's own non-exploitability analysis is correct: net.fetch on a file:// URL is read-only (no body/method-driven mutation), the parser is entity-keyed so the renderer never supplies raw FS paths, and checkPathInsideRoot provides realpath containment as defence-in-depth. So there is no read-outside-root, no write, no SSRF. The only real substance is that a media GET/HEAD endpoint is method-agnostic, which is a least-surprise / contract-explicitness nit, not a vulnerability. This is exactly what the reviewer claimed and they self-rated it info with 0.4 confidence and explicitly disclaimed concrete harm.

**Verifier notes**

Confirmed as a factual code-state observation, not a real security issue. There is genuinely no method check (only the log line at L82-84 references request.method). Severity correctly stays info вҖ” it is pure hardening/least-surprise: returning 405 for non-GET/HEAD would make the contract explicit and let HEAD be answered without a body. Note even HEAD currently isn't special-cased: it would still issue a full net.fetch and return the body, so the suggested fix also addresses a minor HEAD-returns-body wrinkle. No data is mutated and no path escapes root, so this should not be prioritized as a security defect.

---

### F87 вҖ” klip-media protocol handler logs full attacker-controlled request.url unredacted

- **Severity:** в„№пёҸ INFO
- **Category:** security
- **Location:** `src/main/framework-drivers/electron/KlipMediaProtocolHandler.ts:82-89`
- **Confidence:** 0.5 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

request.url here is fully renderer/attacker-controlled (any HTML/CSS context can issue a klip-media:// request with arbitrary path/query). It is written verbatim вҖ” via the console->electron-log monkey-patch (logger.ts:57-59) вҖ” into the persistent log file at <userData>/logs/klip.log (or the project-local logs/klip-dev.log in dev). Because the value is unsanitised it permits log-line injection (embedded CRLF forging fake log entries) and, if a poisoned comment/description ever drives a klip-media request, copies attacker content into a file the user is likely to share when debugging. Low marginal risk under the threat model, but it is the one spot in an otherwise carefully redacted logging surface (everything else routes through redactPath/redactError) that emits untrusted input raw.

**Evidence**

~~~text
console.log(`[klip-media] вҶҗ ${request.method} ${request.url}${rangeHeader ? ` range=${rangeHeader}` : ''}`)
...
console.warn(`[klip-media] reject ${parsed.status} parseKlipMediaUrl: ${request.url}`)
~~~

**Fix**

Strip control characters (at minimum \r\n) from request.url before logging, and consider logging only the parsed (kind,id,asset) tuple on success and a length-capped, sanitized form on reject rather than the raw URL.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I read KlipMediaProtocolHandler.ts:80-90 and confirmed the quoted lines are present and unchanged: line 82-84 logs `[klip-media] вҶҗ ${request.method} ${request.url}...` and line 88 logs the raw `request.url` on reject. I confirmed via src/main/framework-drivers/electron/logger.ts:57-59 that `console.*` in the main process is monkey-patched onto `electron-log` (`Object.assign(console, log.functions)`), and lines 41-45 confirm these lines are persisted to `<cwd>/logs/klip-dev.log` (dev) or `<userData>/logs/klip.log` (prod). So `console.log/warn` in the handler do land verbatim in a persistent, user-shareable file.

The "one unredacted spot" claim holds: every OTHER log line in this handler routes user-derived strings through `redactPath`/`redactError` (lines 107, 113, 126, 132) and only logs the parsed (kind,id,asset) tuple (lines 92, 102, 132) вҖ” confirmed redact.ts exists at src/main/domain/types/redact.ts and is the established convention. Lines 82-84 and 88 are genuinely the only sites that emit the raw, untrusted `request.url`.

`request.url` IS renderer-controlled: any HTML/CSS/fetch in the renderer can request an arbitrary `klip-media://...` URL, and the full URL (including bogus segments/query) reaches the handler before `parseKlipMediaUrl` runs вҖ” and on the reject path (line 88) it is logged even though parsing failed, i.e. for fully arbitrary input.

However the severity is correctly already 'info' and I'd keep it there, NOT raise it: (1) the CRLF/log-injection vector is largely neutralised by Chromium's WHATWG-URL normalization вҖ” `\r`, `\n`, `\t` are stripped from URLs before a resource/fetch request is issued, so a renderer cannot easily smuggle literal newlines into `request.url`; (2) the content is a klip-media URL, not a filesystem path (path-based URLs were removed by design вҖ” see klip-media-protocol.ts:21-26), so no sensitive absolute path leaks here; the worst case is some attacker-chosen text echoed into a log the user might share. The finding is real and the suggested fix (strip control chars / cap length / log only the parsed tuple) is a reasonable defence-in-depth hardening, but the residual risk is genuinely low.

**Verifier notes**

Confirmed but low-impact, matching the claimed 'info'. Real repro: a renderer doing `fetch('klip-media://bogus')` or `<img src="klip-media://x">` causes line 88 to write arbitrary attacker-chosen URL text into the persistent log. The CRLF-injection angle is weak in practice because Chromium normalizes control chars out of URLs before the protocol handler sees them, so forging fake log lines via embedded newlines is mostly blocked; the practical residual is just unredacted attacker text copied into a user-shareable log. The query-string portion (everything after the 3 path segments) is never parsed/validated yet is logged on the success path too (line 82-84). Cheapest robust fix: log `request.url.replace(/[\r\n]/g,'')` (or a length-capped sanitized form), or on success log only the (kind,id,asset) tuple like the rest of the handler already does.

---

### F88 вҖ” MediaCard / CollectionRow img alt uses YouTube-origin title but renders before load вҖ” acceptable; no XSS, noting the audited img-src surface is intact

- **Severity:** в„№пёҸ INFO
- **Category:** security

A repo-wide grep for dangerouslySetInnerHTML returns zero hits. Thumbnail/avatar src values come from the allow-listed klip-media:// scheme or the CSP-allowlisted google CDNs (index.html img-src). So the renderer feature components have no HTML/script injection surface for hostile YouTube metadata. The prior audits/06-security.md klip-media path-containment concern is a main-process issue, out of this area.

**Evidence**

~~~text
const src = hasThumbnail ? mediaUrl(entityKind, entityId, 'thumbnail') : undefined
<img src={src} alt={title} loading="lazy" ... />
~~~

**Fix**

No change needed in these components; keep rendering YouTube text as React children. (Flagging as info so the 'XSS surface' part of the audit is explicitly answered: none found.)

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I read MediaCard.tsx directly. Line 42 sets `src = hasThumbnail ? mediaUrl(entityKind, entityId, 'thumbnail') : undefined`; mediaUrl (format.ts:38-40) returns `klip-media://${kind}/${encodeURIComponent(id)}/${asset}` вҖ” strictly the allow-listed custom scheme, with id encoded, never YouTube-origin text. So within this area (renderer feature components + shared primitives) there is genuinely no HTML/script-injection surface for hostile YouTube metadata. The cited lines match the quoted evidence exactly. This is an accurate audit confirmation rather than a defect; the reviewer correctly scopes the real klip-media path-containment risk (audits/06-security.md:64) to the main-process protocol handler, outside this area.

**Verifier notes**

Verified, not a bug вҖ” informational confirmation. The only substantive related risk lives elsewhere: audits/06-security.md:64 describes a klip-media:// protocol handler lacking path containment (a malicious img src could in principle point the privileged scheme at an arbitrary file). That is a main-process concern in the protocol registration/handler, explicitly out of this reviewer's renderer-component scope, and is unaffected by MediaCard because MediaCard only ever emits `klip-media://<kind>/<encoded-id>/thumbnail`. If anything is actionable, route it to the main-process handler review, not these components.

### F89 вҖ” AGENTS.md persistent-player description (capture-phase scroll listeners) no longer matches the rAF implementation

- **Severity:** в„№пёҸ INFO
- **Category:** spec-violation
- **Location:** `AGENTS.md:43`
- **Confidence:** 0.9 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

The shipped code tracks the slot rect with a requestAnimationFrame loop reading getBoundingClientRect() every frame (the documented fix in the project memory note 'Radix ScrollArea scroll listeners are unreliable; use rAF'). AGENTS.md still describes the abandoned capture-phase scroll-listener approach. No functional gap вҖ” purely a stale architectural doc that would mislead a contributor reading the spec.

**Evidence**

~~~text
AGENTS: "Detail mode tracks a route-owned slot rect via `ResizeObserver` + capture-phase scroll listeners" вҖ” but PersistentPlayer.tsx:244 uses `let rafId = requestAnimationFrame(function tick() { update(); rafId = requestAnimationFrame(tick) })` and the comment at line 230 explicitly says it stopped "attempts to listen on `window` (capture phase)".
~~~

**Fix**

Update AGENTS.md line 43 to describe the ResizeObserver + per-frame rAF reposition loop actually used in PersistentPlayer.tsx.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I verified both halves of the claim against the real files.

AGENTS.md line 43 reads exactly as quoted: "Detail mode tracks a route-owned slot rect via `ResizeObserver` + capture-phase scroll listeners; mini mode pins to a fixed bottom-right corner."

The actual implementation lives at src/renderer/components/features/player/PersistentPlayer.tsx (not the reviewer's cited src/renderer/src/... path, but the quoted code matches verbatim). The mode/slot effect uses:
- A requestAnimationFrame loop: line 244-247 `let rafId = requestAnimationFrame(function tick() { update(); rafId = requestAnimationFrame(tick) })`, where `update()` (line 207-224) reads `slotEl.getBoundingClientRect()` each frame and repositions only on change.
- A ResizeObserver (line 252-253) as a supplementary same-frame trigger.
- An explicit comment block (lines 227-243) that says earlier "attempts to listen on `window` (capture phase)" left the player stationary and were abandoned in favor of the rAF approach.

So the doc describes the exact approach the code's own comment says it abandoned. This matches the project memory note 'Radix ScrollArea scroll listeners are unreliable; use rAF'. It is a stale architectural doc with no functional gap вҖ” purely misleading to a contributor reading the spec.

**Verifier notes**

Real, but trivially low impact (stale doc only, no runtime effect) вҖ” 'info' is correct. Note the cited code path was wrong: actual file is C:/Users/lenin/OneDrive/Documents/GitHub/klip/src/renderer/components/features/player/PersistentPlayer.tsx (no extra src/ segment; rAF loop at line 244, abandoned-capture-phase comment at lines 227-243). Suggested fix is right: AGENTS.md:43 should read something like "ResizeObserver + per-frame requestAnimationFrame reposition loop reading getBoundingClientRect()".

### F92 вҖ” README 'post-download enrichment (... comments ...)' overstates what download actually fetches

- **Severity:** в„№пёҸ INFO
- **Category:** spec-violation
- **Location:** `README.md:16`
- **Confidence:** 0.72 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

Listing 'comments' as part of automatic post-download enrichment implies the download pipeline pulls comment threads, which it deliberately does not (ban-risk mitigation, per the design). What is enriched is the comment COUNT metadata, not the comments. Minor wording overstatement in the user-facing feature list; the actual comments viewer is a separate on-demand feature.

**Evidence**

~~~text
README Features: "YouTube downloads вҖ” Bundled yt-dlp pipeline with channel detection, progress reporting, and post-download enrichment (description, tags, comments, view counts)". Comments are fetched only on explicit user action via FetchVideoComments (GetCachedVideoComments cache, no DB persistence) вҖ” plan-nextSteps Step 6 states comments are 'On-Demand, No Persistence' and are 'never fetched automatically or in batch'. DownloadVideo/FetchVideoDetail enrichment persists description/tags/viewCount/likeCount/commentCount but never the comment bodies.
~~~

**Fix**

Reword the README enrichment parenthetical to '(description, tags, view/comment counts)' and, if desired, separately mention the on-demand comments viewer so the automatic-vs-on-demand distinction is clear.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

README.md:16 still reads verbatim: "post-download enrichment (description, tags, comments, view counts)". I traced the actual enrichment write-paths. DownloadVideo.ts (the download pipeline) upserts the Video with description, viewCount, tags:[], and explicitly commentCount: null (lines 254-282) вҖ” no comment bodies. The deeper enrichment, FetchVideoDetail.ts (lines 162-177), persists commentCount (the COUNT integer from yt-dlp's comment_count), plus likeCount/dislikeCount/tags/description/viewCount/category вҖ” again never comment bodies. The only place comment text is fetched is FetchVideoComments.ts (line 37: downloader.fetchComments), which runs strictly on explicit user action, writes to an on-disk CommentsCache (7-day TTL) and does NO DB persistence. plan-nextSteps.prompt.md Step 6 (line 396, 400, 431) labels this "On-Demand, No Persistence" and states comments are "never fetched automatically or in batch" as deliberate ban-risk mitigation; line 264 even notes comment_count is "count only, not the comments themselves вҖ” comments are Step 6". So three of the four parenthetical items (description, tags, view counts) are genuinely auto-enriched, but "comments" conflates the comment COUNT with the comment bodies, implying the automatic pipeline pulls comment threads when by design it never does. The finding is accurate.

**Verifier notes**

Real but cosmetic/doc-only вҖ” no behavioral or security impact. Confirmed against three sources: DownloadVideo.ts:269 sets commentCount:null and never touches comment bodies; FetchVideoDetail.ts:166 persists commentCount (the integer) only; FetchVideoComments.ts is the sole comment-body path, on-demand + cache-only (no DB). The reviewer's suggested reword to "(description, tags, view/comment counts)" is accurate and minimal. Optionally the README could add a separate mention of the on-demand Comments viewer (CommentsTab.tsx) to make the automatic-vs-on-demand split explicit. Severity info is correct; not worth more.

### F93 вҖ” Repositories use raw sql`` for json_each / UNION / FTS despite AGENTS 'raw SQL is never used in repositories'

- **Severity:** в„№пёҸ INFO
- **Category:** spec-violation
- **Location:** `src/main/interface-adapters/repositories/SqliteVideoRepository.ts:119-132, 178-187`
- **Confidence:** 0.75 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

AGENTS.md line 113 asserts 'Raw SQL is never used in repositories вҖ” all queries go through Drizzle's type-safe query builder.' In practice findByTags, getAllDistinctTags, searchByTitle (FTS), and SqliteCollectionRepository.getItems all use hand-written raw sql`` strings (json_each, UNION ALL, FTS5 MATCH/bm25) cast to untyped row shapes. These are legitimate (Drizzle cannot model json_each / virtual tables), and the user-supplied values are parameter-bound (no injection), so this is a documentation accuracy issue, not a security/correctness bug. Flagging because the spec is presented as authoritative and the cast-to-`as VideoRow[]` loses Drizzle's type safety, so a schema/column rename won't be caught by the compiler in these queries.

**Evidence**

~~~text
const rows = this.db.all(sql`SELECT DISTINCT v.*\n          FROM videos v, json_each(v.tags) AS t\n          WHERE v.status = 'active' AND t.value IN (${tagValues})\n          ORDER BY v.created_at DESC`) as VideoRow[]
~~~

**Fix**

Reword AGENTS.md line 113 to 'Raw SQL is confined to queries Drizzle cannot express (json_each, UNION across join tables, FTS5); user input is always parameter-bound' so the rule matches the code, and consider centralizing the raw row shapes in shared types to reduce drift risk.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

I read AGENTS.md and the cited repository files directly. AGENTS.md (in the "Database Layer (Drizzle ORM)" section) states verbatim: "Raw SQL is never used in repositories вҖ” all queries go through Drizzle's type-safe query builder." This absolute claim is contradicted by the actual code. SqliteVideoRepository.findByTags (lines 124-129) and getAllDistinctTags (lines 178-184) issue hand-written sql`SELECT ... json_each(v.tags) ...` strings via this.db.all(...) cast `as VideoRow[]` / `as Array<{tag,count}>`. searchByTitle (lines 147-153) uses raw FTS5 sql`... videos_fts MATCH ${matchExpr} ORDER BY bm25(videos_fts) ...` cast `as Array<typeof videos.$inferSelect>`. SqliteCollectionRepository.getItems (lines 114-119) uses raw sql with UNION ALL. So all four cited sites are real. The reviewer's framing is accurate: user-supplied values ARE parameter-bound (tags via sql`${t}`, matchExpr/limit via sql`${...}`, the LIKE fallback uses ESCAPE), so there is no SQL injection. The genuine downside is the `as ...` casts bypass Drizzle's compile-time column checking, so a schema/column rename would not be caught by tsc in these queries. This is a documentation-accuracy + minor type-safety-drift issue, not a security or correctness bug. The raw SQL itself is legitimate вҖ” Drizzle cannot model json_each, FTS5 virtual tables, or this UNION cleanly.

**Verifier notes**

All cited lines match the quoted code exactly. Confirmed raw-SQL sites: SqliteVideoRepository.ts findByTags (124-129, json_each), searchByTitle (147-153, FTS5 MATCH/bm25), getAllDistinctTags (178-184, json_each GROUP BY); SqliteCollectionRepository.ts getItems (114-119, UNION ALL). All bind user input as parameters вҖ” no injection. The accurate-but-stale doc line lives in AGENTS.md under "## Database Layer (Drizzle ORM)" ("Raw SQL is never used in repositories вҖ” all queries go through Drizzle's type-safe query builder"). Severity info is correct: this is a doc-vs-code accuracy gap; the only functional risk is the `as VideoRow[]` casts losing Drizzle's column-rename safety in these four queries. Reviewer's suggested reword (confine the rule to "queries Drizzle cannot express; user input always parameter-bound") faithfully matches the code.

### F94 вҖ” Cross-table collection position uniqueness has no DB constraint and is only enforced by single-threaded use-case logic

- **Severity:** в„№пёҸ INFO _(verifier corrected from low)_
- **Category:** weird-logic
- **Location:** `src/main/interface-adapters/repositories/SqliteCollectionRepository.ts:130-203`
- **Confidence:** 0.5 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

The 'position is unique within a collection across collection_videos UNION collection_cuts' invariant is enforced purely in AddToCollection (max+1) and ReorderCollection inside transaction.run. There is no UNIQUE index spanning both tables (SQLite can't express a cross-table unique constraint), so any code path that inserts a join row without going through those use-cases вҖ” or a future concurrent writer вҖ” can produce duplicate positions, which getItems' ORDER BY position would then render in an arbitrary order. This is correct today only by construction (single main thread, all writes funnel through the two use-cases). Worth a guard/test rather than a fix.

**Evidence**

~~~text
addVideo(...) { this.db.insert(collectionVideos).values({ collectionId, videoId, position, addedAt }).run() }
addCut(...) { this.db.insert(collectionCuts).values({ collectionId, cutId, position, addedAt }).run() }
~~~

**Fix**

Add an integration test asserting positions stay collision-free across mixed add/remove/reorder sequences, and consider a per-table UNIQUE(collection_id, position) plus the application-level cross-table rule so at least intra-table collisions are caught by the DB.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

The factual core of the finding is accurate. SqliteCollectionRepository.addVideo (L130-132) and addCut (L134-136) do raw inserts with a caller-supplied position; getItems (L109-128) is a plain UNION ALL ... ORDER BY position ASC with NO renumbering/dedup. The cross-table "position unique within a collection across collection_videos UNION collection_cuts" invariant is enforced only by application logic: AddToCollection (max+1 inside transaction.run, AddToCollection.ts:34-55) and ReorderCollection->reorderItems (two-phase SHIFT). The per-table schema (schema.ts:205-226) has a composite PK on (collectionId, videoId/cutId) and an index on (collectionId, position) but NO UNIQUE on (collection_id, position) вҖ” so even intra-table duplicate positions are not DB-prevented, and SQLite genuinely cannot express the cross-table rule. So the technical claim holds. HOWEVER, this is already explicitly known and consciously deferred: schema.ts:167-183 documents the exact invariant, states "SQLite cannot express that as a DB constraint," and carries an "AUDIT-2026-05-02 (deferred)" note weighing a UNIQUE(collection_id, position) against the awkwardness of cross-table constraints, concluding the existing two-phase shift covers every realistic in-app write path and to "Revisit if a multi-process writer is ever introduced." That matches the finding's own "correct today only by construction" framing. One inaccuracy worth noting: the schema comment claims a "defensive renumber-on-read in getItems," but the actual getItems does not renumber вҖ” so the documented mitigation is slightly weaker than the comment asserts.

**Verifier notes**

Real but a no-op risk today and explicitly documented/deferred in schema.ts:167-183 (AUDIT-2026-05-02), so this is informational, not a low bug. The reviewer's suggested integration test (mixed add/remove/reorder collision check) is the right increment; a per-table UNIQUE(collection_id, position) would also catch intra-table collisions cheaply since SQLite supports it (unlike the cross-table case). Minor doc bug to flag separately: schema.ts says getItems does a "defensive renumber-on-read," but getItems (L109-128) does not renumber at all вҖ” that comment is misleading. No concurrent writer exists today (single main-thread, all writes funnel through AddToCollection/ReorderCollection via the AuditedCollectionRepository decorator).

---

### F95 вҖ” Queue-rejection error path emits an error event but writes no download_history row

- **Severity:** в„№пёҸ INFO _(verifier corrected from low)_
- **Category:** weird-logic
- **Location:** `src/main/use-cases/DownloadVideo.ts:115-132`
- **Confidence:** 0.6 В· **In 2026-04-28 baseline:** no

**Impact**

Every terminal outcome inside performDownload appends a history row (success, error, cancelled, duplicate). But the outer queue .catch вҖ” which fires when the queue rejects a task without ever running it (shutdown drain) or when performDownload's own inner catch throws вҖ” emits a transient 'error' progress event and nothing else. The Finished-downloads list (sourced from download_history) will therefore never show these attempts, and the Retry button can't act on them. Minor because these are edge/shutdown paths, but it is an inconsistency in the otherwise-complete history ledger.

**Evidence**

~~~text
this.downloadQueue.enqueue(() => this.performDownload(...)).catch((err) => { this.notifier.notify('download-progress', { ... status: 'error', ... retriable: classifyDownloadError(err) === 'retriable' }) ; console.error(...) })  вҖ” no this.appendHistory(...) call in this catch.
~~~

**Fix**

Append an error history row in the outer .catch too (videoId/title null, creatorFolderName = slugify(trimmedCreator), errorRetryable from the same classifier), mirroring performDownload's catch.

**Verifier вҖ” confirmed**

The cited lines (115-132) match the quote exactly: the outer queue `.catch` emits a transient `download-progress` error event and a `console.error`, with no `appendHistory(...)` call. Every terminal outcome inside `performDownload` (success line 291, duplicate line 197, cancelled line 307, error line 343) does append a history row, so the outer catch is genuinely the one terminal path that writes no history row. Since the Finished-downloads list and Retry are sourced from download_history, an attempt that ends here is invisible to both. That core inconsistency is real.

However, the reviewer's reachability reasoning is partly incorrect. I checked PQueueDownloadQueue (`enqueue` => `pQueue.add(task)`) and the shutdown path in composition-root.ts:605 (`downloadQueue.clear()` => `pQueue.clear()`). p-queue's `clear()` simply empties the internal queue; it does NOT reject the already-returned promises of dropped tasks вҖ” they hang unsettled. So the headline "queue rejects a task without ever running it (shutdown drain)" does NOT actually fire this `.catch`. And even if it did, the process is exiting, so no UI/history would be observed anyway. The only path that genuinely reaches this `.catch` is the second one the reviewer names: `performDownload`'s own inner catch throwing вҖ” concretely, the `notifier.notify('download-progress', ...)` at line 323 (or `classifyDownloadError`) throwing before reaching `appendHistory` at line 343. `appendHistory` itself swallows its own DB errors, so it can't be the thrower. That path is real but extremely narrow (the in-process notifier failing to deliver an event).

**Verifier notes**

Confirmed-but-narrowed. The factual code claim (outer catch writes no history row; it is the sole terminal path that doesn't) is correct. The primary cited trigger is not actually reachable: p-queue `clear()` on shutdown does not reject pending task promises, so the "shutdown drain" never invokes this catch, and shutdown exits the process regardless. The only live trigger is the inner-catch notifier throwing вҖ” an in-process EventEmitter/IPC failure вҖ” which is exceedingly rare. The suggested fix (mirror performDownload's catch: appendHistory with videoId/title null, creatorFolderName = slugify(trimmedCreator), errorRetryable from classifyDownloadError) is correct and low-cost if applied, and is consistent with the code's own comment at lines 105-113 describing this catch as the residual-path guarantee. Severity dropped from low to info given the genuine trigger is so marginal and the comment already documents the catch's intent.

---


# Refuted вҖ” false positives, verified clean (8)

These were raised by a reviewer but the adversarial verifier independently read the code and rejected them. Listed so they are not re-investigated.

### EnrichMediaMetadata skips db-updated notification when all probes fail, leaving stale probing UI

- **Location:** `src/main/use-cases/EnrichMediaMetadata.ts:78-83` В· **Category:** bug В· **Claimed severity:** low

**Reviewer claimed**

The notify only fires when at least one probe SUCCEEDED. When every probe fails, probeStatus rows are flipped from 'pending' to 'failed' (updateProbeStatus at 47/71) but no 'db-updated' is emitted, so the renderer never re-queries and keeps showing the pending/probing state until some other event triggers a refetch. The status change is real and user-visible but the UI is not told about it.

**Why refuted**

The code at EnrichMediaMetadata.ts:78-83 does match the quoted evidence: `db-updated` only fires when `videosProbed > 0 || cutsProbed > 0`, so an all-failures run (failures > 0, probed = 0) flips probeStatus rows 'pending'вҶ’'failed' via updateProbeStatus (lines 47/71) without emitting a notification. That part of the observation is factually correct. But the claimed USER-VISIBLE harm вҖ” "the renderer keeps showing the pending/probing state until some other event triggers a refetch" вҖ” does not hold for this codebase:\n\n1. The renderer never consumes `probeStatus`. It is present in VideoDto (src/shared/dtos/VideoDto.ts:24) and CutDto, but a grep for `probeStatus` across src/renderer returns ZERO matches. No component renders a spinner, badge, or 'probing'/'pending' indicator keyed on probeStatus. There is no probing UI to go stale.\n\n2. On the failure path, only probeStatus changes вҖ” `updateProbeStatus(id,'failed')` writes nothing else. duration/resolution/fileSize remain null. So even if db-updated WERE emitted and the videos/cuts query trees re-fetched, the rendered card would be byte-identical (still null duration/resolution). There is no stale displayed value for the notification to correct.\n\n3. The only probe-pending logic in the renderer is EditorApp.tsx:153-155, which treats `duration <= 0` as probe-pending at edit-open time (and is gated by the main-window Edit button). A probe failure leaves duration null/0 regardless of whether db-updated fires; the editor is not passively subscribed to a live 'probing' indicator that this notification would clear.\n\nThus the missing notification has no observable effect: every renderer query that db-updated would invalidate (videos/cuts/tags/search/collections/stats per use-db-listener.ts) would re-render identical data on the all-fail path. The finding's repro premise (a visible probing state that never clears) is not present in the code.

**Notes:** If a future renderer feature surfaces probeStatus (e.g. a 'metadata unavailable' / failed badge), this gap would become real вҖ” so emitting db-updated when failures > 0 is a reasonable forward-compat hardening, but today it fixes nothing user-visible. Note also: the metadata fields written on SUCCESS are themselves filtered out of the audit log as pure enrichment (AuditedVideoRepository.ts:118-121), reinforcing that probe state is treated as a non-user-meaningful implementation detail. Verified probeStatus has no renderer consumer via grep over src/renderer (0 hits) and via VideoDto. Caller sites: src/main/index.ts:203 (startup) and ProcessFileNotifications.ts:143-144 вҖ” both fire-and-forget, neither emits its own follow-up db-updated on the all-fail outcome, so there is genuinely no compensating event, but also nothing that needs compensating.

---

### diffObjects only iterates newObj keys, so removed/cleared fields are not recorded in the audit diff

- **Location:** `src/main/interface-adapters/repositories/diff-objects.ts:10-17` В· **Category:** weird-logic В· **Claimed severity:** low

**Reviewer claimed**

The diff iterates only Object.keys(newObj). Any key present in oldObj but absent from newObj (e.g. an optional field that becomes undefined and is dropped from the object literal, rather than set to null) is never compared, so its removal is silently omitted from the audit 'changes'. For the current entities the upsert mappers always emit every column (often as null), so in practice both objects share the same key set and the gap is latent; but it makes the audit trail incomplete the moment any mutator constructs a sparser object. Low impact today, real correctness gap for the audit feature's stated purpose ('what changed').

**Why refuted**

The factual mechanic is accurate: diffObjects (src/main/interface-adapters/repositories/diff-objects.ts:11) iterates only Object.keys(newObj), so a key present in oldObj but absent from newObj is never compared and its removal is omitted. But this is an intentional, documented design rather than a latent bug. (1) The only callers are the four Audited*Repository decorators, which call diffObjects with two objects of the SAME concrete domain entity type (e.g. upsertWithPrevious passes previous: Creator and creator: Creator). (2) Every domain entity interface (Creator, Video, Cut, Collection) declares its optional fields as `T | null` with ZERO optional `?` properties вҖ” confirmed by grep finding no `?:` props across all entity files. TypeScript therefore guarantees both objects always carry the identical, fully-populated key set; a 'sparser object' cannot be constructed without first changing an entity interface. (3) The behavior is explicitly documented and pinned by tests/main/interface-adapters/repositories/diff-objects.test.ts:25-31 ('does not detect a field removed... Documented behavior... domain entities have stable shapes, every field is always present, just nullable'). The reviewer's own claim concedes 'Low impact today' and that the gap only appears 'the moment any mutator constructs a sparser object' вҖ” no such mutator exists and the all-nullable convention plus the type system prevent one arising accidentally. This is intended-and-documented behavior, the FALSE-POSITIVE pattern.

**Notes:** Not a defect in the current codebase. The union-of-keys fix the reviewer suggests is a reasonable defensive hardening, but it changes nothing for any present caller (key sets are always equal by entity construction). If pursued, it should be paired with making the limitation harder to violate вҖ” e.g. a lint/type guard вҖ” but the existing test (diff-objects.test.ts:20-31) already encodes both the add and remove semantics deliberately, so any change must update that test. Treat as a documentation/robustness note, not a correctness gap.

---

### resolveMediaFilePath 'any media file' fallback can pick a leftover sidecar/partial audio as the video file

- **Location:** `src/main/framework-drivers/yt-dlp/YtDlpDownloader.ts:692-699` В· **Category:** weird-logic В· **Claimed severity:** low

**Reviewer claimed**

When the `<videoId>.<ext>` prefix match fails (e.g. yt-dlp wrote a temp `.f###.m4a` audio-only stream that wasn't cleaned, or an interrupted-then-resumed run left a partial non-.part fragment), the `anyHit` branch returns whatever media-extension file readdir surfaces first. That file is then stored as the Video.filePath and fed to ffprobe / the player. The download dir is per-video so cross-video contamination is unlikely, but an orphaned audio fragment from a format-merge can still be mis-selected, yielding an audio-only or partial 'video'. The candidates-from-info path (requested_downloads[0].filepath) normally saves this, so the window is narrow.

**Why refuted**

I read YtDlpDownloader.ts:670-700 (resolveMediaFilePath) and the call chain. The cited code matches the quote. The output directory is per-video and isolated: DownloadVideo.ts:217-223 builds outputDir = <root>/<folderName>/downloads/<videoId>/, so cross-video contamination is impossible (reviewer concedes this). The core claim вҖ” that the anyHit fallback can pick up an orphaned audio fragment from a format-merge вҖ” is refuted by the -o template. YtDlpDownloader.ts:464-465 sets -o `${outputDir}/${videoId}.%(ext)s`, so EVERY file yt-dlp writes, including interim DASH streams, is named `${videoId}.f###.mp4` / `${videoId}.f###.m4a`. Those all satisfy startsWith(`${videoId}.`) and are therefore caught by the prefixHit branch (line 696), NOT the anyHit branch (line 698) the finding targets. The anyHit branch only fires for a media file that does NOT carry the videoId prefix, and this configuration produces no such file in a per-video directory. The reviewer's specific repro (orphaned .f###.m4a) actually carries the prefix, so it cannot reach anyHit. The suggested fix (drop m4a/mp3/opus from the fallback set) doesn't even address the only residual issue and would break legitimate audio-only output. Additionally, candidates from info (requested_downloads[0].filepath, _filename, filename) are resolved and existence-checked first (lines 676-687), pointing at the canonical merged output, so the directory scan is a last resort in practice.

**Notes:** The only genuine (and very narrow) residual risk is in the prefixHit branch, not anyHit: if a leftover interim `${videoId}.f140.m4a` survives the merge AND readdirSync surfaces it before `${videoId}.mp4`, files.find() could return audio-only. But yt-dlp deletes interim format files after a successful merge by default, and the info-based candidates (requested_downloads[0].filepath) normally resolve before the scan ever runs, so this is doubly guarded. If any hardening is wanted, it belongs in prefixHit (prefer container/largest file or skip the `.f\d+.` interim pattern), not in constraining anyHit's extension set as the finding suggests. As written, the finding mis-identifies the branch and the repro is not achievable under this -o template.

---

### Relevant-file regex omits audio + .mov/.gif extensions the protocol/editor actually serve

- **Location:** `src/main/framework-drivers/file-system/chokidar-path-filter.ts:24-25` В· **Category:** bug В· **Claimed severity:** low

**Reviewer claimed**

A file event for, e.g., an audio-only cut (`.m4a`/`.opus`) or a `.mov`/`.gif` asset landing under {creator}/cuts/{id}/ would not match RELEVANT_FILE_COMBINED_RE. It can still slip through via the looser RELEVANT_PATH_RE fallback (which only requires being inside a downloads|cuts dir), so for `add` events under those dirs the file is still forwarded вҖ” meaning the impact is limited. But the explicit extension allow-list is now out of sync with what the app considers media, so the filter's intent (only forward media/metadata) is partially defeated and the omission looks accidental rather than deliberate.

**Why refuted**

I read chokidar-path-filter.ts, the protocol's EXT_TO_MIME, the watcher consumer, the downloader's media-resolution regex, and the unit tests. The finding's premise is correct on one narrow point (RELEVANT_FILE_COMBINED_RE at line 25 lists only mp4|mkv|webm|jpg|jpeg|png|webp plus the json names, while EXT_TO_MIME in KlipMediaProtocolHandler.ts:32-48 serves m4a/aac/mp3/opus/ogg/wav/mov/m4v/gif). But the claimed impact does not exist, and even the "intent partially defeated" framing is wrong.

isRelevantPath (line 43) for file events returns `RELEVANT_FILE_COMBINED_RE.test(relative) || RELEVANT_PATH_RE.test(relative)`. Crucially, every path that RELEVANT_FILE_COMBINED_RE can match (`{seg}/(downloads|cuts)/...`) is a strict SUBSET of what RELEVANT_PATH_RE matches (`{seg}/(downloads|cuts)/`). So the extension allow-list contributes NOTHING to the OR for file events: any file under downloads/<id>/ or cuts/<id>/ passes via the fallback regardless of extension. An .m4a/.opus/.mov/.gif file under those dirs is therefore forwarded вҖ” there is no dropped event.

This is not accidental: the test at chokidar-path-filter.test.ts:44-53 explicitly documents the behavior ("accepts ANY file under downloads/<videoId>/ ... filter is structure-keyed, not extension-keyed"), shows notes.txt and file.mp4.part passing, and states the downstream ProcessFileNotifications use case is what actually filters by file shape. The reviewer themselves concedes the fallback forwards the file. So the extension list in the combined regex is effectively dead/redundant for the gate's purpose; the real shape-filtering happens downstream, not here. Extending it to match EXT_TO_MIME would change zero runtime behavior.

The downloader (YtDlpDownloader.ts:692-693) independently maintains its own broad media-extension regex including mov/opus/m4a/m4v/aac/wav and comments that the OLD narrow regex caused dropped files вҖ” that fix lives in resolveMediaFilePath, not in the watcher filter, and is unrelated to this allow-list.

**Notes:** No behavioral bug. For file events, RELEVANT_FILE_COMBINED_RE's extension alternation is dominated by the RELEVANT_PATH_RE fallback (both require the same `{seg}/(downloads|cuts)/` prefix), so audio/.mov/.gif assets under those dirs are still forwarded. The shape filter that matters runs downstream in ProcessFileNotifications, per the documented test at chokidar-path-filter.test.ts:44-53. At most this is a cosmetic/maintainability nit: the extension list is redundant and slightly stale, so syncing it to EXT_TO_MIME (or dropping it) is a tidy-up, not a fix. If the OR is ever tightened to AND (the test even flags this), then the staleness would bite вҖ” but that is a hypothetical future change, not the current code.

---

### Editor preview <video> is conditionally mounted with no key; source switch can reuse the old decoder

- **Location:** `src/renderer/components/features/editor/EditorView.tsx:74-82, 192-205` В· **Category:** bug В· **Claimed severity:** low

**Reviewer claimed**

The preview <video> has no key, so if sourceVideoId changes while timeline stays truthy, React reuses the existing element with the old buffered media until src updates, and positioning relies solely on the 0.05s threshold effect rather than re-seeding on loadedmetadata. Today useHashChangeReload forces a full reload on source switch, so this is largely masked, but the conditional-mount + threshold-seek combination is brittle and would break if in-window source switching is ever added (the documented v2 direction).

**Why refuted**

The cited lines are accurate: EditorView.tsx:74-82 is the threshold-seek effect (deps [timeline]) and :192-205 conditionally mounts the preview <video> with src={mediaUrl('video', sourceVideoId, 'file')} and no key. However, the claimed bug ("sourceVideoId changes while timeline stays truthy, React reuses the old element with stale buffered media") cannot occur in the current codebase. sourceVideoId originates in main.tsx via parseEditorHash(window.location.hash), is parsed ONCE at module-boot time, and is passed as an immutable prop down EditorApp -> EditorBootstrap -> EditorView. It is never reassigned during the component's lifetime. The only way to point the editor at a different source is a hashchange, and EditorApp's useHashChangeReload listener turns every hashchange into window.location.reload() вҖ” a hard reload that re-runs main.tsx, recreates the entire React root, and therefore mounts a brand-new <video> element with the correct src. There is no in-window source-switch path that keeps the component mounted while sourceVideoId changes, so the absence of a key is inert. The reviewer themselves concedes this ("Today useHashChangeReload forces a full reload on source switch, so this is largely masked") and rates confidence 0.4. The finding is a forward-compat/defensive-coding suggestion contingent on a v2 feature ("in-window source switching") that does not exist yet вҖ” not a defect in shipping code. It is also already tracked as a known low-priority item (plans/editor-review-low-priority.md LP-7/LP-... around line 124 discusses the reload-only-if-sourceVideoId-changed optimization, which is the inverse change that would actually be needed before this concern matters).

**Notes:** Not a present bug. Repro is impossible today: sourceVideoId is set once from the URL hash in main.tsx (line 49/63) and is a fixed prop; any source switch fires hashchange -> useHashChangeReload (EditorApp.tsx:75-83) -> window.location.reload(), which fully tears down and recreates the <video>. The key={sourceVideoId} + seed-on-loadedmetadata suggestion only becomes load-bearing IF a future change (a) stops reloading on source switch and (b) mutates sourceVideoId in place. If the team ever implements in-window source switching (plans/editor-review-low-priority.md ~line 124 proposes reloading only when the id changes), they should add the key at that time. As-is, treat as a forward-compat note, not a bug. The threshold-seek effect at :74-82 is also fine in isolation вҖ” it only mirrors store cursor into a same-source element.

---

### useFetchVideoComments seeds a cache that is never invalidated when the video is deleted

- **Location:** `src/renderer/hooks/use-videos.ts:118-132` В· **Category:** weird-logic В· **Claimed severity:** info

**Reviewer claimed**

The commentsCache query is intentionally immortal (staleTime/gcTime Infinity, only re-seeded by a successful fetch). The db-listener never invalidates queryKeys.videos.comments-cache. This is mostly fine, but combined with the lack of any video-detail invalidation on delete, a soft-deleted video that the user re-opens will still show its previously-loaded comments from the in-memory cache. Harmless (comments are read-only and the disk cache has a 7-day TTL) вҖ” noted only for completeness alongside finding #2.

**Why refuted**

The finding's core technical premise is wrong about TanStack Query's matching semantics. The reviewer claims commentsCache (queryKey ['videos','comments-cache',id]) is "never invalidated" and that videos-scope/all invalidation doesn't reach it. But invalidateQueries matches by PREFIX by default (no exact:true anywhere). queryKeys.videos.all = ['videos'] (query-keys.ts:10), which is a prefix of ['videos','comments-cache',id] (query-keys.ts:16). Therefore: (1) the db-listener DOES invalidate commentsCache вҖ” use-db-listener.ts:35 calls invalidateQueries({queryKey: ['videos']}) on any 'videos'/'all' scope push, which prefix-matches commentsCache; (2) useDeleteVideo (use-videos.ts:42) ALSO directly calls invalidateQueries({queryKey: ['videos']}) on success, again prefix-matching commentsCache; same for videos.detail/transcript/transcriptSegments. So both the "db-listener never invalidates comments-cache" and "lack of any video-detail invalidation on delete" claims are false. The staleTime:Infinity / gcTime:Infinity flags do NOT make the cache immortal against invalidation: invalidateQueries marks queries stale (overriding staleTime) and refetches active matches regardless of staleTime; gcTime only governs GC of inactive queries, not invalidation. So on delete, an open detail view's commentsCache refetches immediately, and an inactive one is marked stale so a re-open/remount re-reads getCachedVideoComments from disk rather than serving the stale in-memory copy. The described repro ("re-opened soft-deleted video still shows previously-loaded comments from the in-memory cache") does not occur via the mechanism claimed.

**Notes:** Refuted on TanStack Query semantics. Invalidation is by prefix unless exact:true is set; none of these call sites set it. ['videos'] prefix covers ['videos','comments-cache',id]. Handled in two places: use-db-listener.ts:34-35 (videos/all scope push) and use-videos.ts:42 (useDeleteVideo onSuccess). The only residual is purely disk-level: the on-disk comments cache file for a soft-deleted video persists until its 7-day TTL, but that is unrelated to the in-memory query cache being "immortal" вҖ” and the finding itself already flags that as harmless (comments read-only). Severity stays info but verdict is refuted because the asserted mechanism is incorrect. Note: I left severity at the original 'info' rather than 'unchanged' since the value is unchanged from the claim.

---

### ActiveDownloadsList renders by Object.values order вҖ” active downloads can reorder/jump on every progress tick

- **Location:** `src/renderer/components/features/downloads/ActiveDownloadsList.tsx:26,65-77` В· **Category:** bug В· **Claimed severity:** low

**Reviewer claimed**

The list iterates Object.values() of the activeDownloads record. While insertion order is usually preserved, any store update that rebuilds the record by spreading or that deletes+re-adds a key (e.g. the retry path here calls removeDownload then starts a new download which inserts a fresh key) changes iteration order, causing rows to visually reorder mid-download. Keys are stable (downloadId) so React won't remount, but the on-screen ordering is non-deterministic and not sorted by start time.

**Why refuted**

The cited lines are accurate (ActiveDownloadsList.tsx:22,26,67-69 iterate Object.values(activeDownloads) keyed by downloadId). But the finding's core mechanism is wrong. I read the store (src/renderer/hooks/use-app-store.ts:45-56): upsertDownload does `{ ...state.activeDownloads, [progress.downloadId]: progress }`. In JS, spreading an object and reassigning a key that ALREADY EXISTS preserves that key's original insertion-order slot вҖ” it does not move it to the end. Therefore the routine progress-tick path (the overwhelmingly common update, fired many times per second per download) does NOT reorder rows. The title's claim of "reorder/jump on every progress tick" is false; insertion order is stable across progress updates, and React keys are stable, so nothing remounts or visibly jumps during normal downloading. The ONLY case that changes iteration order is a true delete-then-add of a key, which happens exactly once on the retry path (handleRetry calls removeDownload(oldId), then downloadVideo.mutate inserts a fresh downloadId). That retried download is a genuinely new identity and naturally appends to the bottom of the active list вҖ” sensible, expected behavior, not a non-deterministic glitch. There is also no startedAt/createdAt/queue-position field on DownloadProgress (src/shared/types/download.ts:33-49), so insertion order is in fact the only meaningful ordering signal available, and it is already deterministic for the lifetime of a given download. The suggested fix (sort by startedAt) can't even be implemented without adding a new field, for a problem that doesn't manifest in practice.

**Notes:** Repro reality check: a concurrent download whose percent updates every tick stays in place вҖ” spread over an existing key keeps the slot. The only order change is a retried download moving to the bottom (it gets a brand-new downloadId), which is intuitive. If the author ever wanted retried rows to keep their original position, they'd need to add an explicit order/startedAt field and sort by it; absent that requirement this is cosmetic at most. Mislabeled trigger ("every progress tick") is the key reason this is refuted rather than a real low-severity bug.

---

### BulkImportDialog falls back to a raw creator UUID as the creator name when an override row can't be resolved

- **Location:** `src/renderer/components/features/downloads/BulkImportDialog.tsx:133-139` В· **Category:** bug В· **Claimed severity:** low

**Reviewer claimed**

When a row has an explicit creatorOverride (a creator id) but creators?.data doesn't contain it вҖ” e.g. the creators query is still loading, or the creator list exceeds the pageSize:500 cap and the chosen creator is beyond it вҖ” the code falls back to using row.creatorOverride (a UUID) as the literal creatorName passed to downloadVideo. That would create/route into a creator folder named after a UUID instead of the intended creator. The Select only exposes the first 500 creators, so this is reachable on large libraries.

**Why refuted**

The Select that produces `row.creatorOverride` is populated exclusively from the same `creators?.data` array (BulkImportDialog.tsx:230-235) that the `find` at line 137 searches, plus the AUTO_CREATOR sentinel. `onValueChange` (line 223) can only fire with a value that was actually rendered as a <SelectItem>. Therefore any non-AUTO override id the user can pick is, by construction, present in `creators.data` at the moment of selection. Both reviewer scenarios are ruled out by this coupling: (1) Loading вҖ” while `creators` is undefined only the AUTO item renders, so no creator id is selectable and `creatorOverride` stays AUTO; the non-AUTO branch is never taken. (2) pageSize:500 cap вҖ” creators beyond #500 are never rendered as options, so they cannot be selected; the `find` scans exactly the same (capped) set that the Select offers. The 500 cap limits which creators are *offerable* but can never make a *selected* one unfindable. I confirmed the downstream impact is real IF a UUID ever reached it: DownloadVideo.execute вҶ’ slugify(creatorName) becomes the folderName/creator id (DownloadVideo.ts:211-214, 396-402). But the only way the `?? row.creatorOverride` fallback fires is if `creators.data` mutates to drop a previously-selected id between selection and submit (e.g. a mid-dialog refetch that errors and clears the cache). The dialog is short-lived/modal, the creators list isn't invalidated during it, and React Query retains last-successful `data` unless it errors вҖ” so this is an extremely narrow race, not the mechanism the reviewer claims. The described repro paths are not reachable.

**Notes:** The Select options and the find() both read `creators?.data` (lines 231 and 137), so a selectable id is always findable вҖ” the reviewer's loading/500-cap repros don't hold. Residual: a theoretical race where the creators query errors and clears its cache while the dialog is open could leave a stale `creatorOverride` unmatched, making the `?? row.creatorOverride` UUID fallback fire. Worth a cheap hardening (skip/error the row instead of falling back to the raw id, or resolve the name in the main process from the id) but it is defensive, not a live bug. Tests at tests/renderer/.../BulkImportDialog.test.tsx only exercise the AUTO path (creatorName 'Alice' from channel), never the override-miss path.

---


# Uncertain вҖ” needs a human decision (2)

### Background avatar fetch upserts a stale full-row snapshot, clobbering concurrent creator edits

- **Location:** `src/main/use-cases/DownloadVideo.ts:459-481` В· **Category:** bug В· **Severity:** medium В· **Confidence:** 0.74

**Impact**

scheduleAvatarFetch closes over the Creator object as it existed at download start and, seconds-to-minutes later, calls creatorRepo.upsert with a full-row spread of that snapshot. SqliteCreatorRepository.upsert does onConflictDoUpdate on creators.id and overwrites EVERY column from the incoming row (folderName, name, notes, tags, subscriberCount, profileImagePath, status, ...). If the user edits the creator (renames it, adds notes/tags, sets a profile image) during the download window, those edits are silently reverted when the async avatar fetch resolves вҖ” last-writer-wins data loss of user input. The comment at 451-457 justifies using the snapshot to avoid a read race, but a snapshot-based full-row upsert is exactly what makes the lost-update possible.

**Evidence**

~~~text
void this.fetchChannelAvatar(...).then((avatarUrl) => { ... this.creatorRepo.upsert({ ...creator, avatarUrl, updatedAt: new Date().toISOString() }) ... })  where `creator` is the snapshot captured before the download started.
~~~

**Fix**

Re-read the creator by id just before persisting and only patch avatarUrl (and updatedAt) on the fresh row, or add a column-scoped update method (e.g. setAvatarUrl(id, url)) so the avatar patch never overwrites unrelated fields.

**Verifier вҖ” uncertain**

The mechanism the reviewer describes is real and verified: scheduleAvatarFetch (DownloadVideo.ts:459) closes over the `touched` snapshot captured in ensureCreator BEFORE the actual download runs (ensureCreator at line 214, downloader.download at line 247), so the snapshot is stale for the full download duration plus the ~3-5s background avatar yt-dlp call. The .then at line 475 does `this.creatorRepo.upsert({ ...creator, avatarUrl, updatedAt })`. SqliteCreatorRepository.upsert (lines 113-129) does onConflictDoUpdate on creators.id and sets EVERY column from `excluded` (folderName, name, profileImagePath, youtubeChannelId/Url, subscriberCount, avatarUrl, notes, tags, status, deletedAt, updatedAt). So a full-row spread of a stale snapshot genuinely overwrites all columns = last-writer-wins. Notably, RefreshCreatorAvatar.ts:25 implements the same avatar-patch but RE-READS the row by id immediately before upserting, exactly the fix the reviewer suggests, which corroborates that DownloadVideo's snapshot approach is the riskier one.

HOWEVER, the reviewer's stated IMPACT is largely not reachable in this codebase. I traced every creator write path: CreatorController exposes only get-creators-paginated, get-creator-by-id, delete-creator, restore-creator, register-creator, refresh-creator-avatar. There is NO edit-creator use case вҖ” nothing updates an existing creator's name, notes, tags, or profileImagePath. RegisterCreator (RegisterCreator.ts:84-92) is insert-only and throws CreatorAlreadyRegisteredError / FolderNameTakenError if the folderName or channelId already exists, so it can never patch an existing row. BulkUpdateTags (BulkUpdateTags.ts) only handles entityKind 'video'/'cuts', never creators. profileImagePath is only ever written as null (RegisterCreator.ts:70, DownloadVideo.ts:399); no path sets it to a real value. So 'renames it, adds notes/tags, sets a profile image during the download window' cannot actually happen вҖ” the user has no UI/IPC to do any of that. The only concurrent creator mutation that IS reachable is delete-creator/restore-creator, which call updateStatus (column-scoped, writes status+deletedAt). If a user soft-deletes a creator while a download for that creator is in flight, the snapshot (status 'active', deletedAt null) will resurrect it when the avatar fetch resolves вҖ” a genuine but much narrower lost-update than claimed.

**Notes:** Refuted as written, real in a narrower form. The full-row stale-snapshot upsert pattern is genuinely fragile and the suggested fix (re-read by id before patching, or add a column-scoped setAvatarUrl) is correct and already used by RefreshCreatorAvatar.ts:25. But the headline impact (clobbering name/notes/tags/profileImage edits) is unreachable: no edit-creator use case exists; RegisterCreator is insert-only (throws on existing folderName/channelId); BulkUpdateTags excludes creators; profileImagePath is never set to a non-null value anywhere. The only real repro today: start a download for creator X, then soft-delete X (delete-creator вҶ’ updateStatus status='deleted') before the background avatar fetch resolves; when it resolves, scheduleAvatarFetch upserts the stale snapshot with status='active'/deletedAt=null, silently un-deleting the creator. That's a low-severity status-revert edge case, not the medium-severity 'user input data loss' described. Severity dropped to low. Note: if an edit-creator feature is added later, this becomes medium вҖ” fixing it now (re-read or scoped update) is cheap and forward-proofs it.

---

### Backfill counts a permission/IO read error as 'missing', conflating real failures with absent transcripts

- **Location:** `src/main/use-cases/BackfillTranscriptIndex.ts:25-38` В· **Category:** bug В· **Severity:** low В· **Confidence:** 0.55

**Impact**

On a thrown read error (permission/device problem, explicitly called out in the comment as worth logging), `raw` stays null and the row is counted as `missing` and skipped, identical to a genuinely-absent file. There is no `failed` bump for the IO-error case (failed is only incremented on parse error). The result object therefore under-reports real failures and the video silently never gets re-indexed; since this is a boot-time one-shot backfill, a transient device error means that transcript is permanently unindexed unless transcript_text is cleared and the app restarted.

**Evidence**

~~~text
try {
        raw = this.fsReader.readTextFile(transcriptPath)
      } catch (err) {
        console.warn(`[klip] backfill: read failed for ${id}:`, redactError(err))
      }

      if (!raw) {
        result.missing++
        continue
      }
~~~

**Fix**

On a thrown read error, increment result.failed (not missing) so transient/permission failures are distinguishable and could be retried; reserve `missing` for the readTextFile-returned-null (file genuinely absent) case.

**Verifier вҖ” uncertain**

The cited code at src/main/use-cases/BackfillTranscriptIndex.ts:25-37 matches the quote exactly. Factually: a thrown read error is caught, logged via console.warn with redactError, leaves raw=null, and the row is then counted as result.missing and skipped вҖ” there is no result.failed bump for the IO-error path (failed only increments on parseVtt throw). So the aggregate counters do conflate a permission/device failure with a genuinely-absent file. That much is true.

However, the finding's severity rests on two claims that the surrounding code refutes. (1) "Permanently unindexed unless transcript_text is cleared and the app restarted" is wrong. findVideosNeedingBackfill (SqliteVideoTranscriptIndex.ts:93-101) selects WHERE transcript_text IS NULL AND status='active'. On a read error setTranscriptText is never called, so transcript_text stays NULL and the row remains a backfill candidate. The backfill is wired in src/main/index.ts:217 to run on every app boot and is explicitly documented as idempotent. A transient device error therefore auto-retries on the NEXT restart with no manual intervention вҖ” the opposite of "permanently unindexed". (2) The IO error is NOT silently swallowed: it emits a distinct console.warn line with the real (redacted) error. Only the coarse aggregate counter is imprecise.

Moreover the conflation is arguably by-contract: IBackfillTranscriptIndex.ts:6 documents `missing` as "Number of videos whose VTT file was missing OR unreadable" вҖ” i.e. unreadable-counts-as-missing is the stated semantics. The result object is consumed only by a console.log at index.ts:220-222 (no retry/metric/UI), so the imprecise counter has no functional consequence.

The kernel of the suggestion (split IO failure into `failed` for better observability) is a reasonable cosmetic improvement, but there is no real bug: nothing is permanently lost, the error is already logged distinctly, and the conflation is documented.

**Notes:** Refuting context: candidate selection is driven by `transcript_text IS NULL` (SqliteVideoTranscriptIndex.ts:93-101) and execute() runs on every boot (index.ts:217), so an IO-failed row is automatically re-attempted on next restart вҖ” not permanently unindexed. The IO error already produces a distinct console.warn (line 31). The `missing` field is documented as "missing OR unreadable" (IBackfillTranscriptIndex.ts:6), and the result is only console.log'd (index.ts:220), never used for retry/metrics/UI. The suggested fix (bump `failed` on the catch, reserve `missing` for readTextFile-returned-null) is a fine observability nicety but not a correctness fix.

---
